# Project Memory — Pyrycode

Repo-level session memory. Read this at the start of every session.

## What's Built

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #210)
- **`internal/devices/auth.go` — `(*Registry).Validate(plain string) (Device, bool)`.** New file (~25 prod LOC) co-located with `device.go` (#208) and `registry.go` (#209). One new exported method on the existing `Registry`; zero new exported types, zero new sentinels, zero new packages. Stdlib only (`time`). Production diff: +25 LOC `auth.go` (new). Test diff: +158 LOC `auth_test.go` (new). Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing code, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change. No consumers wired in this slice — the WS-handshake auth handler that calls `Validate` is a follow-up Phase-3 ticket.
- **The WS-perimeter auth predicate.** Single entry point composing the three #208/#209 primitives that previously had to be wired by hand at every prospective call site: `HashToken(plain)` → byte-exact scan against `Registry.devices[i].TokenHash` → in-memory `LastSeenAt = time.Now()` advance on hit. Handler call site is a one-line `d, ok := reg.Validate(plain)`; the empty-plain early-out, the constant-time-vs-byte-exact split, and the locked mutation are co-located so they cannot drift across handler implementations.
- **Method on `*Registry`, not a free function.** AC permitted either; method chosen because the `LastSeenAt` mutation is a registry-side operation and methods on `*Registry` already own `mu` and `devices`. Free-function `Validate(r *Registry, plain string)` would either re-export `mu` / `devices` (encapsulation leak) or call an unexported helper for no abstraction win. Mirrors the existing `Add` / `Remove` / `List` / `FindByTokenHash` shape; `Validate` is the fifth method.
- **Body is five points of structural discipline.** (1) Empty-plain early-out is FIRST — before `HashToken`, before the lock — enforcing the AC's "no registry lookup" structurally and (cheaply) defending the unreachable case of a `Device` persisted with `TokenHash == HashToken("")`. (2) `HashToken` runs OUTSIDE the lock — SHA-256 over a short string is microseconds but moving it outside keeps the critical section to scan + mutate + return-value materialization, which matters because the auth path is the high-frequency reader. (3) Indexed loop (`for i := range r.devices`) — value-loop `for _, d := range r.devices` would copy the element and the `LastSeenAt = ...` assignment would silently no-op. (4) Mutation and snapshot both INSIDE the lock — return value is `r.devices[i]` (value-type copy taken before the deferred unlock fires), so callers observe the just-written timestamp. (5) Byte-exact `==` on `TokenHash`, NOT `subtle.ConstantTimeCompare` — constant-time at the plain↔hash boundary is owned by `HashToken`; once the wire plain has been hashed, comparing two 64-char hex strings reveals only a public derivative. Inherits the chain from #208 + #209 verbatim; do not relitigate.
- **`Validate` does NOT call `Save`.** Disk persistence is the caller's job. Validate runs on the WS hot path and an fsync per auth is a perf footgun. The follow-up consumer ticket schedules `Save` (periodic ticker / graceful-shutdown hook); in-memory `LastSeenAt` is the source of truth for runtime decisions.
- **`Validate` has no `context.Context`, no `*slog.Logger`, no error path.** Body is microseconds at p99 and never blocks (`mu` is uncontended in steady state — pairing is rare, auth is solo per-connection). ctx-cancel plumbing for that window is ceremony without value. Auth-event logging belongs at the WS handler (it has `conn-id`, `remote-host`, attempt counter that the registry doesn't see). AC pins the signature as `(Device, bool)`; the constraint "no log/error/panic contains plain, hash, or device name" stands for any future error path but no error path is added today.
- **Why NOT iterate `VerifyToken` over all devices.** Two reasons. (1) Performance: `VerifyToken` recomputes `HashToken(plain)` internally per call — N devices means N SHA-256 computations vs. one for "hash plain once, byte-exact scan." (2) The constant-time concern is the plain↔hash boundary, which `HashToken` satisfies (deterministic, no early-exit on input). Once hashed, comparing 64-char hex strings is byte-exact; timing of `==` on a hash leaks only what the attacker could compute themselves from any candidate plain. See #208 § "Constant-time compare" and #209 § "Should `FindByTokenHash` use `subtle.ConstantTimeCompare`?" for the full chain. Sibling decisions stand.
- **Concurrency: one critical section under existing `Registry.mu`, no new lock, no ordering.** Two concurrent `Validate` calls on the same token serialize on `mu`; first writes `T1`, second observes `T2 ≥ T1` (Go's `time.Now()` is monotonic per process — same-value reads at clock-granularity edges still satisfy `>=`) and writes `T2`. Final stored `LastSeenAt` is `T2` — the AC's "monotonically-non-decreasing" invariant. Concurrent `Save` snapshots whatever value sits in memory at its lock-acquisition (any of `T1`, `T2`, or pre-update is correct — same durability semantics as #209). Concurrent `Remove` between two `Validate` calls makes the second return `(Device{}, false)` cleanly (no torn read; second scan runs after splice committed).
- **`time.Now()` directly, no clock injection.** Tests verify `after.After(before)` (wall-clock advancing under real concurrency) and `final.After(when)` (the field was actually written) — neither needs a fake clock. Inherits #209's convention (`PairedAt` is caller-filled; the registry doesn't take a clock). If a future test needs deterministic timestamps (e.g. snapshot golden-file diff), introduce a `Clock` interface then.
- **Tests in `auth_test.go`** — same-package, `t.Parallel()` everywhere, stdlib only. Five tests: `TestRegistry_Validate_Hit` (valid token returns matching device + asserts both the returned snapshot AND the in-memory mutation via `List()`; `PairedAt` unchanged), `TestRegistry_Validate_MissUnknown` (`(Device{}, false)` + no mutation observed via `List()`), `TestRegistry_Validate_MissEmpty` (empty plain → `(Device{}, false)` + no mutation; the "no registry lookup" half is enforced structurally by the early-out, the test asserts the observable consequence), `TestRegistry_Validate_EmptyRegistry` (defends against panic on a zero-init `*Registry`), `TestRegistry_Validate_ConcurrentSameToken` (16 goroutines, race-detector probe; sorts the per-goroutine observed `LastSeenAt` values and asserts each `>=` previous; `final.After(when)` proves a structurally-correct lock didn't accidentally skip the mutation due to a value-receiver bug — race detector catches a missing lock on the slice-element write).
- **Out of scope, by design.** WS-handshake auth handler that calls `Validate` (sibling Phase-3 ticket — owns logging with `conn-id`/`remote-host`, returns `auth.invalid_token` per `protocol-mobile.md:97-98` on miss). `Save` cadence policy for `LastSeenAt` durability (consumer's concern — periodic ticker / graceful-shutdown hook; this predicate intentionally does not fsync per auth). Rate-limiting / per-token attempt counters / per-IP lockout (handler ticket; the predicate is a leaf primitive). Structured auth-event metrics. Auto-revocation after N consecutive misses (defer). Per-device session-bind enforcement after Validate succeeds. `ValidateE(plain) (Device, error)` per-cause structured-error sibling (defer until a daemon-side audit-log consumer needs it). Deprecating `FindByTokenHash` in favor of `Validate` — they're different surfaces (read-only inspector vs. auth predicate); revisit only if `FindByTokenHash` ends Phase 3 with zero callers.
- See [knowledge/features/devices-registry.md](knowledge/features/devices-registry.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/210-pair-token-validation-predicate.md`](specs/architecture/210-pair-token-validation-predicate.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #216)
- **`internal/conversations/conversation.go` — `ConversationID` typedef + `Conversation` struct.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`time`); two new files (`conversation.go` ~73 LOC, `conversation_test.go` ~99 LOC). Two exports: `ConversationID` (string newtype, distinct from `sessions.SessionID` to make the swap a compile error at call sites that handle both), `Conversation` (pure value type — `ID ConversationID`, `Name *string`, `Cwd string`, `CurrentSessionID string`, `SessionHistory []string`, `IsPromoted bool`, `LastUsedAt time.Time`). Snake_case JSON tags mirror `internal/sessions/registry.go`'s style. `,omitempty` on `Name` / `CurrentSessionID` / `SessionHistory`; never on `ID` / `Cwd` / `IsPromoted` / `LastUsedAt` so the unpromoted-default ("discussion") is explicit on disk. No constructors, no I/O, no consumers wired in this slice — foundation for the `conv:` ticket series (#217 registry CRUD, #218 promotion API, #219 auto-archive predicate, #220 auto-archive sweep). Greenfield alongside `internal/sessions`; Phase 1/2 sessions untouched.
- **`ConversationID` is a typedef, not bare `string`.** A conversation carries both its own ID and an embedded `CurrentSessionID`; both being plain `string` would make them swappable at any call site. Distinct nominal types make the swap a compile error. Cost is one extra line and the occasional `ConversationID(s)` conversion at the package boundary — accepted. Mirrors the `SessionID` pattern from `internal/sessions/id.go`. Validity predicate (`ValidConversationID`) is **not** defined here — #217 owns the generator and validator, mirroring `sessions.ValidID` if conversation IDs are also UUIDv4.
- **`SessionHistory` is chronological (oldest-first).** Rotation appends in place: `append(SessionHistory, prevID)`. Chronological ordering matches the natural append pattern and avoids O(n) shifts on every rotation; presentation layers that want newest-first reverse on read (one O(n) traversal per render, vs. O(n) shifts on every rotation if newest-first is stored). The most recently retired session sits at the tail (`SessionHistory[len-1]`). Documented in the field comment so the choice survives the type definition.
- **`Name` is `*string`, not `string`.** Pointer distinguishes "absent" (nil — the user has never named this conversation) from "explicitly empty" (non-nil pointer to `""`). Unpromoted conversations typically leave this nil; promoted conversations (channels) usually carry a name. A future `pyry conv name <id> ""` UX would set a non-nil empty string; "rename to nothing" and "never named" are different states.
- **`CurrentSessionID` and `SessionHistory[i]` are typed as `string`, NOT `sessions.SessionID`.** Keeps `internal/conversations` decoupled from `internal/sessions` while Phase 3 lives alongside Phase 1/2. If a future refactor unifies the two packages, those fields can be retyped without touching the JSON wire format.
- **`omitempty` placement is load-bearing.** `Name`, `CurrentSessionID`, `SessionHistory` carry `,omitempty` so unpromoted/unnamed conversations and conversations with no session bound serialize without those keys. `IsPromoted`, `Cwd`, `ID`, `LastUsedAt` do **NOT** use `omitempty` — they must always appear, even at zero value. The `IsPromoted: false` default ("discussion") must be explicit on disk because the field is meaningful in both states; an absent `is_promoted` is ambiguous. `TestConversation_OmitemptyAbsentForUnpromoted` pins both halves: asserts `"name"` / `"current_session_id"` / `"session_history"` are absent from the marshaled bytes, AND spot-checks that `"id"` / `"cwd"` / `"is_promoted"` / `"last_used_at"` are present (the always-present half is otherwise easy to break by accidentally adding `,omitempty` later).
- **No concurrency primitives.** Pure value type — no goroutines, no channels, no mutexes. Safe to copy by value. Safe to pass across goroutines provided the usual "no concurrent mutation of `SessionHistory` slice header" Go rules are followed by the future owner (#217's registry).
- **Tests in `conversation_test.go`** — same-package, table-driven, stdlib `testing` only. Two tests: `TestConversation_JSONRoundTrip` (two cases — promoted + named + non-empty history with ≥2 entries to verify ordering, and unpromoted + unnamed + nil history; each marshals to JSON, unmarshals back, asserts `reflect.DeepEqual(in, out)`), `TestConversation_OmitemptyAbsentForUnpromoted` (marshals the unpromoted case, asserts the three `omitempty` keys are absent and the four always-present keys are present, via `bytes.Contains` against literal byte slices). Test inputs use `time.Date(...)` (no monotonic clock component) so `DeepEqual` on `time.Time` survives the round-trip, per `lessons.md` § "JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state". `SessionHistory == nil` round-trips to nil under `omitempty`; the unpromoted case sets the input to `nil` (not `[]string{}`) so `DeepEqual` holds.
- **Production diff: `internal/conversations/conversation.go` +73 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/conversations/conversation_test.go` +99 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Persistence (#217 — `~/.pyry/<name>/conversations.json` registry CRUD with the same atomic-rename + `0600` recipe `internal/sessions/registry.go` and `internal/devices/registry.go` use). Validity predicate `ValidConversationID` (#217 owns it, mirroring `sessions.ValidID` if UUIDv4). Promotion API `pyry conv promote` / `pyry conv name` (#218). Auto-archive predicate (#219) + sweep (#220). Migration from existing `Session` registry (TBD ticket once Conversations is proven on disk; Phase 1/2 sessions stay untouched). Schema versioning (defer until first migration).
- See [knowledge/features/conversations-package.md](knowledge/features/conversations-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/216-conversation-type.md`](specs/architecture/216-conversation-type.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #212)
- **`internal/pair/render.go` — `Render(p Payload, w io.Writer) error`.** New file (~58 LOC) that wraps the #211 `Encode` output in a QR symbol (UTF-8 half-blocks via `qrterminal.GenerateHalfBlock` at error-correction level `M`), a blank line, the encoded payload string, and a fixed instruction line, all written to a caller-supplied `io.Writer` in that exact order. One new exported function (`Render`); one unexported helper type (`errTrackingWriter`). Production diff: +58 LOC `render.go` (new). Test diff: +158 LOC `render_test.go` (new). One new module dependency: `github.com/mdp/qrterminal/v3 v3.2.1` (pure-Go, MIT, built on `rsc.io/qr v0.2.0` — also pure-Go, MIT, by Russ Cox / the Go team). Zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside `Render`, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change. No consumers wired in this slice — the eventual `pyry pair` CLI ticket will pass `os.Stdout`.
- **`GenerateHalfBlock` over `Generate`.** `qrterminal/v3` exposes both. `Generate` uses one terminal cell per QR module (`█` and space); the printed shape is roughly twice as tall as wide on typical 2:1 terminal cell aspect ratios, which trips up phone-camera QR detectors that expect a square symbol. `GenerateHalfBlock` packs two QR rows per terminal row using `▀`/`▄`/`█`/space; the printed shape comes out roughly square and scans more reliably. The AC explicitly named "the half-block variants emitted by `qrterminal/v3`," and `protocol-mobile.md`'s security model #3 names unscannable QR codes as a UX-degrading failure mode.
- **Error-correction level `M`** (medium, ~15% recovery) — library default for `Generate*`. Fits the ~120-140 base64-character payload at QR version 5–6, well within an 80-column terminal. `L` shrinks the symbol slightly but is fragile to terminal font glitches; `Q`/`H` enlarge the symbol and risk wrapping. Locked at the call site as a literal `qrterminal.M` — no package-level var, no config knob, no exposing the choice in the function signature. If the trade-off ever needs revisiting, change it here.
- **`errTrackingWriter` propagates writer errors through qrterminal's no-error-return API.** `qrterminal.GenerateHalfBlock` has signature `func(text string, l Level, w io.Writer)` — no error return, internally calls `w.Write` and discards errors. To honor AC #3 ("returns an error if the writer fails; does not panic on writer failure; does not partially-render-and-swallow"), `Render` passes a small unexported wrapper that captures the first non-nil write error and short-circuits all subsequent `Write` calls (returning `(0, t.err)` once errored). After the four ordered writes complete, `Render` returns `tw.err`. The pattern matches the stdlib idiom (cf. `bufio.Writer.flush` short-circuit on `b.err`); `TestRender_DoesNotPanicOnBrokenWriter` is the belt-and-suspenders proof that a writer panicking on the second call is never reached.
- **The returned error is the bare underlying writer error, NOT wrapped.** `errors.Is(err, io.ErrShortWrite)` matches in `TestRender_WriterError` because the bare error propagates. The AC says "returns an error if the writer fails," not "returns an error annotated with context." The stdlib idiom for "you handed me a writer; here's what your writer told me" is the bare error; `pyry pair`'s top-level error handler is the wrapping site, not `Render`.
- **Output is plain ASCII + the half-block code points qrterminal emits.** No ANSI color codes, no emoji, no terminal control sequences. Paste-fallback users in non-TTY contexts (logs piped to a file) need ANSI-free output; the AC's "instruction line" is a fixed-copy string the developer must not paraphrase: `"Scan the QR with the Pyrycode mobile app, or paste the string above into the app's pairing screen."`.
- **`Render` does NOT validate `p` or call `Decode` on the encoded string before writing.** Same posture as `Encode`: a zero `Payload` produces a string `Decode` and the phone reject — the failure surfaces on scan, not on render. Round-trip is `payload.go`'s invariant proven by `TestEncodeDecodeRoundTrip`; re-running it inside `Render` would couple this surface to that test for no protocol benefit. `Render` also caches `Encode(p)` in a local — `Encode` is deterministic, but one call is one call.
- **`Render` adds NO surrounding framing.** No banner, no server-id summary, no relay summary, no warning copy. AC #2 pins exactly four output sections in fixed order; the eventual `pyry pair` CLI ticket owns the surrounding presentation. The illustrative CLI lines in `protocol-mobile.md:705-714` (`==> Server-id: …`, `==> Scan QR or paste this:`, …) are the future ticket's concern, NOT this slice's contract.
- **`Render` adds NO terminal-width sizing.** `qrterminal/v3` produces a symbol whose width is fixed by the QR version (encoded length); narrower terminals wrap, that is the user's concern. Sizing detection is later-ticket scope at best.
- **Token-secrecy contract continues at the render layer.** Render's output **contains the plaintext device-token** (visible inside the QR symbol and verbatim on the paste-fallback line). The function doc-comment instructs callers explicitly: never log the writer's destination, never capture this output into any persisted context (CI logs, telemetry, error reports), treat the calling goroutine's stdout as the only intended sink. The future `pyry pair` ticket will pass `os.Stdout`; tests pass a `bytes.Buffer` that goes out of scope at function exit. `Render` itself does not log, persist, or otherwise duplicate the rendered bytes — pure write-to-supplied-writer; no `slog` calls, no error wrapping that would echo bytes, no telemetry. Aligns with `protocol-mobile.md:608` ("Paste-fallback is one-time-only") and `:603` ("QR screenshots auto-uploaded to cloud backup" is the user's risk; the render layer does not introduce a *third* exposure surface beyond the two already documented).
- **Test-failure logging discipline extends from `payload_test.go`.** No `t.Logf("rendered: %s", buf.String())`, no `t.Logf("encoded: %s", Encode(p))` anywhere in `render_test.go`. Test failures report category-only messages: "did not contain a QR block code point," "Encode(p) substring not found in rendered output," etc. The `testToken` constant is a fixed test-file value (not a real device token), but writing the discipline into tests exercises the muscle for when this code path runs against real tokens in the future `pyry pair` integration test.
- **Tests in `render_test.go`** — same-package, stdlib `testing` only, `t.Parallel()` everywhere. Five tests: `TestRender_Format_Happy` (non-empty buffer; contains at least one of `{█, ▀, ▄}`; contains `Encode(p)` as substring; contains the exact instruction string), `TestRender_FieldOrder` (split buffer at `Encode(p)` substring; QR block code point in prefix; instruction line in suffix; at least one blank line between QR and encoded payload), `TestRender_Deterministic` (Render twice into two buffers; assert `bytes.Equal` — phone re-scanning doesn't see a different symbol; pinned via JSON marshal determinism + `qrterminal/v3`'s stateless `Generate*`), `TestRender_WriterError` (writer returning `io.ErrShortWrite` on every `Write`; assert `errors.Is(err, io.ErrShortWrite)` — bare error propagated, not wrapped), `TestRender_DoesNotPanicOnBrokenWriter` (writer that panics if called more than once after the first error — pins the `errTrackingWriter` short-circuit). No fixtures, no `t.TempDir`, no PTY; runs under `go test -race ./...` in milliseconds.
- **Dependency justification.** `github.com/mdp/qrterminal/v3` (~200 LOC, MIT, single-call API `Generate*(text, level, w)`) + `rsc.io/qr` (~1500 LOC, MIT, by Russ Cox / the Go team — well-maintained QR encoder). Both pure-Go, no cgo, stdlib-only otherwise. CODING-STYLE.md "Stdlib over dependencies" allows external deps when they "provide significant value (like `creack/pty`)" — a QR encoder is not in the stdlib and writing one is a multi-hundred-LOC undertaking that duplicates a battle-tested, widely-used library. `go.sum` checksum verification (Go default) is the supply-chain defense.
- **Out of scope, by design.** `pyry pair` CLI itself (later phase-3 ticket — mints token, builds `Payload`, calls `Render(p, os.Stdout)`, prints surrounding banner with server-id summary + warning copy). Token generation / hashing / persistence (#208 hashes; minter is later). Anything mobile-side: QR alphabet selection, error-correction trade-offs, app-side decoding. Terminal-width sizing detection. Configurable error-correction level. Color codes / ANSI sequences. Logging or persistence of rendered bytes anywhere.
- See [knowledge/features/pair-package.md](knowledge/features/pair-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/212-pair-qr-render.md`](specs/architecture/212-pair-qr-render.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #209)
- **`internal/devices/registry.go` — `Registry` (mutex-guarded device list) + atomic-write `Save` + `Load` + `Add` / `Remove` / `List` / `FindByTokenHash`.** New file (~154 LOC) co-located with `device.go` (#208). Six exports on the new `Registry` type. Stdlib only (`encoding/json`, `os`, `path/filepath`, `sort`, `sync`). Production diff: +154 LOC `registry.go` (new). Test diff: +354 LOC `registry_test.go` (new). Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing code, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **Atomic-write recipe is structurally identical to `internal/sessions/registry.go:saveRegistryLocked`.** `MkdirAll(dir, 0o700)` → `CreateTemp(dir, ".devices-*.json.tmp")` → `defer os.Remove(tmp)` → `Chmod(0o600)` → `json.NewEncoder(f).Encode(...)` → `f.Sync()` → `f.Close()` → `os.Rename(tmp, path)`. SIGKILL anywhere before rename leaves the pre-existing target byte-identical; SIGKILL after leaves the new version. Partial JSON in the target is unreachable. The `0o600` chmod is unconditional even though `os.CreateTemp` defaults to that mode — same belt-and-suspenders pattern as `saveRegistryLocked`. No parent-directory fsync (per `lessons.md` § "Atomic on-disk writes").
- **`Save` snapshots the slice under `mu`, releases, then performs sort + I/O outside the lock.** Diverges from `internal/sessions`'s hold-across-I/O specifically because the auth path is the high-frequency reader (`FindByTokenHash(HashToken(presented))` per WS handshake) and pairing is the rare writer. Holding the mutex across the syscall window (`MkdirAll` + `CreateTemp` + `Chmod` + encode + `Sync` + `Close` + `Rename`) would block every concurrent `List` / `FindByTokenHash`. `Device`'s all-value-type fields make a shallow snapshot fully decoupling — no field aliases the registry's storage, so the snapshot is strictly safe. Two concurrent `Save` calls produce two complete temp files and two renames; the later rename wins (`os.Rename` is atomic per call). See [ADR 020](knowledge/decisions/020-devices-registry-snapshot-then-write.md). If a future `Device` field becomes a reference type (slice/map/pointer), the snapshot logic must deep-copy that field; today's value-type invariant is what makes the pattern correct.
- **Sort by `PairedAt` ascending, tiebreak `Name` byte-exact, on every Save.** `time.Time.Equal` (not `==`) for the primary comparator — JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state and `==` would treat otherwise-equal timestamps as unequal (per `lessons.md` § "JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state"). Sort runs on the Save-side snapshot, not on the live in-memory slice — `Add` insertion order in memory is preserved (a future "most recently added first" UI is unaffected) while disk output stays byte-deterministic (`TestRegistry_SaveStableOrdering` pins this — same logical content + different `Add` permutations produce byte-identical files).
- **Envelope shape is `{"devices": [...]}`, not a bare top-level array.** Reserves room for future top-level fields (schema version, push-token registration metadata per `protocol-mobile.md:495`) without a wire break, jq-pipeline break, or stdlib-decoder discipline change. Same future-proofing rationale as `sessions.json`'s `{"sessions": [...]}` envelope (per `lessons.md` § "Don't pick a real verb name as the still-unknown placeholder…"). No `version` field today (out of scope per AC; defer until first migration).
- **Load semantics: missing → empty + nil; zero-byte → empty + nil; malformed → wrapped `registry: parse` error + nil registry.** Empty-as-cold-start asymmetry vs. `internal/config.Load` (which surfaces zero-byte as a parse error) is deliberate: `devices.json` is pyry-owned and zero bytes is a benign cold-start state; `config.json` is operator-owned and zero bytes is operator error.
- **`Add` does not validate uniqueness.** AC pins the signature as `Add(d Device)` returning nothing. Pair-mint-side uniqueness check (`Name` collision, `TokenHash` collision) belongs in the consumer (`pyry pair` sibling), not the storage primitive. `Remove(name)` returns `true` iff a device with matching `Name` was found and removed — consumers can assert "the device I just revoked actually existed" before logging.
- **`FindByTokenHash` is byte-exact `==` over a linear scan, not `subtle.ConstantTimeCompare`.** Constant-time concern is the plain↔hash boundary (owned by `VerifyToken` from #208). Once the wire-presented plain has been hashed (deterministic SHA-256), comparing two 64-char hex strings is byte-exact — and any timing leak from `==` early-exit reveals a public derivative (a hash the attacker could compute themselves), not a secret. A linear scan with `==` is the simpler, correct shape.
- **`List` returns a shallow copy.** Callers may mutate the returned slice and its elements without affecting registry state. Deep copy is unnecessary because `Device`'s fields are all value types (`string`, `time.Time`); no field is a reference type that would alias.
- **Path is caller-supplied; the registry doesn't store it.** `Load(path)` and `Save(path)` take the absolute path each call. Daemon-startup wiring (Phase 3 sibling ticket) resolves `~/.pyry/<sanitized-name>/devices.json` alongside the existing `resolveSocketPath` / `resolveRegistryPath`. Storing the path inside the `Registry` would couple it to a single file location and prevent test patterns that load/save against `t.TempDir()`. Mirrors `internal/sessions`'s `loadRegistry(path)` / `saveRegistryLocked(path, reg)` discipline.
- **No logger, no `context.Context`, no `Config`.** Leaf primitive over the filesystem; the existing `slog` discipline applies to *callers* (the pair command logs "paired device <name>" after Save returns; the daemon's startup `Load` failure is fatal). Atomic-write is two syscalls (`Sync`, `Rename`) totaling a few hundred microseconds at p99 on a healthy local fs — adding ctx-cancel plumbing for that window would be ceremony without value. Mirrors `internal/sessions/registry.go`'s no-logger pattern.
- **Tests in `registry_test.go`** — same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere, stdlib only. Ten tests: `TestRegistry_LoadMissingFile`, `TestRegistry_LoadEmptyFile`, `TestRegistry_LoadMalformedJSON` (asserts wrapped `registry: parse` prefix), `TestRegistry_AddSaveLoadRoundTrip` (two devices, all four `Device` fields preserved; compares times via `time.Time.Equal`), `TestRegistry_RemovePresent`, `TestRegistry_RemoveAbsent`, `TestRegistry_FindByTokenHash` (table: hit, miss-empty, miss-non-matching, miss-empty-registry), `TestRegistry_SaveFilePermissions` (asserts parent dir mode `0o700` + file mode `0o600`; skipped on Windows), `TestRegistry_SaveStableOrdering` (two `Add` permutations → byte-identical bytes), `TestRegistry_SaveAtomicRenamePreservesOldFile` (chmod-the-dir-readonly trick proves the pre-existing file survives a failed save unchanged; skipped on Windows), `TestRegistry_ConcurrentReadWrite` (8 goroutines, mixed `Add` / `List` / `FindByTokenHash`; race-detector probe — if any method drops the lock, `go test -race` flags the slice header / element accesses).
- **Out of scope, by design.** `pyry pair` mint (sibling — builds a `Device`, calls `Add` then `Save`). `pyry pair revoke <name>` (sibling — calls `Remove(name)` then `Save`). WS-handshake auth (Phase 3 — calls `Load` once at daemon startup, `FindByTokenHash(HashToken(presented))` per phone connect). Per-device `last_seen_at` updates on each WS connect (auth-handler concern; this ticket persists the field, doesn't update it). Push-token registration metadata (future top-level field per `protocol-mobile.md:495`; the envelope shape supports additive growth). Schema versioning (defer until first migration). Encrypting `devices.json` at rest (defer; current threat model doesn't justify the operator UX cost). Migration to a database (defer).
- See [knowledge/features/devices-registry.md](knowledge/features/devices-registry.md), [knowledge/decisions/020-devices-registry-snapshot-then-write.md](knowledge/decisions/020-devices-registry-snapshot-then-write.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/209-pair-devices-registry-crud.md`](specs/architecture/209-pair-devices-registry-crud.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #207)
- **`internal/identity/store.go` — `LoadOrCreate(path) (ServerID, error)` first-run bootstrap.** New file (~96 LOC) co-located with the existing `server_id.go` (#206); package doc-comment relaxed to drop the "Pure types and validation; no I/O" claim. Production diff: +96 LOC `store.go` (new) + 5 LOC `server_id.go` (doc-comment edit). Test diff: +200 LOC `store_test.go` (new). Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing exported names, zero CLI surface.
- **Atomic-write recipe is structurally identical to `internal/sessions/registry.go:53-92`.** `MkdirAll(dir, 0o700)` → `CreateTemp(dir, ".server-id-*.tmp")` → `Chmod(0o600)` → `Write(<id>+"\n")` → `Sync` → `Close` → `Rename(tmp, path)`, with `defer os.Remove(tmp)` cleanup. SIGKILL between any two syscalls either commits cleanly or leaves no observable change. The temp's `0600` is set *before* writing data; rename preserves mode, so the final file is `0600` from byte one.
- **`strings.TrimSuffix(s, "\n")`, NOT `strings.TrimSpace`.** AC says "tolerates an *optional* trailing newline but otherwise validate strictly." `TrimSuffix` strips at most one terminal `\n` and leaves leading whitespace, `\r`, tabs, internal spaces in place — `ParseServerID` then rejects them. `TrimSpace` would tolerate `\r\n`, surrounding spaces, form-feeds, broadening the parser's accept set for no concrete reason. The corrupt-file test table pins this: CRLF, double-newline, leading-whitespace all return `ErrInvalidServerID`.
- **Corruption is operator-escalated, structurally.** A file failing `ParseServerID` returns `fmt.Errorf("identity: parse %s: %w", path, err)` — `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidServerID)` matches via the `%w` chain. The loader does **NOT** call `mintAndPersist` on the parse-fails path; the no-rewrite invariant is enforced by code structure (parse arm has no fallback into mint), not a flag a future maintainer could flip. Paired devices bind tokens to a specific server-id; silently regenerating would invalidate every pairing without operator awareness — this is a one-way decision.
- **Error strings include the path, never file contents.** A future log site that formatted corrupt bytes into a record would create an exfiltration vector for whatever happened to be in the file (operator's `/etc/shadow` if a symlink trick worked). The bare sentinel from `ParseServerID` carries no caller bytes; the wrap adds the path and nothing else. Operators investigate via the path, not via the error log.
- **No parent-directory fsync.** Per `lessons.md` § "Atomic on-disk writes": the rename's directory-entry update is durable enough on Linux ext4 / macOS APFS for operator-recoverable identity data. Stays consistent with `sessions.json`'s recipe.
- **No locking, no `context.Context`.** Bootstrap runs once on daemon startup before any goroutines fan out. Two pyry processes sharing HOME both observe ENOENT, both mint, both rename — the later rename wins; this is undefined behavior at the application level (two daemons sharing HOME is itself a misconfiguration). No security property is violated; the AC explicitly says no locking required. Documented in the function doc-comment.
- **Symlink/hardlink TOCTOU surface.** Write path: `Rename(tmp, path)` replaces the directory entry — a pre-existing symlink at `path` is unlinked; the original target is never touched (no write-through-symlink). Read path: `os.ReadFile` follows symlinks; an attacker-pre-created symlink to a readable file returns its contents, which fail `ParseServerID` and surface as `ErrInvalidServerID`. The path-only error message ensures contents do not leak via the loader's return value. Pre-existing parent-dir perms (e.g. `~/.pyry` already at `0o755` from an earlier tool) are NOT tightened by `MkdirAll(dir, 0o700)` — install/setup tooling owns that, not the loader.
- **Package boundary: `internal/identity` keeps the loader; the package doc-comment is relaxed.** `LoadOrCreate` lives at `internal/identity/store.go` rather than a sibling `internal/identitystore`. The loader has no API surface beyond `ServerID` — splitting forces every caller to dual-import for no abstraction win. Future identifier-loaders (e.g. `~/.pyry/devices.json` for the paired-device list) compose by adding files within `internal/identity` / `internal/devices`, not by adding packages. The "no I/O" claim was a #206-scope claim, not a permanent invariant. See [ADR 019](knowledge/decisions/019-identity-loader-co-located.md).
- **Caller resolves the absolute path.** `LoadOrCreate` takes an absolute path so tests can use `t.TempDir()`. The Phase-3 wiring ticket calls it from `cmd/pyry/main.go` against `~/.pyry/server-id` resolved alongside `resolveSocketPath` / `resolveRegistryPath`. Path resolution belongs to the daemon-startup site, not the loader (mirrors the `internal/config.Load(path)` discipline from #205).
- **Tests in `store_test.go`** — same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere, stdlib only. Five tests: `TestLoadOrCreate_FirstRunGeneratesAndPersists` (path under a non-existent subdir to verify `MkdirAll`; asserts file contents `<id>\n`, parent dir mode `0700`, file mode `0600`, second-call returns same id), `TestLoadOrCreate_ExistingFileRoundTripsWithoutRewrite` (pre-seeded canonical UUIDv4 + newline; asserts mtime unchanged via `time.Time.Equal` AND bytes byte-identical — mtime granularity on some filesystems is 1s, bytes are the harder check), `TestLoadOrCreate_ToleratesNoTrailingNewline` (pre-seed without newline, no rewrite), `TestLoadOrCreate_CorruptFileReturnsErrInvalidServerID` (six rows: not-a-uuid, empty, uppercase, leading whitespace, CRLF, double newline; each asserts `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidServerID)`, returned id `""`, **file bytes unchanged after the call**), `TestLoadOrCreate_ReadFileError` (make `path` itself a directory so `os.ReadFile` returns EISDIR; asserts non-nil error that is **not** `Is(ErrInvalidServerID)` — I/O errors distinguishable from corruption). Mode assertions use `info.Mode().Perm()`.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Path resolution (caller's job — `~/.pyry/server-id` is resolved at startup wiring). Caller wiring at daemon startup (Phase-3 ticket calls `LoadOrCreate` from `cmd/pyry/main.go`). `devices.json` persistence (sibling concern with multiple records, same atomic-write recipe). CLI surface (`pyry server-id` to print). Mode tightening for pre-existing parent dirs (install/setup tooling, not the loader). JSON round-trip (string newtype, library behavior).
- See [knowledge/features/identity-package.md](knowledge/features/identity-package.md), [knowledge/decisions/019-identity-loader-co-located.md](knowledge/decisions/019-identity-loader-co-located.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/207-server-id-store.md`](specs/architecture/207-server-id-store.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #211)
- **`internal/pair/payload.go` — QR pairing payload `Payload` + `Encode`/`Decode`.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`bytes`, `encoding/base64`, `encoding/json`, `errors`, `fmt`, `io`) plus `internal/identity` for `ServerID`; two new files (`payload.go` ~108 LOC, `payload_test.go` ~165 LOC). Four exports: `Payload` struct (`Server identity.ServerID` + `Relay string` + `Token string`, JSON tags `server`/`relay`/`token` — order pinned by `protocol-mobile.md`'s pairing-flow appendix lines 705-714), `Encode(p Payload) string` (`json.Marshal` → `base64.RawURLEncoding.EncodeToString`), `Decode(s string) (Payload, error)`, `ErrInvalidPayload` sentinel. No consumers wired in this slice — QR rendering and paste-fallback display are sibling #212; `pyry pair` CLI glue lands later.
- **Wire format is JSON then base64url with the URL-safe alphabet and NO padding** (`base64.RawURLEncoding`, not `URLEncoding` which has padding, not `StdEncoding` which uses `+/=`). Chosen for QR alphanumeric-mode compatibility and for paste-fallback robustness in URL contexts. Round-trip is byte-stable: same `Payload` produces a byte-identical encoded string twice (JSON marshaller emits fields in struct-declaration order) — the QR symbol scanned twice is the same QR symbol. `TestEncode_StableFieldOrder` pins this.
- **`Encode` panics on `json.Marshal` error rather than returning `(string, error)`.** `json.Marshal` of a struct whose fields are all stdlib string types with no `MarshalJSON` methods cannot fail. The AC pins the signature as `Encode(p Payload) string` (no error). Surfacing the impossible case via `panic` keeps the pure-function signature and makes the impossibility loud — silently returning a corrupt string would let an unreachable bug ship. The defensive branch is a `panic(fmt.Errorf("pair: json.Marshal of Payload failed: %w", err))`; operators will never see it on supported platforms.
- **`Encode` does NOT validate `p`.** The encoder's contract is "marshal what you're given." Empty fields produce a string `Decode` will reject; the round-trip surfaces the error. The minter (sibling ticket) is responsible for handing in a `ServerID` produced by `identity.NewServerID`, a token from `crypto/rand`, and a relay URL from `internal/config`. `Encode` does not log, redact, persist, or transform the token; pure function.
- **`Decode` applies five rejection categories in order, returning the first failure.** (1) Base64 — `base64.RawURLEncoding.DecodeString` is already strict (rejects characters outside the URL-safe alphabet, padding chars `=`, trailing bits not aligned to a byte; no extra check needed). (2) JSON — `json.Decoder.Decode(&p)` against a `bytes.Reader`. (3) Trailing bytes — a second `Decoder.Decode(&trailing)` MUST return `io.EOF`; `json.Unmarshal` silently consumes only the first JSON value, trailing bytes are lost, and the second-decode-must-be-EOF idiom catches `{"server":…}garbage` and `{"server":…}{"another":1}` (concatenated payloads — usual symptom of a malformed paste). Same idiom `internal/control`'s JSON framing already uses. (4) Field presence — `Server`, `Relay`, `Token` all non-empty strings; the error names the JSON tag (`server`, `relay`, `token`) — public protocol vocabulary, not secrets. (5) Server-id shape — `identity.ParseServerID(string(p.Server))` re-validates canonical UUIDv4 form. Package contract: `Decode` returns a `Payload` whose `Server` field is parse-validated.
- **Relay URL is NOT parsed/validated here.** Protocol contract is "the relay's domain is part of the pairing payload and trust-on-first-use from the phone's POV"; the binary doesn't dial it from this code path. Validation belongs to whichever caller actually dials. Token is NOT length- or alphabet-checked — protocol fixes the token at "256-bit random, hex-encoded" but that's the minter's contract, not the encoding layer's. `Decode` rejects empty; that's the contract this slice owns.
- **On any error, `Decode` returns the zero `Payload`.** Matches the `config.Load` discipline ("on any error the returned Config is the zero value"). Callers that ignore `err` see empty fields and break loudly rather than working with partial data. `TestDecode_ZeroPayloadOnError` pins this for every rejection case.
- **Sentinel + wrap shape mirrors `internal/identity`'s `ErrInvalidServerID`.** `var ErrInvalidPayload = errors.New("pair: invalid payload")`; every rejection path returns `fmt.Errorf("%w: <category>", ErrInvalidPayload)`. `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidPayload)` is the only matcher callers should use. Categories: `"invalid base64url encoding"`, `"invalid JSON"`, `"trailing data after JSON object"`, `"missing field: <name>"`, `"invalid server id"`. Bounded-length category strings; field NAMES (`server`/`relay`/`token`) are safe to include — public protocol vocabulary; field VALUES are never echoed.
- **SECURITY: error strings never include input bytes or decoded field values.** The `Token` field carries the plaintext bearer; `protocol-mobile.md:608-609` and `:663` pin "visibility ends when the QR symbol is dismissed" / "MUST never display the device-token in plaintext after initial pairing." Three discipline points enforce this: (a) `Decode` errors are category strings only, no input echo — `TestDecode_Errors` asserts the error string contains no character of the input on every row; (b) the package doc comment instructs callers to never log `Payload`, `Encode` output, or `Decode` errors in any context that may persist user-visible output; (c) `Encode` does not log, redact, or persist anything (pure function). The QR screenshot itself is the user's risk (auto-uploaded cloud backup is the documented threat); this package contributes the encoding layer that does NOT introduce a second exposure surface.
- **Why a separate `internal/pair` package** — pairing is its own concern, owned by neither `internal/identity` (typed identifiers, no transport encoding) nor `internal/devices` (on-disk device entries + token-hash) nor `internal/config` (operator-editable settings). The name mirrors the user-visible verb (`pyry pair`); future siblings (QR/paste rendering #212, `pyry pair` CLI implementation, `pyry pair list` surface) land naturally without bloating an unrelated package.
- **Tests in `payload_test.go`** — same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere, stdlib `testing` only. Five tests: `TestEncodeDecodeRoundTrip` (AC #4 — 100 iterations against fresh `identity.NewServerID()` ids), `TestEncode_Format` (AC #3 — encoded string non-empty, only base64url-safe chars `[A-Za-z0-9_-]`, no `=` padding, decodes via `RawURLEncoding` to a valid JSON object — pins wire format so future encoder swap can't pass round-trip silently), `TestEncode_StableFieldOrder` (encode-twice byte-identical), `TestDecode_Errors` (table covers empty, non-base64, non-JSON, missing-each-field, present-but-empty-each-field, invalid server-id, uppercase server-id, trailing JSON object, trailing garbage, padded base64; each row asserts `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidPayload)` AND error string contains no character of input — token-leakage defense), `TestDecode_ZeroPayloadOnError`. No fixtures, no `t.TempDir`, no PTY; runs under `go test -race ./...` in milliseconds.
- **Production diff: `internal/pair/payload.go` +108 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/pair/payload_test.go` +165 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package, zero CLI surface, zero wire format change.
- **Out of scope, by design.** QR rendering and paste-fallback display (sibling #212 — this package owns the string, #212 owns the surface that displays it). `pyry pair` CLI (later phase-3 ticket — wires `identity.NewServerID()` + token mint + `config.Load().RelayURL` into a `Payload`, calls `Encode`, hands string to #212). Token minting (later phase-3 ticket — `crypto/rand` 256-bit + hex). On-disk persistence of paired devices (#208 owns hashing; registry-CRUD sibling loads/saves rows). Envelope versioning (a future v2 encrypted payload would land as a separate `EncodeV2`/`DecodeV2` pair or a versioned wire format). Relay URL syntax validation (owned by whichever caller dials). Token alphabet/length checks (minter owns format).
- See [knowledge/features/pair-package.md](knowledge/features/pair-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/211-pair-qr-payload-encoding.md`](specs/architecture/211-pair-qr-payload-encoding.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #208)
- **`internal/devices/device.go` — `Device` struct + token hashing primitives.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`crypto/sha256`, `crypto/subtle`, `encoding/hex`, `time`); two new files (`device.go` ~48 LOC including doc comment, `device_test.go` ~98 LOC). Three exports: `Device` (on-disk shape with `TokenHash string`, `Name string`, `PairedAt time.Time`, `LastSeenAt time.Time`; snake_case JSON tags, no `omitempty`), `HashToken(plain) string` (lowercase SHA-256 hex via `sha256.Sum256` + `hex.EncodeToString`), `VerifyToken(plain, hash) bool` (`subtle.ConstantTimeCompare` on `HashToken(plain)` vs `hash`). No exported errors; the verify primitive returns bool by design — auth-decision-as-error belongs to the caller. No consumers wired in this slice — registry CRUD, token minting, and WS-handshake auth wiring are sibling tickets.
- **`subtle.ConstantTimeCompare` is the only comparison.** Returns 0 (false) when slice lengths differ, in constant time relative to the slice arguments. Empty `hash`, malformed `hash`, any-length-≠-64 `hash` all fall out via the length-mismatch path — there is intentionally **no early-return guard on `hash == ""`**. The unguarded shape is shorter, makes the constant-time discipline auditable in one line, and the AC bullet "false on empty/malformed hash" is satisfied by `ConstantTimeCompare`'s documented semantics. `==`, `bytes.Equal`, `strings.EqualFold` on hash material are forbidden by review.
- **No bcrypt, no per-token salt.** Recorded in the feature doc so the next reviewer doesn't relitigate it. The token is 256 bits of `crypto/rand` (sibling minting ticket); brute force across 2^256 is infeasible regardless of hash speed. The hash exists only to prevent plaintext-at-rest — if `devices.json` leaks, the attacker holds hashes, not tokens. Bcrypt is designed for low-entropy human passwords (irrelevant at 256 bits; also caps input at 72 bytes — a footgun for future format changes). Per-token salt defends against precomputation on shared-keyspace inputs (irrelevant for 256-bit random). Both add complexity for no defensive gain. Aligns with `protocol-mobile.md:62` ("binary stores `sha256(token)` in `devices.json`, never the plaintext") — protocol spec already commits the binary to plain SHA-256.
- **JSON tags are snake_case, no `omitempty`, mirror `internal/sessions/registry.go:17-29`'s `registryEntry` shape.** Required fields round-trip at zero value. The sibling registry-CRUD ticket can marshal `Device` with stdlib `encoding/json` unchanged. The struct definition is in this ticket; the registry CRUD that marshals it is in a sibling ticket — adding the tags here keeps that sibling trivial. Tags are pure addition (compiler sees them, runtime only via `encoding/json`); the AC bullet's literal field list is satisfied — the tags are metadata, not new fields.
- **SECURITY contract is in the package doc comment**, not just review tribal knowledge. The package doc names: callers MUST NOT log a plain device-token, MUST NOT wrap a plain token into error context, MUST NOT pass a plain token across log/slog fields. The plain appears at exactly two sites — pairing (QR + paste-fallback string) and per-WS-connect (phone presents) — outside those, only the SHA-256 hex hash exists on disk and in memory. Neither `HashToken` nor `VerifyToken` logs anything; the package returns no error and never embeds caller input — leaks can only originate in callers. Code review enforces this on any future caller that accepts plain.
- **Determinism is intentional.** Same plain produces the same hash across runs, machines, processes — what makes verify trivial (compute once, compare). The cost is "two binaries with the same plain token would store identical hashes" — irrelevant because each binary mints its own tokens for its own paired devices; tokens don't cross binaries.
- **Pure functions, no concurrency primitives.** No package-level state, no goroutines, no mutexes. Concurrent callers are safe by construction. No `*slog.Logger` parameter (neither function logs), no `context.Context` (no I/O, no cancellation point), no `Config` (SHA-256 is the chosen primitive, not a switch).
- **Tests in `device_test.go`** — same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere. `TestHashToken_Deterministic` (same input → same output, length 64, all lowercase hex; pins `HashToken("abc") == ba7816bf...015ad` — published SHA-256("abc") test vector — as a regression guard against accidental swap to SHA-1 or different encoding). `TestVerifyToken` (seven-row table covering AC's four bullets plus three malformed-hash rows): matching token (true), non-matching token (false), empty hash, too-short hash, too-long hash, non-hex `"zzz...zzz"` (proves no accidental hex-decode of either side), uppercase hex hash (documents on-disk is canonical lowercase; the package does not silently normalise — a caller storing uppercase by mistake gets `false` and discovers the bug at first authentication). No fuzz target (input space fully covered by the table). No `-race` test (pure functions, no shared state).
- **Production diff: `internal/devices/device.go` +48 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/devices/device_test.go` +98 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package, zero CLI surface, zero wire format change.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Token minting (sibling: `crypto/rand` 256-bit + hex encode + QR display + paste-fallback). Registry CRUD (sibling: load/save `Device` rows to `~/.pyry/<name>/devices.json` via the same atomic-rename + `0600` pattern `saveRegistryLocked` uses). Auth wiring (Phase 3: WS handshake calls `VerifyToken(presented, device.TokenHash)`; on false returns `auth.invalid_token` per `protocol-mobile.md:97-98`). `pyry pair revoke <name>` (per-device revocation falls out of removing the row; structurally supported — each row is independent). `Device.TokenHashPrefix() string` for `pair list` UI (defer; display rule lives in `protocol-mobile.md:663`). `[]byte` overload for `HashToken` (rejected — AC fixes signature as `string`; both call sites naturally hold strings). Memory-zeroing `plain` after hashing (Go strings are immutable; runtime exposes no "secure erase" — rely on protocol-level discipline instead).
- See [knowledge/features/devices-package.md](knowledge/features/devices-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/208-pair-device-entry-and-token-hashing.md`](specs/architecture/208-pair-device-entry-and-token-hashing.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #206)
- **`internal/identity/server_id.go` — typed `ServerID` + UUIDv4 generation + canonical validation.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`crypto/rand`, `errors`, `fmt`); two new files (`server_id.go` ~83 LOC, `server_id_test.go` ~94 LOC). Three exports: `ServerID` (string newtype, public routing identifier for one pyrycode-binary instance), `NewServerID() ServerID` (fresh UUIDv4 from `crypto/rand`, version + variant nibbles set, formatted canonical lowercase hex), `ParseServerID(s string) (ServerID, error)` (validates canonical UUIDv4 shape, returns `ErrInvalidServerID` on failure). One sentinel: `ErrInvalidServerID`. Empty `ServerID("")` is the unset sentinel; never a valid generated id. No consumers wired in this slice — persistence sibling and Phase 3 pairing/relay tickets land separately.
- **Pattern mirrors `sessions/id.go` almost verbatim**, with three AC-forced divergences: (1) `NewServerID` returns `ServerID` (no error) — `crypto/rand.Read` is documented infallible on supported platforms, so the impl panics on the impossible-on-supported-platforms branch rather than returning an error the AC's signature can't carry; silently degrading to a zero-entropy id would break the unguessability the relay-routing security model depends on. (2) `ParseServerID` returns `(ServerID, error)`, not a bool — wraps the same validation logic as `sessions.ValidID`. (3) **No code reuse between packages** — `internal/identity` does NOT import `internal/sessions`; the dependency direction is wrong (sessions are an implementation detail that should be free to import identity later, not the reverse), so the six-line `validUUIDv4` switch/case is duplicated intentionally.
- **`internal/identity` is a separate package from `internal/sessions`** because `sessions.ServerID` would suggest a per-session id, which is wrong (one server-id per binary instance, independent of session lifecycle). Splitting also frees `internal/identity` to grow with future identifier types (device-id, paired-device-id) without bloating sessions. The package is positioned as the home for typed identifiers that span subsystems.
- **No caller-input embedding in `ErrInvalidServerID`.** The error is returned as the bare sentinel — no `fmt.Errorf("...%q...", s, ErrInvalidServerID)` wrap with the input string. Embedding caller-supplied bytes in the error message is a needless log-injection vector for a function that may run on relay-supplied input. Callers that need richer context wrap themselves; `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidServerID)` is the contract.
- **`crypto/rand`-failure panics, not silently degrades.** The defensive branch is `panic(fmt.Errorf("identity: crypto/rand failed: %w", err))`. Operators will never see this on supported platforms; if they do, the alternative (returning a zero-entropy `ServerID`) is strictly worse — silently broken unguessability vs. an immediate crash that surfaces the missing system rng.
- **Package boundary forbids `ServerID(rawString)` outside `internal/identity`.** Go's type system can't strictly prevent direct conversion in another package since `ServerID` is exported. The rule is documented in the type comment and review-enforced; `internal/` visibility contains the exposure to the pyrycode module itself, which is sufficient (no public API surface here).
- **Tests in `server_id_test.go`** — same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere. `TestNewServerID_Format` (regexp tighter than sessions/id_test.go's because `ParseServerID` enforces version + variant). `TestNewServerID_Unique` (1000-iteration uniqueness; catches a constant-zero rng wiring bug, mirrors `sessions/id_test.go`). `TestParseServerID` (table covers valid variants 8/9/a/b, empty, length 35/37, uppercase, wrong version, wrong variant, non-hex char, missing dash, dash at wrong position; negative assertions use `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidServerID)` so the sentinel is verified reachable, not just "some error"). `TestNewServerID_RoundTripsParseServerID` is AC #4's first item directly: generate → parse → equal.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Persistence (sibling ticket — load raw string from disk, feed to `ParseServerID`). JSON round-trip tests (`encoding/json` on a string newtype is library behavior; persistence sibling covers JSON disk format). Human label suffix in QR (per `protocol-mobile.md:61`'s "may have a human label suffix in the QR for UX" — that's a QR-encoding concern, not an id-type concern). CLI surface (`pyry server-id` print verb — defer). Pairing payload / relay handshake wiring — Phase 3 follow-ups.
- **Production diff: `internal/identity/server_id.go` +83 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/identity/server_id_test.go` +94 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package.
- See [knowledge/features/identity-package.md](knowledge/features/identity-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/206-server-id-type-and-generation.md`](specs/architecture/206-server-id-type-and-generation.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #205)
- **`internal/config/config.go` — typed schema + overlay loader for `~/.pyry/config.json`.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`encoding/json`, `errors`, `fmt`, `io/fs`, `os`); two new files (`config.go` ~46 LOC, `config_test.go` ~82 LOC). Three exports: `Config` struct (one field today, `RelayURL string` with `json:"relay_url"`, no `omitempty` so the field round-trips when set to its zero value), `DefaultConfig() Config` (returns `Config{RelayURL: "wss://relay.pyrycode.dev"}` — placeholder domain, real one TBD when the relay is provisioned), and `Load(path string) (Config, error)`. No consumers wired in this slice — daemon startup and `pyry pair` will import from their own tickets. No `Save`, no watcher, no path resolution, no URL validation, no schema versioning. Foundation for Phase 3 (mobile + relay) work.
- **Overlay-decode is the load-bearing trick.** `Load` initializes `cfg := DefaultConfig()` *before* `json.Unmarshal(data, &cfg)`. `encoding/json` only writes fields present in the document — absent fields keep their pre-decode value. So `{}` returns `DefaultConfig()`, and `{"relay_url": "wss://my-relay.example/"}` returns defaults with only `RelayURL` overridden. Adding a Phase 3 field is then additive: append to the struct, append a default, no migration code, no schema version bump. Existing config files pick up new defaults automatically; users who pinned a value are unaffected. See [ADR 018](knowledge/decisions/018-config-overlay-decode.md).
- **Five behaviors, three error wraps.** Missing file → `DefaultConfig(), nil` (canonical `errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist)` predicate, same one `loadRegistry` uses). Valid JSON → merged config + nil. `{}` → `DefaultConfig()` (overlay no-op). Malformed JSON → `Config{}, fmt.Errorf("config: parse %s: %w", path, err)`. Read errors (perms, IO) → `Config{}, fmt.Errorf("config: read %s: %w", path, err)`. Empty file (0 bytes) falls out as a wrapped JSON-parse error naturally — `json.Unmarshal([]byte{}, ...)` returns `unexpected end of JSON input`. Asymmetry vs. `loadRegistry`'s empty-as-missing is deliberate: the registry is pyry-owned, the config is user-owned; an empty config file is operator error.
- **Error path returns `Config{}`, not `DefaultConfig()`.** Callers that ignore `err` see an empty `RelayURL` and break loudly rather than silently using the placeholder default. Returning defaults on error would mask real problems (e.g. a typo in `relay_url` would silently keep talking to the placeholder relay).
- **`config:` wrap prefix matches the `registry:` convention** `loadRegistry` established. Same `errors.Is`-friendly shape — callers can branch on `fs.ErrPermission` / `fs.ErrInvalid` etc. without losing context.
- **Default lives in the function body, not a package-level `const`.** Two reasons: (1) the surface stays minimal — one exported function, no exported constant for callers to confuse with "the current value"; (2) when more fields land, the constructor grows naturally to a multi-line struct literal, the canonical Go idiom for default-with-options.
- **Tests in `config_test.go`** — same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` on every case (no shared state — each writes its own `t.TempDir()`). `TestDefaultConfig` pins the literal default (will fail loudly when the real relay domain lands — that's the right signal). `TestLoad` table covers the four file-path AC bullets: missing file → defaults, valid full file → override, partial file `{}` → defaults preserved (regression guard for the overlay property when more fields land), malformed JSON → wrapped error containing `"config: parse"`. `Config` is a small comparable struct → direct `==` works, no `reflect.DeepEqual`. No checked-in golden files, no `testdata/` directory. Inline `ptr := func(s string) *string { return &s }` for the optional-fileBody table column over importing a generics utility.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Path resolution (`Load` takes any `path` string; the consumer ticket adds `resolveConfigPath()` alongside `resolveSocketPath` / `resolveRegistryPath` in `cmd/pyry/main.go` — doing it here would bind to `os.UserHomeDir` semantics that some future caller with a `--config` override wants to compose differently). `Save` (read-only this slice; future ticket adds atomic-rename write primitive if/when needed). Hot reload (one-shot read at startup; if needed later, a separate seam — most likely `sync/atomic.Pointer[Config]` swapped on file-watcher events). Schema versioning (per the ticket: "if `Config` ever grows incompatibly, version it at that point" — `encoding/json`'s default lenient handling covers backward-additive changes for free; mirrors `registryFile.Version`'s "reserved but unused" posture). URL validation (`pyry pair` validates before connecting; the config package's contract is "decode JSON into a struct"). Permission-denied test row (hard to make portable across CI users; one-line read-error wrap is covered by inspection).
- **Production diff: `internal/config/config.go` +46 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/config/config_test.go` +82 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package, zero CLI surface.
- See [knowledge/features/config-package.md](knowledge/features/config-package.md), [knowledge/decisions/018-config-overlay-decode.md](knowledge/decisions/018-config-overlay-decode.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/205-config-load-and-schema.md`](specs/architecture/205-config-load-and-schema.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #203)
- **`install.sh` — post-install smoke check**, ~80 LOC appended after the existing "next: see deployment.md" line. New helpers: `service_present_darwin`/`service_present_linux` (running-state detection), `restart_darwin`/`restart_linux`, `classify_status` (pure classification of captured `pyry status` output + exit code), `smoke_check` (orchestrator). New `fail_with_code` helper next to `err` for structured-exit errors (4 = restart-fail). The script's `set -euo pipefail` contract is preserved: detection helpers are called from `if`-guards (consumes the non-zero return); restart and `pyry status` are wrapped in `set +e` / `set -e` bands so their exit codes can be inspected without aborting the script.
- **Bash, not Go.** The probe runs at the install chokepoint (curl-piped + the `deployment.md`-documented "Updating the binary" command), which is `install.sh`. A Go subcommand would have added a new public CLI surface and a chicken-and-egg problem on first install (the freshly-extracted binary needs to know its service-management context). The ticket's technical-notes section asked for "Bash, grep, awk only — no new binary dependencies"; the impl honors that. See [ADR 017](knowledge/decisions/017-install-script-smoke-check.md).
- **Detection gates on currently-running services**, not "unit file present." `launchctl print "gui/$(id -u)/dev.pyrycode.pyry" | grep -q 'state = running'` on darwin; `systemctl --user is-active --quiet pyry` on linux (preceded by a `is-system-running` D-Bus-availability check that returns false for `offline`/`unknown`/empty — CI runners). The architect's open-question note flagged this: gating on "loaded" would auto-start a unit the operator deliberately disabled. `is-active` matches the population at risk (the update path where #202 manifested), not first-install where the operator hasn't yet run `enable --now`.
- **Four exit codes, four messages.** `0` healthy, `2` sentinel detected (the canonical #202 observable), `3` dial-fail (`pyry status` non-zero — control socket unreachable inside its own retry+timeout window), `4` restart-fail (service manager rejected `kickstart`/`restart`). AC #4 explicitly distinguishes sentinel from dial-fail; the four-code split preserves the diagnostic for downstream automation. Each message names the symptom, the issue link (#202 for the sentinel case), and a next action (e.g. `journalctl --user -u pyry` / `tail /tmp/pyry.{out,err}.log`).
- **Sentinel match is one anchored grep**: `^Uptime: +2562047h47m16\.854775807s$` against captured stdout+stderr from `${INSTALL_DIR}/pyry status`. The `+` (not single-space) allows `runStatus`'s variable-width column padding when other keys (`Last uptime:`) are wider. We deliberately do NOT also parse `Started at: 0001-01-01T00:00:00Z` — two checks against the same observable add zero coverage and one risks false negatives if the format drifts.
- **No manual `sleep` before the probe.** `pyry status` already retries `ENOENT`/`ECONNREFUSED` for ~1.5s via `internal/control.dialWithRetry` (#199) and times out at 5s total via `runStatus`'s context deadline. That window IS the AC's "brief grace period." Adding `sleep 5` on top would double the wall-clock cost on the healthy path.
- **Probes `${INSTALL_DIR}/pyry`, not bare `pyry`.** First-time install may not have `INSTALL_DIR` on `$PATH` yet (the existing PATH-advisory block warns about this). Calling the freshly-installed binary directly is robust.
- **`internal/install/test_smoke_classify.sh` is a bash-only unit test for `classify_status`.** Sources only the `# ---------- post-install smoke check` to `# ---------- main` band of `install.sh` (extracted via `awk`) so `main()` doesn't run, then feeds three pre-canned `pyry status` outputs and asserts return codes 0 / 2 / 3. Not wired into Go's test runner — XS bash test for the bash classifier. Manual round-trip on each platform is the load-bearing coverage; this script is the cheap regression net for the pure rule.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Custom `-pyry-name foo` deployment detection (operator already off the default; falls through to skip with the same generic message). `--no-smoke-check` / `--dry-run` flags (no observed need; the detection branch IS the no-op path). Detection of failure classes other than the canonical `Uptime` sentinel — broader liveness checks belong in `pyry status` itself or a separate health-check ticket. Automated `install.sh` integration tests in `internal/e2e/` — extending those would balloon scope; manual round-trip on each platform is the agreed coverage for an XS bash change.
- **Production diff +117 LOC `install.sh` (no Go code touched), +96 LOC `internal/install/test_smoke_classify.sh` (new file), zero changes to the published binary surface, zero new dependencies.**
- See [knowledge/features/install-script.md](knowledge/features/install-script.md), [knowledge/decisions/017-install-script-smoke-check.md](knowledge/decisions/017-install-script-smoke-check.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/203-install-smoke-check.md`](specs/architecture/203-install-smoke-check.md), [ADR 016](knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md) for the underlying #202 fix this probe defends.

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #202)
- **`internal/sessions/pool.go:275` — bootstrap-only carve-out at the load layer.** Two-line production-code fix: `Pool.New`'s `pickBootstrap` arm replaces `lcState = parseLifecycleState(entry.LifecycleState)` with `lcState = stateActive` plus an explicit `_ = entry.LifecycleState` to flag the field is intentionally read-and-ignored. Doc comment names the reason verbatim ("daemon-mode startup contract is 'claude is available' … persisting `evicted` for the bootstrap and waking with no attach client to drive `Activate` would hang the daemon forever"). Non-bootstrap sessions still go through `parseLifecycleState` — lazy respawn on attach is correct for them.
- **Symptom: `pyry --dangerously-skip-permissions </dev/null` hangs forever on v0.10.1** under non-TTY stdin (launchd / systemd / piped wrapper). Daemon reaches `"pyrycode starting"` and the control server (`pyry status` and `pyry stop` answer) but never logs `"spawning claude"`. `pyry status` reports `Started at: 0001-01-01T00:00:00Z` and `Uptime: 2562047h47m16.854775807s` — `time.Duration(math.MaxInt64).String()`, the smoking-gun zero-time tell that `Supervisor.Run` was never called. `sample <pid>` shows the main goroutine parked on `pthread_cond_wait`.
- **Latent since #40 (idle eviction, v0.8.0); surfaced by #190's `pyry update` auto-restart (v0.10.1).** Sequence: cold start → bootstrap active → claude spawns → idle timer fires after 15min with no attach → `transitionTo(stateEvicted)` writes `lifecycle_state: "evicted"` to disk → daemon restart (`pyry update` post-replace, machine reboot, manual `launchctl kickstart`, crash-loop) → `Pool.New.pickBootstrap` loads `lcState = stateEvicted` → `Session.Run` enters `runEvicted` → `select { case <-ctx.Done(): … case <-s.activateCh: … }` → nothing ever sends on `activateCh` because `Pool.Run` only calls `p.supervise(bootstrap)` then `g.Wait()`; consumer-driven `Activate` paths (attach, `sessions.new`, `GetOrCreate`) don't fire under `</dev/null`. Pre-#190, kickstart cycles were operator-driven and rare; users typically restarted the daemon before the first idle window elapsed, so `sessions.json` still had `lifecycle_state: "active"`. #190's auto-restart is the trigger that exposed the latent bug, not the cause.
- **The fix lives at the load layer, not in `Pool.Run`.** Architect explicitly considered and rejected three alternatives: (1) `p.Activate(ctx, p.bootstrap)` after `p.supervise` in `Pool.Run` — extra disk write at every evicted-bootstrap warm-start plus a synchronous park inside `Activate`'s wait; (2) raw send on `activateCh` from `Pool.Run` — bypasses the `Activate` / `Evict` contract and is brittle to future refactors of the lifecycle goroutine's drain order; (3) special-case `runEvicted` to peek for the bootstrap — conflates concerns inside the lifecycle goroutine. Load-layer carve-out keeps the state machine uniform; only the bootstrap's initial condition differs. See [ADR 016](knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md).
- **AC#3 (`pyry status` shows real `Started at`, not zero-time) is satisfied structurally.** Once `lcState = stateActive` on warm-load, `Session.Run` goes straight into `runActive`, which spawns `Supervisor.Run`, which sets `State.StartedAt = time.Now()` at `supervisor.go:156`. The zero-time sentinel becomes unreachable on the supervisor-mode startup path. No changes to the `status` verb or `Supervisor.State`.
- **Disk consistency: warm-start does NOT rewrite the registry.** The on-disk `lifecycle_state: "evicted"` is left untouched per the existing "warm start is not a state change" invariant in `Pool.New`. The first state transition the running daemon makes (almost always the next idle eviction) rewrites the registry with the then-current state. Brief disk/memory disagreement during the warm-start window is harmless; in-memory state is the source of truth for a running daemon.
- **Tests in `internal/sessions/pool_test.go`** (+101 LOC). `TestPool_BootstrapEvictedOnDisk_StartsClaudeOnWarmStart` (new): pre-writes `sessions.json` with a single bootstrap entry whose `lifecycle_state` is `"evicted"` (the exact on-disk shape after one idle-eviction-then-restart cycle), runs `Pool.New` + `Pool.Run` against `/bin/sleep 3600` as the supervised child via `Bridge` mode, polls `sess.State()` for `Phase == PhaseRunning && ChildPID > 0` within a 5s deadline, asserts `StartedAt` is non-zero. Verified to fail against the pre-fix v0.10.1 binary (the supervisor never reaches `PhaseRunning` because `runEvicted` parks). `TestPool_BootstrapWarmStart_IgnoresPersistedEvicted` (renamed from `TestPool_BootstrapWarmStartsEvicted`): asserts the new contract directly via `pool.Default().LifecycleState() == stateActive`. `TestSession_ActivateBlocksUntilPersisted` (rewritten in `session_persist_test.go`): the previous "warm-start in evicted" fixture is no longer reachable for the bootstrap; the persist-blocks-wake contract is now exercised by `Evict-then-Activate` instead of `warm-start-from-evicted`.
- **Bridge mode mirrors the non-TTY supervisor path the user reproduces** (`cmd/pyry/main.go:373` — non-TTY stdin selects supervisor mode with the bridge wired up). It also keeps the supervisor's I/O pumps off `os.Stdin` so the test doesn't contend with `go test`'s stdin.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Friendlier `pyry status` rendering for un-initialised supervisors (the technical-notes paragraph in the ticket; correctly flagged as out of scope because the fix makes the zero-time sentinel structurally unreachable on the supervisor-mode startup path). Defensive `install.sh` post-install check for the same failure mode (split out as a sibling ticket per the issue body). Auditing whether non-bootstrap sessions need similar warm-start activation logic — they don't; non-bootstrap sessions are designed for lazy respawn on attach (Phase 1.3's whole point), and persisted `evicted` is the correct steady state for them between daemon restarts.
- **Production diff +12 LOC `internal/sessions/pool.go`. Test diff +101 LOC `pool_test.go` + 45 LOC reshape `session_persist_test.go`.** Zero new files, zero new dependencies, zero changes to the lifecycle state machine itself, zero changes to `Pool.Run`, zero changes to `Session.Run` / `runEvicted` / `runActive`.
- See [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md § Registry schema delta](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md](knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/202-supervise-bootstrap-evicted-warm-start-hang.md`](specs/architecture/202-supervise-bootstrap-evicted-warm-start-hang.md), [`docs/lessons.md` § Persisted lifecycle state needs a driver](lessons.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #199)
- **`internal/control/dial.go` — bounded retry loop wrapping the existing `dial()` primitive.** Consumes #198's `isTransientStartupError` predicate. Production diff: `dial.go` +75 LOC (existing file, predicate already there); `client.go` -13 LOC (the old `dial()` body relocated, `net` import dropped). Test diff: `dial_test.go` +114 LOC (new `TestDialWithRetry` with three subtests against a shared `fakeDialer`). Zero behaviour change on the non-transient exit; zero server-side changes; zero new exports; zero new dependencies. Wire output for budget-exhaustion is byte-identical to pre-#199 single-shot dial — preserved structurally via three identical `fmt.Errorf("dial %s: %w", socketPath, err)` exit-door wraps.
- **One site covers every client verb.** `pyry status`, `pyry sessions list/new/rename/rm`, `pyry attach`, `pyry attach --stdio` all route through `request()` → `dial()` → `dialWithRetry`. The two attach paths (`attach_client.go:53`, `attach_stdio_client.go:34`) don't need their own retries — they call the same package-private `dial`. The PO ticket's "single-site wrap of the dial primitive" framing held literally.
- **`dialWithRetry(ctx, socketPath, fn dialFunc, budget, interval)` is the test-driven loop; `dial()` is a one-line wrapper passing production constants and `netDialUnix`.** Constants (`dialRetryBudget = 1500 * time.Millisecond`, `dialRetryInterval = 50 * time.Millisecond`) are package-level `const`, not `var` — production behaviour is fixed; tests parameterise via `dialWithRetry`'s arguments rather than mutating package state. ~30 attempts fit inside the budget. Sized for the launchctl-kickstart and `pyry update` self-restart window observed 2026-05-08 during the v0.9.1 → v0.10.1 Mac upgrade.
- **`dialFunc` is the test seam** — an unexported function-typed alias (`func(ctx context.Context, socketPath string) (net.Conn, error)`). Production passes the package-private `netDialUnix` (thin `net.Dialer.DialContext("unix", …)` wrapper, kept as a named function rather than a closure so each call avoids capturing a `net.Dialer` per invocation). Tests pass a `fakeDialer.dial` method satisfying the same shape. Same pattern as `updateOptions`'s function-typed seams (#190's `runRestart` / `probeRestart`) — function-typed field on a callable, not a package-level var or build tag.
- **Default-deadline fallback moved into `dialWithRetry`, not `dial`.** The `if _, ok := ctx.Deadline(); !ok { ctx, cancel = context.WithTimeout(ctx, DialTimeout) }` block that used to live in `dial()` now sits at the top of `dialWithRetry` so production `dial` stays a one-liner. Caller-deadline behaviour is unchanged from pre-#199.
- **Three exit doors, all preserving the original transient error.** Non-transient: return `fmt.Errorf("dial %s: %w", socketPath, err)` immediately. Budget exhaustion (`!time.Now().Before(deadline)`): same wrap. Ctx cancel during the inter-attempt sleep: same wrap. Use `Before` with negation rather than `After` to handle the boundary tick — at `t = deadline` exactly we exit with the wrapped transient error rather than sleeping past the budget. The three wraps are identical strings so a future grep on the wrap shape finds all three.
- **First attempt is immediate.** No pre-sleep. The fast-path "daemon is up" stays one `connect(2)` + return — no behavioural cost when the daemon is healthy.
- **`time.NewTimer` + `Stop()` on ctx cancel**, not `time.After`. The `time.After` leak is bounded (interval = 50 ms) but harmless to fix and matches the "no leaks under cancel" discipline already in the codebase.
- **`ctx.Done()` short-circuits the inter-attempt sleep, not the dial call.** A caller-side context cancel during the sleep returns the most recent transient error wrapped (not `ctx.Err()`). During a dial attempt itself, the cancel propagates through `net.Dialer.DialContext` per the stdlib contract and surfaces as a wrapped `context.Canceled` — *not* a transient startup error, so the next loop iteration takes the non-transient exit immediately. Two propagation paths, both correct, both preserve the wrap shape.
- **No new goroutines, no new shared state, no mutexes.** Same shape as the pre-#199 per-call dial — synchronous loop driven by `time.NewTimer` and `ctx.Done()`.
