The retry is per-`dial()`-call; concurrent `pyry status` invocations each run their own loop independently. Same per-call concurrency model the rest of the control client uses.
- **Tests in `dial_test.go`** — three subtests under one new `TestDialWithRetry` driven by a shared `fakeDialer{seq []error, calls int}` whose `dial` method counts calls and returns the next entry from `seq` (or `syscall.ENOENT` when exhausted, so an under-counting test doesn't accidentally succeed). On `nil` entries it returns `net.Pipe()`'s c1 (with c2 closed inline) — the cheapest stdlib `net.Conn` that doesn't need a listener. Tests close the returned conn before exiting. Subtests: (1) **recovers after N transient failures** — `seq: [ENOENT, ENOENT, ENOENT, nil]`, `budget = 200 ms`, `interval = 10 ms`, asserts non-nil conn, `f.calls == 4`, elapsed ≤ `N*interval + 50 ms`; (2) **always-transient exhausts budget** — empty `seq` (defaults to ENOENT), `budget = 100 ms`, `interval = 10 ms`, asserts `errors.Is(err, syscall.ENOENT)`, error string contains `"dial /fake/path:"`, elapsed ∈ `[budget, budget + 50 ms]` — lower bound proves retries actually ran for the full budget; (3) **non-transient error fails immediately** — `seq: [io.EOF]` with production constants (safe since failure is immediate regardless of budget), asserts `f.calls == 1`, `errors.Is(err, io.EOF)`, elapsed ≤ 50 ms.
- **+50 ms slack on timing assertions, documented in code comment as "for CI scheduling".** Architect's "+~5 ms" was the loop's steady-state intent, not the assertion margin — 5 ms is too tight under loaded `-race` runs. If real flakes appear under CI's `-race` we raise to 100 ms; the slack is modest enough that "no retry" or "wrong budget" still fails.
- **No e2e in this ticket.** Driven by `dialFunc` injection; the real dial path is exercised by every existing `pyry status` / `pyry sessions list` e2e that already routes through `dial`. AC #1 ("success after `launchctl kickstart -k`") is satisfied structurally — the wrapper covers all client verbs at one site, so a later e2e for any client verb that runs against a freshly-kickstarted daemon will exercise the retry transparently.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Server-side ready signaling (launchd has no `sd_notify` equivalent; would be platform-specific code in the daemon). A `pyry wait` UX verb (client-side retry covers more cases — manual kickstart, `pyry update` auto-restart, `install-service`). Dispatcher-side restart-then-wait. Tuning the retry budget after observation (start with 1.5 s / 50 ms; revisit only when a real workload bumps the cap). A "context cancelled mid-loop" test case (no production surface triggers it today — `pyry status -timeout=Xms` style doesn't exist; cancel propagation is correct by inspection of `dialWithRetry`'s body).
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Client dial: transient-startup retry (#198 + #199)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/199-dial-with-retry.md`](specs/architecture/199-dial-with-retry.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #198)
- **`internal/control/dial.go` — `isTransientStartupError(err error) bool` predicate.** New file (~20 LOC including doc comment), one new pure unexported function. No new exported API, no callers — the bounded retry loop that consumes this predicate lands in #199. Body is `errors.Is(err, syscall.ENOENT) || errors.Is(err, syscall.ECONNREFUSED)`. Imports are exactly `errors` + `syscall`; no `net`, `os`, `io`, no `context`, no goroutines.
- **Why `errors.Is` against the leaf `Errno`, not `errors.As(*net.OpError)`.** `errors.Is` walks the full unwrap chain — through `client.go:282`'s `fmt.Errorf("dial %s: %w", socketPath, err)`, through `*net.OpError.Unwrap`, through `*os.PathError.Unwrap` / `*os.SyscallError.Unwrap`, matching at the leaf `syscall.Errno`. The wire-shape (`*net.OpError`) is incidental; the contract is "did the unwrap chain reach one of the two named errnos?" Resisted the urge to add `errors.As(*net.OpError)` plumbing for "shape verification" — that pins the predicate to today's wrapping shape, which is precisely what `errors.Is` is designed to make irrelevant. `errors.Is(nil, sentinel)` returns `false` for any non-nil sentinel, so the nil case falls out for free with no guard.
- **Why the predicate is unexported.** The only intended consumer is the retry wrapper in the same `internal/control` package (#199). Exporting now would be speculative API surface — the public verbs (`Status`, `Attach`, `SessionsList`, etc.) all route through `request` → `dial`; downstream packages neither call `dial` directly nor need to classify dial errors. If a future consumer materialises, lift to exported then.
- **File placement: `internal/control/dial.go`, NOT a refactor that moves the existing `dial()` from `client.go:273-285`.** The architect explicitly scoped this as predicate-only and rejected the "move dial helpers into a sibling file while we're here" cleanup as out-of-scope refactor cascade. `dial.go` will house future dial-related helpers from #199 (the retry wrapper); `dial_test.go` lives there for obvious co-location.
- **Two-errno scope — no `io.EOF`, no timeouts, no protocol errors.** The two transient shapes the daemon-restart race produces: (a) socket file absent (`*net.OpError` ⇢ `*os.PathError{Err: ENOENT}`), (b) socket file present + no listener accepting (`*net.OpError` ⇢ `*os.SyscallError{Err: ECONNREFUSED}`, also covers a stale socket file from a crashed previous daemon). Every other dial outcome means "the daemon answered and something is wrong" — retrying would mask real failures. The misclassification ledger: false negative = client surfaces immediately (today's no-retry behaviour, acceptable); false positive = #199 retries to its bounded budget then surfaces (slower failure, not incorrect).
- **No syscall-shape sentinel test (e.g. `*net.OpError`-pinning).** Architect's call: "don't test that `errors.Is` works (it's stdlib); don't test `*net.OpError` traversal independently (covered transitively by the live-ENOENT row)". The live-ENOENT case is the structural proof that the unwrap chain runs end-to-end against a real kernel error.
- **Tests in `internal/control/dial_test.go`** (~62 LOC, single `TestIsTransientStartupError` with six rows). True cases: (1) **real** `net.Dial("unix", filepath.Join(t.TempDir(), "missing.sock"))` against a never-created path — pins the production-shape unwrap chain end-to-end; (2) synthetic `&net.OpError{Op: "dial", Net: "unix", Err: &os.SyscallError{Syscall: "connect", Err: syscall.ECONNREFUSED}}` — synthetic because live construction via `Listener.Close` differs across macOS (leaves socket file) / Linux (removes socket file) and adds nothing the synthetic shape doesn't cover. False cases: (3) `nil`; (4) `io.EOF` (protocol-level, no syscall in chain); (5) synthetic `*net.OpError` wrapping `context.DeadlineExceeded` (timeout shape); (6) plain `errors.New("kaboom")` (opaque, no unwrap chain — pins no-false-positive on bare strings).
- **Production diff +20 LOC `internal/control/dial.go` (new file). Test diff +62 LOC `internal/control/dial_test.go`** (new file). Zero changes to `client.go`, zero new dependencies, no public API surface, no wire change.
- **Out of scope, by design.** The bounded retry wrapper that consumes this predicate (sister ticket #199 — wires the loop into the dial path with a backoff schedule appropriate for the 100ms–2s daemon-restart window). Server-side ready-signaling (separate consideration). A `pyry wait` UX verb (separate decision). Live-ECONNREFUSED via short-lived listener (flaky cross-OS; synthetic case 2 is the canonical shape). Exporting the predicate (defer until a downstream consumer exists).
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Client dial: transient-startup predicate (#198)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/198-transient-startup-error-predicate.md`](specs/architecture/198-transient-startup-error-predicate.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #190)
- **`cmd/pyry/update.go` — daemon-restart wiring on `pyry update`**, the cap on the `internal/update/restart.go` pure-decision slice (#181) that has been sitting unused since #189 landed. Production diff is +56 LOC inside the existing file (no new files): three new fields on `updateOptions` (`noRestart bool`, `probeRestart func() update.RestartProbe`, `runRestart func(ctx context.Context, argv []string) error`), one new flag on `runUpdate` (`--no-restart`), two new package-private helpers (`defaultProbeRestart` / `defaultRunRestart`), and an eight-line restart block at the end of `doUpdate`. The `==> Updated to <v>.` line moved to be terminal in the happy path so the success line is the very last thing printed (was: immediately after replace).
- **Probe lives inline in `cmd/pyry/update.go`, NOT in `internal/update`.** Boundary established at #181 reaffirmed here: `internal/update/restart.go` stays a pure function (`DetectRestartCommand(probe) → argv`) with no filesystem dependencies; the `os.Stat` calls on `~/Library/LaunchAgents/dev.pyrycode.pyry.plist` and `~/.config/systemd/user/pyry.service` are co-located with the subcommand handler that consumes them. `defaultProbeRestart` stats both paths regardless of `runtime.GOOS` (Linux's launchd plist won't exist anyway → bool false; one extra wasted stat removes a `runtime.GOOS` branch). Stat errors of any kind collapse to "not present"; if `os.UserHomeDir()` fails, both stats fail → `DetectRestartCommand` returns nil → silent skip. See [ADR 015](knowledge/decisions/015-update-restart-probe-inline.md).
- **Restart executor is an injectable function-typed seam on `updateOptions`** mirroring the existing `replace` / `executablePath` pattern. Production default `defaultRunRestart` uses `exec.CommandContext` (so a cancelled `doUpdate` propagates to a slow `launchctl kickstart`) with stdio wired to the real terminal so launchctl/systemctl diagnostics reach the user verbatim. Tests substitute a closure that records argv into a captured slice or returns a sentinel error — no globals, no build tags, one consistent pattern across all `updateOptions` seams.
- **Probe seam separate from executor seam.** Could fold both behind one `restartIfManaged func(ctx) error`; rejected because the progress line `==> Restarting daemon (<manager>: <unit>)...` derives the manager label from the `RestartProbe` directly (rather than string-matching `argv[0]`), and keeping probe + decide + execute as three composable pieces matches the natural decomposition of the work.
- **Manager label tie-break uses the probe, not argv parsing.** `DetectRestartCommand`'s tie-breaker is "launchd wins when both are present"; the wiring reads `probe.SystemdUnitExists && !probe.LaunchdPlistExists` to switch the label to `systemd`, otherwise stays on `launchd`. The decision lives in one place (`internal/update/restart.go`) and the wiring trusts it.
- **Progress-line shape `==> Restarting daemon (launchd: gui/501/dev.pyrycode.pyry)...`** matches the issue body example exactly. The argv's last element is the unit identifier — for launchd it's the domain target; for systemd it's `pyry` (without `.service` suffix). Acceptable as-is per the architect's open-question note.
- **`--no-restart` is a silent skip, not a warning.** Both the no-flag-but-no-unit-detected case and the `--no-restart` case print nothing about restart — only the existing `==> Updated to <v>.` line. Matches the issue body's framing. With `--no-restart` the probe is not even called (cheap optimisation; also avoids a stat on systems where the user explicitly opted out).
- **Restart-failure error message foregrounds "binary replaced".** Wrapped as `update: binary replaced to <v>, but daemon restart failed: <inner>` so under `main()`'s `pyry: <err>` prefix the user sees `pyry: update: binary replaced to v0.9.2, but daemon restart failed: exit status 1`. The new version is on disk; the user retries the restart manually. Single line, exit 1. AC #4 satisfied.
- **`==> Updated to <v>.` is now last in the happy path.** Moved from "immediately after replace" to "after the restart step." Reads "doing the last step → all done" rather than "we're done — oh, and one more thing." If the restart fails, `doUpdate` returns early and the success line never prints, which is correct: a failed restart is partial-success the user must act on.
- **Renamed daemons (`pyry install-service --name elli`) are silently skipped on update.** The probe hardcodes `dev.pyrycode.pyry.plist` / `pyry.service`. A renamed install means no managed unit detected → silent skip → user manually restarts. Known limitation, follow-up ticket if observed.
- **Tests in `cmd/pyry/update_test.go`** (+168 LOC, five new tests). `TestUpdate_RestartLaunchd` (probe `{LaunchdPlistExists: true, UID: "501"}`, asserts argv == `[launchctl kickstart -k gui/501/dev.pyrycode.pyry]` and the `(launchd: ...)` progress line), `TestUpdate_RestartSystemd` (probe `{SystemdUnitExists: true}`, asserts argv == `[systemctl --user restart pyry]` and `systemd:` label), `TestUpdate_NoRestartFlag` (`noRestart: true` plus a probe that *would* match → `runRestart` is `t.Fatalf` sentinel, proves flag short-circuits before probe runs), `TestUpdate_NoManagedUnit` (zero-value `RestartProbe{}` → success line prints, no restart progress, `runRestart` never called), `TestUpdate_RestartFailure` (`runRestart` returns `errors.New("exit status 1")` → asserts wrapped error contains both `binary replaced to v0.9.2` and `daemon restart failed`, and that the success line is NOT in captured output because we returned early). Updates to existing tests: `TestUpdate_Success` and `TestUpdate_PinVersion` reach the replace step and therefore execute the new restart block — both populate `probeRestart: func() update.RestartProbe { return update.RestartProbe{} }` and `runRestart: t.Fatalf` sentinels. The other three (`AlreadyAtLatest`, `CheckOnly`, `DevBuildSkips`) short-circuit before replace and need no changes.
- **Real `defaultProbeRestart` and `defaultRunRestart` are not unit-tested.** Manual smoke test on a Mac with `pyry install-service`-installed daemon covers the production paths. Both are short and well-understood; a tempdir-based `$HOME` rig + fake `launchctl` on `$PATH` would be heavier than the duplication.
- **Production diff: `cmd/pyry/update.go` +56 LOC (existing file). Test diff: `cmd/pyry/update_test.go` +168 LOC.** Zero new dependencies, zero new files in production, zero changes to `internal/update/restart.go` or any other primitive — the architect's "purely the wiring slice" framing held.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Renamed-daemon detection (silent skip is the documented behaviour). Real-`os.Stat` and real-`exec.CommandContext` unit tests (manual smoke test instead). Real-PTY for the executor (stdout/stderr to terminal is fine for one-shot CLI; `launchctl kickstart` and `systemctl restart` don't need a PTY). Concurrent restart (sequential, single-goroutine; `exec.CommandContext` blocks until child exits — intentional, user wants to see the kick complete or fail before pyry's process exits). Retry on restart failure (the user retries `launchctl kickstart` / `systemctl --user restart pyry` manually if they want).
- See [knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md § Daemon-restart wiring (#190)](knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md), [knowledge/decisions/015-update-restart-probe-inline.md](knowledge/decisions/015-update-restart-probe-inline.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/190-update-daemon-restart-wiring.md`](specs/architecture/190-update-daemon-restart-wiring.md), [`docs/guide.md` § Updating pyry](guide.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #189)
- **`cmd/pyry/update.go` — `pyry update` CLI verb wiring**, the cap on the six `internal/update` primitive slices (#179, #180, #181, #182, #186, #187). New file (~159 LOC) plus 2-line dispatch in `cmd/pyry/main.go:165` and a 3-line entry in `printHelp`. The verb-level command composes the primitives in the documented order: print current version → resolve target tag (latest via `Fetcher.FetchLatestRelease` + `ParseLatestRelease`, or `--version <tag>` pin) → `CompareVersions` short-circuit on `Same` / `ErrInvalidVersion` (dev) → `AssetName` + URL-template → `Fetcher.FetchAsset` (tarball + `checksums.txt`) → `ParseChecksumsFile` → `VerifySHA256` → `ExtractBinary` → `AtomicReplace(os.Executable(), bin, 0o755)` → print `==> Updated to <v>.`. Daemon restart deliberately out of scope; `DetectRestartCommand` (#181) is unused by this verb until the follow-up ticket lands.
- **`runUpdate(args []string) error` parses flags (`--check`, `--version <tag>`); `doUpdate(ctx, updateOptions) error` runs the flow.** Splitting them lets the integration tests drive `doUpdate` directly with an `updateOptions` literal (httptest server + tempdir target + capture buffer) without intercepting `flag.Parse` or `os.Stdout`. The `updateOptions` struct bundles four field-level seams the tests need: `Fetcher.BaseURL` (already a Fetcher field), `releaseBaseURL` for the tarball/checksums URL templating, `executablePath` so the test points at `tempdir/pyry` instead of `/usr/local/bin/pyry`, and `out io.Writer` for capturing progress lines. No `init()`, no global vars, no `httptest` import in production code.
- **URL-template the asset URLs (`<base>/<tag>/<asset>`, `<base>/<tag>/checksums.txt`) rather than parsing `assets[*].browser_download_url` from the release JSON.** `ParseLatestRelease` extracts `tag_name` only; expanding the parser would grow #179's surface for no value because the GitHub `releases/download/<tag>/<filename>` scheme is documented stable and matches what `.goreleaser.yaml` produces. The same `.goreleaser.yaml`-coupling caveat that already applies to `AssetName` covers this — both values live in this repo, both move together if GitHub ever changes the scheme. Tests stub `releaseBaseURL` against `srv.URL + "/releases/download"`.
- **`Version == "dev"` short-circuits via `errors.Is(err, update.ErrInvalidVersion)` from `CompareVersions` and prints `==> Running a development build (dev); skipping update.` then returns nil.** Failing with `ErrInvalidVersion` would force every `pyry update` invocation in a development worktree to exit 1, which fights the developer's muscle memory ("I run `pyry update` to refresh"). The skip is the user-friendly path: dev builds came from `go install` or `make build`; replacing them with a release tarball would silently revert the working copy. This consumes the `ErrInvalidVersion` sentinel exactly the way #179's PROJECT-MEMORY entry forecast.
- **Homebrew hint when `os.Executable()` resolves under `/opt/homebrew/`** prints `Hint: this pyry was installed via Homebrew; consider 'brew upgrade pyry' instead.` before the rest of the flow runs. Non-blocking — refusing would block the rare Homebrew user who knowingly wants the GitHub-release version, and a Homebrew install hits `AtomicReplace` cleanly anyway. The hint nudges the user to the right command without forcing pyry to detect-and-refuse.
- **`resolveExecutable()` falls back to `os.Args[0]` if `os.Executable()` errors** (rare; mostly `/proc` unavailability on exotic platforms). Tests bypass the wrapper by overriding `executablePath` in `updateOptions`.
- **Sequential, single-goroutine flow.** No `errgroup`, no parallel fetch of tarball+checksums (would shave ~1s on fast networks but complicates the `==> Downloading <asset>...` progress-line ordering for no observed user benefit). One `context.Background()` from `runUpdate`; tests pass `t.Context()`. Ctrl-C / SIGINT handling deferred — swap to `signal.NotifyContext(ctx, os.Interrupt)` if the need arises. The Fetcher already honours context cancellation per #182's AC.
- **HTTP timeout is 60s via `&http.Client{Timeout: 60 * time.Second}`** baked into the Fetcher in `runUpdate`. Generous for a ~20 MiB tarball on a slow connection but bounded enough that a hung `pyry update` doesn't sit forever. `--http-timeout` flag is YAGNI — users can re-run.
- **`fmt.Fprintf` to `out`, not `slog`.** This is a one-shot CLI verb, not a daemon. Output is human-facing progress lines on stdout, not structured-logging events. `runInstallService` already uses `fmt.Printf` for the same reason — the convention is preserved.
- **Errors propagate as `update: <step>: %w` and are printed by `main()`'s wrapper as `pyry: update: <step>: <inner>` to stderr** (exit 1). Each step contributes its own context prefix: `update: fetch latest release: …`, `update: parse latest release: …`, `update: download tarball: …`, `update: download checksums: …`, `update: parse checksums: …`, `update: verify checksum: …`, `update: extract binary: …`, `update: replace binary: …`. On checksum mismatch the verify-line prints `FAIL` before the wrapped error surfaces. No retry, no fallback — a checksum miss after a clean download is either GitHub serving a corrupt asset or a hostile MITM, and silently retrying masks both.
- **Tests in `cmd/pyry/update_test.go`** (~292 LOC, five integration tests). `TestUpdate_Success` (AC #2 happy path: on-disk binary swapped at `tempdir/pyry`, all six progress lines print verbatim including `==> Updated to v0.9.2.`), `TestUpdate_AlreadyAtLatest` (current==latest short-circuit; injects a `replace` that `t.Fatal`s if called), `TestUpdate_CheckOnly` (AC #3: `--check` prints versions and exits without downloading; injects a `replace` that fails if called), `TestUpdate_PinVersion` (AC #3: `--version <v>` skips the latest-release API call — the fake handler 500s if hit — and downloads from the pinned URL), `TestUpdate_DevBuildSkips` (`currentVersion == "dev"` exits 0 with "skipping update", `replace` not called). Each test stands up its own `httptest.NewServer` with three handlers (`/repos/.../releases/latest`, `/releases/download/<tag>/<asset>`, `/releases/download/<tag>/checksums.txt`); helpers `buildTarGzForTest` + `fakeRelease` + `newFakeReleaseServer` are inline in the test file, not shared with `internal/update/install_test.go` (the duplication is ~10 lines; an `internal/testutil` package would be heavier).
- **Production diff: `cmd/pyry/update.go` +159 LOC (new file). `cmd/pyry/main.go` +2 LOC dispatch + 3 LOC `printHelp`. `docs/guide.md` +1 paragraph "Updating pyry" section.** Test diff: `cmd/pyry/update_test.go` +292 LOC (new file).
- **Out of scope for #189, by design.** Daemon restart (the explicit follow-up ticket — `DetectRestartCommand` from #181 sits unused until then; the user manually `launchctl kickstart -k gui/$(id -u)/dev.pyrycode.pyry` (macOS) or `systemctl --user restart pyry` (Linux), documented in the guide). `--no-restart` flag (lands with the restart follow-up). Rollback / `.bak` of the old binary (deferred entirely; `AtomicReplace`'s crash-safety covers in-progress writes, but undoing a *successful* update is a separate feature — where to store the old binary, how to garbage-collect, how the user invokes it). Scheduled auto-update / channel selection (deferred; only the `latest` GitHub release is consulted, pre-release tags ignored). Ctrl-C / SIGINT handling. Retry on transient network failure (Fetcher's AC forbids it). Exposing the asset list via `pyry update --list`.
- See [knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md](knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md), [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/189-update-subcommand-wiring.md`](specs/architecture/189-update-subcommand-wiring.md), [`docs/guide.md` § Updating pyry](guide.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #187)
- **`internal/update/replace.go` — fourth slice of `pyry update`, the atomic in-place binary replacement primitive.** New file (~64 LOC) in the existing `internal/update` package, alongside #179's `version.go`, #180's `checksum.go`, and #181's `restart.go`. Stdlib-only (`fmt`, `os`, `path/filepath`); first member of the package to perform I/O. The wiring ticket calls this *after* extracting the new pyry binary from the downloaded tarball (#186) and *before* running the `DetectRestartCommand` argv (#181) to kick the daemon. Sister tickets #186 (in-memory tar extraction → produces the `[]byte` input) and #182 (HTTP fetcher) are still in flight; this slice's file-level non-overlap with both lets it land in any order.
- **`AtomicReplace(targetPath string, newData []byte, mode os.FileMode) error`.** Standard POSIX safe-overwrite dance: `os.CreateTemp(filepath.Dir(targetPath), "."+base+".*.tmp")` so the temp file lands in the same directory as the target (eventual `os.Rename` never crosses a mount point — `rename(2)` returns `EXDEV` and degrades to copy-then-unlink across filesystems, not atomic), then **write → fchmod → fsync → close → rename**. SIGKILL anywhere before the rename leaves `targetPath` byte-identical to its pre-call state; SIGKILL after, the new bytes are durable. On Linux a target currently mmap'd for execution is handled cleanly: the rename unlinks the old inode while leaving its open-for-execution refcount intact, so running pyry processes keep their old binary mapped and the on-disk path now points to the new one.
- **Order is `write → fchmod → fsync → close → rename`, not `write → fsync → fchmod → …`.** Chmod-then-fsync ensures the mode change is durably persisted along with the contents in the same fsync; the reverse would leave the mode change un-fsynced — a needless durability gap. `f.Chmod` (fchmod on the open fd) over `os.Chmod(path, …)` avoids a TOCTOU between create and chmod (`os.CreateTemp` opens at 0o600; the requested mode is applied via the open fd before any other process could swap the file underneath us).
- **Each f-method failure closes the file before returning** rather than relying on a single `defer f.Close()`. Ordering with respect to the cleanup `defer` is then unambiguous — the `os.Remove(tmp)` in the cleanup defer always runs after the explicit close. A `renamed` bool gates the cleanup `defer`: after `os.Rename` succeeds, `tmp` no longer names a file; calling `os.Remove(tmp)` would either fail with `ENOENT` (harmless) or, in a freak race, remove an unrelated file some other process subsequently created at the same temp name. The flag closes that gate cheaply.
- **Temp-file naming `"."+base+".*.tmp"` (e.g. `.pyry.123456789.tmp`).** Leading dot keeps stragglers (which only appear in failure modes) hidden from `ls`; embedding `base` makes accidental collisions during concurrent updates structurally impossible and gives ops a hint about origin if one ever does leak. `os.CreateTemp` substitutes a random suffix for `*` (no caller-side counter, no race).
- **Mirrors `internal/sessions/registry.go`'s `saveRegistryLocked` pattern** (the in-tree precedent for atomic file writes) with two deliberate differences: raw bytes instead of a JSON encoder; **no `os.MkdirAll`** on the parent. The wiring ticket guarantees the install directory already exists (it's where `pyry` is currently running from); creating it here would mask a configuration bug in the caller. The "parent missing" error path is tested explicitly to pin this contract.
- **Caller MUST pass a path whose parent directory exists and is writable.** Doc comment names the same-filesystem caveat verbatim because the `CreateTemp(filepath.Dir(targetPath), …)` choice is what makes the rename atomic; a future refactor that "helpfully" moves the temp file to `os.TempDir()` or `~/tmp` would silently break atomicity across the install-dir / `/tmp` mount-point boundary common on Linux.
- **No sentinel errors.** None of the AC's error cases need `errors.Is`-style branching; the wiring ticket will log-and-fail uniformly. `CreateTemp`'s wrapped `*PathError` already lets a future caller introspect with `errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist)` if they ever need to. Adding sentinels speculatively would violate "Don't add ... for scenarios that can't happen".
- **Concurrency.** Reentrant in the formal sense (no package-level state) but two concurrent calls *with the same `targetPath`* race at the rename step: temp names are unique random suffixes from `CreateTemp` (no collision there), but whichever rename runs last wins on `targetPath` and the loser's bytes are silently overwritten. No corruption; lost update only. The `pyry update` flow is single-goroutine in the wiring ticket, so we don't defend against this; the doc comment doesn't promise anything about concurrent calls. No `context.Context` parameter — a single sub-megabyte buffered write isn't meaningfully cancellable, and the wiring ticket can wrap the whole update with its own ctx.
- **Out of scope, by design.** **Parent-directory fsync after the rename.** The crash-durable-rename pattern includes `open(dir, O_RDONLY) + fsync + close` after the rename so the directory entry survives a power loss between rename and the next dirent flush. `saveRegistryLocked` omits it; we omit it; both rest on "process interrupt (signal/SIGKILL)" being the threat model rather than "power loss". If/when a `pyry update` user reports a missing binary after a power outage, revisit. **`os.MkdirAll` on the parent** (configuration-bug exposure, see above). **Backup/rollback of the old binary** as a `.bak` artifact — wiring layer's call (it can `AtomicReplace` to `.bak` first if it wants belt-and-suspenders rollback). **Linux `renameat2(RENAME_NOREPLACE)` for the new-file case** (single-goroutine update flow; not in threat model). **`io.Reader` variant** — today's binary is ~12 MiB and #186 already produces `[]byte`; streaming would force #186 to expose a reader instead, not worth the contract change.
- **Tests in `internal/update/replace_test.go`** (~90 LOC, four targeted subtests using `t.TempDir()` exclusively). `TestAtomicReplace_CreatesNewFile` (target absent), `_OverwritesExistingFile` (target seeded with `0o644` "OLD" → overwrites with `0o755` "NEW"), `_PreservesMode` (request `0o755`, assert `os.Stat().Mode().Perm() == 0o755`), `_ParentDirMissing` (path inside a non-existent subdir → assert error AND `os.ReadDir` of the surrounding tempdir is empty — the "no stray `.pyry.*.tmp` stragglers on the error path" pin). Targeted subtests over a single table because the error case has different setup; mirrors `checksum_test.go`'s style (`t.Parallel()` per subtest, inline assertions, no helpers, no `testdata/`).
- **No umask test.** Asking for `0o755` and asserting `0o755` is robust under any sane umask (`0o022`, `0o002`, `0o077` all preserve the requested 0o755 — wait, `0o077` would mask group/other and produce `0o700`). To stay deterministic across CI environments we'd need `syscall.Umask(0)` + restore in `t.Cleanup`; the AC doesn't demand it and CI runs default umask, so deferred to implementer judgment per the spec. If a maintainer ever runs CI with `0o077` and sees this test fail spuriously, harden then.
- **Production diff +64 LOC `internal/update/replace.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +90 LOC `internal/update/replace_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#187 is the replace primitive only); CLI surface unchanged.
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md § Atomic in-place replace](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/187-update-atomic-replace.md`](specs/architecture/187-update-atomic-replace.md), [`internal/sessions/registry.go`](../internal/sessions/registry.go) for the in-tree precedent, [`lessons.md § Atomic on-disk writes`](lessons.md) for the canonical write-temp + fsync + rename rules.

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #182)
- **`internal/update/fetch.go` — HTTP fetcher slice of `pyry update`.** Stdlib-only `net/http` wrapper exposing one struct (`Fetcher`) and two methods (`FetchLatestRelease(ctx, repo)` + `FetchAsset(ctx, url)`). Sits alongside #179's `version.go` and #180's `checksum.go` in the same `internal/update` package; no package doc comment (lives on `version.go`). The wiring ticket composes it with the pure functions: `Fetcher.FetchLatestRelease` → `ParseLatestRelease` → `CompareVersions` + `AssetName` → `Fetcher.FetchAsset(checksums.txt)` → `ParseChecksumsFile` → `Fetcher.FetchAsset(tarball)` → `VerifySHA256` → `ExtractBinary` → next ticket's atomic-replace.
- **`Fetcher` is a struct with zero-value-usable defaults** (vs a `New(opts) *Fetcher` constructor). Three independently-optional fields: `BaseURL` (default `"https://api.github.com"`), `HTTPClient` (default `http.DefaultClient`), `UserAgent` (default `"pyry/dev"`; the wiring ticket sets `"pyry/" + main.Version`). Same shape as `http.Client` itself. Defaults resolved per-call inside the methods via private helpers (`baseURL` / `httpClient` / `userAgent`) so a caller mutating package-level `http.DefaultClient` after `Fetcher{}` construction is supported. Tests need to override `BaseURL` and `HTTPClient` — direct field assignment is the readable form. No invariants between fields require a constructor.
- **Two methods over one** because the latest-release endpoint needs URL templating (`<BaseURL>/repos/<repo>/releases/latest`) and asset fetches do not (caller passes a fully-formed URL extracted from the release JSON, e.g. `assets[].browser_download_url`). The fetcher cannot template asset URLs — it doesn't know the GoReleaser asset-name conventions and shouldn't. Implementation core (`get` helper: build request → set User-Agent → Do → status check → drain-on-non-2xx → ReadAll) is shared and unexported. `*Fetcher` receivers (not value) so a shared `Fetcher{}` can't be accidentally copied with all-zero fields.
- **`http.NewRequestWithContext` (not `http.NewRequest`).** Propagates `ctx` to the transport so cancellation interrupts an in-flight read, not just a queued send. This is what makes `errors.Is(err, context.Canceled)` fire mid-transfer rather than only at request-construction time. `*url.Error.Unwrap` participates in the unwrap chain transparently — no special handling in the fetcher.
- **Non-2xx error contract: `fmt.Errorf("GET %s: unexpected status %d", url, resp.StatusCode)`** — bare `Errorf`, no `%w`, because there's no inner error to wrap. The AC's "wrapped error containing status code and URL" is satisfied by this single line. **No new exported sentinel.** The wiring ticket cannot retry (forbidden) and therefore cannot branch on transient-vs-permanent — a typed sentinel would be unused. If a future caller needs typed branching, add `ErrUnexpectedStatus` then; defer until observed (Pipeline Principle: Evidence-Based Fix Selection).
- **Drain-then-discard up to 1 KiB on non-2xx** via `io.Copy(io.Discard, io.LimitReader(resp.Body, 1<<10))`. Lets the underlying TCP connection back into the pool; the bound caps reading megabytes of error HTML from a misconfigured server. Errors from the drain are ignored — we already have a status to report. Transport-hygiene optimisation, not correctness; documented in `net/http`.
- **No retries, no caller-imposed timeouts.** Stdlib only. Caller passes `&http.Client{Timeout: 60*time.Second}` if it wants a budget. GitHub's API blanket-rejects no-User-Agent requests, which is why the header is unconditionally set rather than optional. The `pyry/<Version>` shape (vs `pyry/v<Version>`) matches the binary's self-report so log correlation stays grep-friendly.
- **`io.ReadAll` on the response body is acceptable** despite tarballs being 10–30 MiB — the wiring ticket holds the bytes in memory anyway to compute SHA-256 (`VerifySHA256(data []byte, …)`) and feed tar extraction. Streaming would force the wiring layer to either tee or hash twice. Revisit only if profiling shows pressure.
- **Concurrency: stateless across calls, safe for concurrent use.** All fields are read-only after construction; `*http.Client.Do` is concurrency-safe; each call constructs a fresh `*http.Request`. No goroutines, no mutexes, no internal channels in the fetcher itself.
- **Tests in `internal/update/fetch_test.go` (~158 LOC).** Six tests, all `t.Parallel()`, each with its own `httptest.NewServer` + `t.Cleanup(ts.Close)`. `TestFetcher_FetchLatestRelease_OK` (path + User-Agent inbound, body verbatim), `_FetchAsset_OK` (16 bytes binary fixture), `_DefaultUserAgent` (zero-value default `"pyry/dev"`), `_NonOKStatus` (table over 404/500/503; substring assert on status code AND `ts.URL` in error message — the one place substring-match is the right shape per the AC), `_ContextCancelled` (handler blocks until either `release` channel closes or `r.Context().Done()`; `time.AfterFunc(50ms, cancel)` triggers cancellation; assert `errors.Is(err, context.Canceled)`), `_FetchLatestRelease_RepoSlugInPath` (URL templating shape with `owner/different-name`).
- **Production diff +115 LOC `internal/update/fetch.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +158 LOC `internal/update/fetch_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#182 is fetcher only); CLI surface unchanged. Stdlib-only — no new dependencies.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Parsing JSON / checksums.txt (#179, #180 — already merged). Verifying SHA-256 (#180). Tar extraction (#186 — already landed). Atomic on-disk replace. `pyry update` CLI verb wiring. Retries / exponential backoff (AC explicitly forbids). Caller-side timeouts (caller's responsibility via `*http.Client`). `If-None-Match` / ETag-based caching (anonymous 60/hr limit fine for interactive use). `Fetcherer` / `Mockable` interface (tests use `httptest.NewServer` directly; the wiring ticket may add a 2-method consumer-defined interface there if needed). Exposing GitHub 4xx body content in errors (URL is in the message — operators can `curl` it; revisit if real failures generate complaints).
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/182-update-http-fetcher.md`](specs/architecture/182-update-http-fetcher.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #186)
- **`internal/update/install.go` — fourth pure-function slice of `pyry update`.** New file (~63 LOC) in the existing `internal/update` package, alongside #179's `version.go`, #180's `checksum.go`, and #181's `restart.go`. Stdlib-only (`archive/tar`, `bytes`, `compress/gzip`, `errors`, `fmt`, `io`, `path/filepath`); no I/O, no goroutines, no `context.Context`. The wiring ticket consumes this between `VerifySHA256` and the still-pending atomic on-disk replace step.
- **`ExtractBinary(tgzData []byte, binaryName string) ([]byte, error)` reads a gzipped tar archive entirely from memory and returns the bytes of the regular-file entry whose tar header `Name` (under `filepath.Base`) matches `binaryName`.** Memory-only: no temp files, no streaming-to-disk. The function is a pure (input-bytes → output-bytes) transform; callers who need the binary on disk apply the future atomic-replace function to the returned bytes.
- **`filepath.Base(hdr.Name)` matching, not exact-`hdr.Name` equality.** GoReleaser lays files at the archive root (`pyry`, `LICENSE`, `README.md`) but docs and unit templates carry directory prefixes (`docs/INSTALL.md`, `systemd/pyry.service`). `filepath.Base` matching is robust against a future GoReleaser change that wraps everything in a top-level `pyry_v0.9.1/` directory (a common archives layout) without requiring `ExtractBinary` to change. The cost is that a hypothetical archive with a `subdir/pyry` entry would also match — accepted because GoReleaser does not produce such archives, and a stricter exact-`hdr.Name` check would force this slice to be revisited the moment GoReleaser's layout changes.
- **Skips non-regular entries (`hdr.Typeflag != tar.TypeReg`).** `tar.TypeReg` is the only file type GoReleaser emits. Skipping `TypeDir`, `TypeSymlink`, `TypeLink`, etc. defends against a quirky archive that names its top-level directory `pyry/` (which would otherwise be returned as a zero-length "binary"). Cheap check, silent-and-weird failure mode without it. Returns the first matching regular-file entry — a duplicate-name archive is malformed and there is no documented preference.
- **No size cap (`io.LimitReader`), no streaming variant.** Release tarballs are ~10–20 MiB. The wiring ticket already holds `tgzData` in memory for checksum verification (HTTP GET body fully buffered), so streaming in this layer wins nothing. A defensive cap is **not** added — evidence-based-fix call: no malicious archive observed, the operator's update flow is bounded by HTTP content-length and `tgzData`'s in-memory size, and the wiring ticket checksum-verifies before extraction (forecloses the attacker-controlled-tarball path entirely). Revisit only if pyry ever ships a 1 GiB binary.
- **Two new exported sentinel errors for `errors.Is` branching.** `ErrBinaryNotInArchive` (iterated to `io.EOF` without finding a regular-file entry matching `binaryName`) and `ErrMalformedArchive` (gzip-open failure or any `tar.Next` / `io.ReadAll` error). Both wrapped with context at the return site (`fmt.Errorf("opening gzip stream: %w", ErrMalformedArchive)`, `fmt.Errorf("reading tar header: %w", ErrMalformedArchive)`, `fmt.Errorf("looking up %q: %w", binaryName, ErrBinaryNotInArchive)`, `fmt.Errorf("reading %q from tar: %w", binaryName, ErrMalformedArchive)`). No error path returns the sentinel bare — matches `checksum.go`'s convention.
- **Tests in `internal/update/install_test.go`** (~120 LOC, single `t.Parallel` table mirroring `checksum_test.go` shape). Five rows: `binary_present_returned_unchanged` (asserts `bytes.Equal` on the pyry bytes; the fixture also contains `LICENSE` plus a directory-prefixed `docs/INSTALL.md` to demonstrate the `filepath.Base` matcher), `binary_missing` (`ErrBinaryNotInArchive`), `garbage_not_gzip` (plain text, fails at `gzip.NewReader`; `ErrMalformedArchive`), `valid_gzip_garbage_tar` (gzip wrapper around non-tar payload — forces the code path past `gzip.NewReader` so `tar.Next`'s error path is exercised, distinguishing it from the previous case; `ErrMalformedArchive`), `empty_input` (`ErrMalformedArchive`). Two helpers: `buildTarGz(t, map[string][]byte) []byte` constructs an inline tarball via `bytes.Buffer` → `gzip.NewWriter` → `tar.NewWriter`; `gzipOf(t, []byte) []byte` is a one-liner for the gzip-only fixture. No `testdata/` — suite is hermetic.
- **Production diff +63 LOC `internal/update/install.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +119 LOC `internal/update/install_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#186 is extraction-only); CLI surface unchanged.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Atomic on-disk replacement (the wiring ticket lands `os.CreateTemp` + `os.Rename` in `install.go` alongside `ExtractBinary` and consumes its `[]byte` output). HTTP fetcher (sister ticket). Checksum verification (#180, already landed). Restart detection (#181, already landed). `pyry update` CLI verb wiring + `--dry-run` flag (wiring ticket). A streaming-extraction variant (`io.Reader` input or pipe-out output) — defer until tarball size demands it. A defensive size cap on `io.ReadAll(tr)` — defer pending evidence.
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/186-update-extract-binary.md`](specs/architecture/186-update-extract-binary.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #181)
- **`internal/update/restart.go` — third pure-function slice of `pyry update`.** New file (~37 LOC) in the existing `internal/update` package, alongside #179's `version.go` and #180's `checksum.go`. Stdlib-only; no I/O, no goroutines, no `context.Context`, no errors. The wiring ticket calls this after the binary has been swapped to kick the running daemon.
- **`RestartProbe` struct.** Three fields: `LaunchdPlistExists bool` (does `~/Library/LaunchAgents/dev.pyrycode.pyry.plist` exist?), `SystemdUnitExists bool` (does `~/.config/systemd/user/pyry.service` exist?), `UID string` (numeric uid as string, templated into the launchctl `gui/<uid>/dev.pyrycode.pyry` domain). Struct rather than three positional bools so the call site labels each signal and survives signal additions in future tickets (e.g. SMF on illumos, Windows service entry) without breaking existing callers.
- **`DetectRestartCommand(probe RestartProbe) []string` returns the argv (program plus args) of the restart command, or `nil` when no managed daemon is detected.** Two-branch switch, launchd checked first so the tie-breaker falls out naturally: `launchctl kickstart -k gui/<uid>/dev.pyrycode.pyry` (launchd) or `systemctl --user restart pyry` (systemd). The `nil` return is the foreground / unknown case — caller prints "restart your pyry yourself" guidance; not an error because foreground users running `pyry` from a terminal are a supported deployment.
- **Tie-breaker: launchd wins when both probes return true.** Rationale (verbatim in doc comment per AC): macOS is pyrycode's primary daily-driver platform, so a stray systemd user unit on a Mac (e.g. left over from a dotfiles sync) is more likely cruft than the active manager. The reverse case — a launchd plist on Linux — cannot occur because `launchctl` does not exist on Linux; the probe will return false. No `runtime.GOOS` filter inside `DetectRestartCommand`: the probe **is** the OS filter, and filtering by GOOS would re-introduce non-purity (tests would need to set GOOS) and forbid the legitimate "wrong-OS file lying around" case from being deterministic.
- **Why `kickstart -k` over `unload`/`load`.** `kickstart -k` SIGTERMs the running instance and starts a fresh one in a single command. `unload`/`load` would round-trip the plist and race with `KeepAlive=true`. The `-k` flag is the canonical way to tell launchd "restart this label now" per `man launchctl`.
- **Why `systemctl --user restart` over `try-restart` or `reload`.** `restart` is unconditional and matches the user's intent (the binary changed; restart it). `try-restart` would silently no-op if the unit is inactive; `reload` requires `ExecReload=` which the unit file doesn't define.
- **Tests in `internal/update/restart_test.go`** (~48 LOC, single `t.Parallel` table mirroring `checksum_test.go` shape). Four rows from the AC: `launchd_only` (`UID: "501"` → `gui/501/dev.pyrycode.pyry`), `systemd_only` (no UID needed), `both_present_launchd_wins` (`UID: "1000"` so the hard-coded `"501"` from the first row would fail this case — UID-templating verification falls naturally out of the differing UIDs), `neither_present` (`nil`). Compares with `slices.Equal` (Go 1.21+, idiomatic for `[]string`); `nil` and `[]string{}` are equal under it but the implementation returns `nil` matching the AC.
- **Production diff +37 LOC `internal/update/restart.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +48 LOC `internal/update/restart_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#181 is restart-detect only); CLI surface unchanged.
- **Out of scope, by design.** The probe half (the wiring ticket performs `os.Stat` on the launchd plist + systemd unit file paths and `os.Getuid()`, then calls `DetectRestartCommand` with the results). Actually running the restart argv (`exec.Command`) and watching for restart success. HTTP fetcher, tar extraction, atomic binary replacement (sister tickets). `pyry update` CLI verb wiring + `--dry-run` flag (wiring ticket).
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/181-update-restart-detect.md`](specs/architecture/181-update-restart-detect.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #180)
- **`internal/update/checksum.go` — second pure-function slice of `pyry update`.** Three new exported functions plus four new sentinel errors, all stdlib-only (`crypto/sha256`, `encoding/hex`, `errors`, `fmt`, `strings`); no I/O, no goroutines, no `context.Context`. Sits alongside #179's `version.go` in the same `internal/update` package — package doc comment on `version.go` already forward-stated this ticket, so `checksum.go` adds none. The wiring ticket consumes #179 + #180 together (`ParseLatestRelease` → `CompareVersions` → `AssetName` → fetch → `ParseChecksumsFile` → fetch tarball → `VerifySHA256` → next ticket's untar + atomic-replace).
- **`AssetName(version, goos, goarch string) (string, error)`** mirrors `.goreleaser.yaml`'s `archives.name_template` verbatim. Returns `pyry_<X.Y.Z>_<Darwin|Linux>_<arm64|x86_64>.tar.gz`; strips a leading `v` via `TrimPrefix` (no-op when absent). Two package-level lookup tables: `osTitles = {"linux":"Linux","darwin":"Darwin"}`, `archNames = {"amd64":"x86_64","arm64":"arm64"}`. Any other os/arch combo wraps `ErrUnsupportedPlatform` — both unsupported-OS and unsupported-arch use the same sentinel; the error message names the inputs (`"asset name for windows/amd64: …"`) so logs are unambiguous, but `errors.Is(err, ErrUnsupportedPlatform)` is the single branch. Does **not** validate that `version` parses as semver — that's `CompareVersions`'s job upstream; double-validating would create two error contracts to keep in sync. Empty `version` is permitted (produces `pyry__Darwin_arm64.tar.gz`), since the wiring ticket guarantees `version` has already passed `CompareVersions`; a stray empty would surface as a 404 from the HTTP fetcher.
- **`ParseChecksumsFile(text, assetName string) (string, error)`** parses GoReleaser-produced `checksums.txt` (one line per asset: `<sha256-hex>  <filename>`, two spaces, matching `sha256sum` output). Returns the lowercase hex digest for the matching asset. `strings.SplitN(line, "  ", 2)` so future filenames containing single spaces survive; per-line `TrimRight(line, "\r")` defensively handles CRLF. Lines that don't split into exactly two non-empty parts are skipped silently — forward-compatible with future header comments or trailing blanks. The `sawAny` flag distinguishes "checksums.txt was junk" (`ErrMalformedChecksums` — upstream broken) from "checksums.txt was a valid file but didn't list our asset" (`ErrAssetNotInChecksums` — built without our platform, unrecoverable for this host). Different sentinels because they imply different upstream actions. Per-line digest length / hex-ness is **not** validated — `VerifySHA256` will catch any mangling, and a regex check would couple two layers without observed benefit.
- **`VerifySHA256(data []byte, expectedHex string) error`** computes `sha256.Sum256(data)`, hex-encodes via `hex.EncodeToString(sum[:])`, compares with `strings.EqualFold` (so a future caller passing mixed-case `expectedHex` works — `ParseChecksumsFile` already lowercases). Mismatch error message normalises both digests to lowercase so logs are consistent regardless of input casing: `"expected %s, got %s: %w"`. Takes `[]byte` rather than `io.Reader` because the wiring ticket already needs the full tarball in memory for tar extraction (release tarballs are <10 MiB); switching to streaming would force the wiring ticket to either tee the body or hash twice. Revisit only if tarball size ever demands it.
- **Four new exported sentinel errors for `errors.Is` branching.** `ErrUnsupportedPlatform` (any os/arch combo not in `.goreleaser.yaml`'s build matrix), `ErrAssetNotInChecksums` (asset not listed in checksums body — built without our platform), `ErrMalformedChecksums` (empty input or no parseable lines at all — upstream broken), `ErrChecksumMismatch` (digest mismatch). All wrapped with context at the return site (`fmt.Errorf("looking up %q: %w", assetName, ErrAssetNotInChecksums)`, etc.).
- **`AssetName` returning `""` and `ParseChecksumsFile` returning `""` on error are conventional** — callers must check the error first; the value is meaningless when err != nil. Same bias as `CompareVersions` returning `Same` on error: a misuse silently routes through "no match" rather than a wrong match.
- **GoReleaser-template coupling is intentionally fragile.** The `osTitles` / `archNames` maps and the `pyry_<v>_<OS>_<arch>.tar.gz` skeleton duplicate `.goreleaser.yaml:24-46`. We own both files in the same repo; `pyry update` only ever reads releases produced by this repo's own `release.yml` workflow — no upstream-consumer compatibility concern. If `.goreleaser.yaml` changes, `checksum.go` changes. No CI drift-check today; deferred follow-up could run `goreleaser release --snapshot` and grep filenames against `AssetName`'s output.
- **Tests in `internal/update/checksum_test.go`** (~219 LOC, three `t.Parallel` tables). 9 `TestAssetName` rows (all four supported os/arch combos, leading-`v` no-op, four unsupported combos: `windows/amd64`, `freebsd/amd64`, `linux/386`, `linux/riscv64`). 8 `TestParseChecksumsFile` rows (asset present first/last, asset missing, empty input, whitespace-only, no parseable lines, CRLF normalised, uppercase-hex normalised, garbage-then-valid). 6 `TestVerifySHA256` rows (empty-data correct hash `e3b0c442…b855`, nonempty correct, mismatch, mismatch-message-includes-both-digests substring assertion, case-insensitive match, empty `expectedHex` rejects). All sentinel-error rows assert via `errors.Is(err, sentinel)`. `t.Parallel()` at outer + subtest level (no shared state — package-level maps are read-only post-init).
- **Production diff +102 LOC `internal/update/checksum.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +219 LOC `internal/update/checksum_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#180 is asset-name + checksum-parser + verifier only); CLI surface unchanged.
- **Out of scope, by design.** HTTP fetcher (sister ticket — GET `releases/latest`, GET `<release>/checksums.txt`, GET `<release>/<assetName>`, retries, timeouts, takes `context.Context`). Tar extraction (separate ticket). Atomic binary replacement / restart detection (separate ticket). `pyry update` CLI verb wiring (wiring ticket). A `MapHostPlatform()` helper wrapping `runtime.GOOS`/`runtime.GOARCH` (the wiring ticket can pass the raw runtime constants — adding a host-detection helper before the wiring ticket exists is YAGNI). Streaming-hash variant of `VerifySHA256` (defer until tarball size demands it). CI drift-check between `AssetName` and `.goreleaser.yaml` (deferred follow-up).
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/180-update-checksum.md`](specs/architecture/180-update-checksum.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #179)
- **`internal/update` — pure-function half of `pyry update`.** First slice of self-update wiring: `ParseLatestRelease(jsonBytes []byte) (string, error)` extracts `tag_name` from a GitHub Releases API JSON payload; `CompareVersions(current, latest string) (Comparison, error)` returns `Older`/`Same`/`Newer`. Stdlib-only (`encoding/json`, `strconv`, `strings`); no I/O, no goroutines, no `context.Context`. Safe for concurrent use by definition. Sister tickets land the HTTP fetcher, checksum verification, and binary replacer; the wiring ticket adds the `pyry update` CLI verb and consumes both functions.
- **`Comparison` is `int`-typed `-1`/`0`/`1`** mirroring `cmp.Compare` / `strings.Compare`. No `String()` method (YAGNI per architect's spec; add when a caller needs `slog`-friendly formatting).
- **Two exported sentinel errors for `errors.Is` branching.** `ErrMalformedRelease` (invalid JSON, non-object top-level, missing/empty/non-string `tag_name`) and `ErrInvalidVersion` (non-semver input, including the `main.Version == "dev"` sentinel). Both wrapped with context at the return site (`fmt.Errorf("decoding release JSON: %w", ErrMalformedRelease)`). On error, `CompareVersions` returns `Same` rather than `Older`/`Newer` — the safer bias when a caller forgets to check the error: silently reports "no update needed" rather than spurious downgrade.
- **Tag preserved verbatim by the parser; comparator does the stripping.** `ParseLatestRelease` returns whatever string GitHub put in `tag_name` (leading `v`, whitespace, pre-release suffixes flow through unchanged). `CompareVersions` strips a leading `v` via `TrimPrefix` (no-op when absent — handles `"v0.9.1"` and `"0.9.1"` symmetrically) and strips pre-release / build-metadata suffixes at the first `-` or `+` before the dot split. Deliberate simplification: pyry's tags are plain `major.minor.patch` and the comparator does not implement SemVer 2.0.0 pre-release precedence — `v0.10.0-rc1 == v0.10.0` after suffix strip. Document in the doc comment so reviewers see the deferred behaviour; revisit only when pyry actually publishes a pre-release operators must distinguish.
- **Default `encoding/json` decoder, NOT `DisallowUnknownFields`.** GitHub's payload has dozens of fields we don't read; strict decoding would convert "GitHub adds a field" into a load failure. Same convention as `sessions.json` (`lessons.md § Atomic on-disk writes`). Whitespace in `tag_name` is **not** trimmed — that's GitHub's own value, never operator-typed; trimming would mask a real upstream bug.
- **`"dev"` is documented as out-of-band.** `cmd/pyry/main.go:53`'s `var Version = "dev"` produces `ErrInvalidVersion` when passed through `CompareVersions`; the wiring ticket will branch on this with `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidVersion)` and print "running a dev build, skipping update check" or similar. Empty-string, too-few-components (`v0.9`), too-many (`v0.9.1.2`), non-numeric components, empty components (`v0..1`), and negative components (`v-1.0.0`) all reject identically. Negatives are explicitly rejected via post-`Atoi` `< 0` check (Atoi *will* parse `-1`); leading zeros (`v01.02.03`) are accepted — SemVer 2.0.0 forbids them, we don't care because GitHub never produces them.
- **Tests** in `internal/update/version_test.go` (~155 LOC, two `t.Parallel` tables). 13 `TestParseLatestRelease` rows cover the happy path + every reject branch (malformed/truncated JSON, non-object top level, missing/empty/null/wrong-type `tag_name`, empty input, extra fields tolerated, `v` prefix preserved verbatim, prerelease tag preserved verbatim). 20 `TestCompareVersions` rows cover all three results across major/minor/patch boundaries (numeric not lexical: `v0.10.0 > v0.9.99`), `v` prefix tolerance on either side or both, prerelease + build-metadata suffix stripping, and every reject branch. Both error tables assert via `errors.Is(err, sentinel)`. `t.Parallel()` at outer + subtest level (no shared state).
- **Production diff +127 LOC `internal/update/version.go` (new package + new file). Test diff +155 LOC `internal/update/version_test.go`.** Zero new callers (#179 is parser + comparator only); CLI surface unchanged.
- **Out of scope, by design.** HTTP fetcher (sister ticket — GET `releases/latest`, retries, timeouts, takes `context.Context`). Checksum verification of the downloaded binary (separate ticket). Atomic binary replacement / restart detection (separate ticket). `pyry update` CLI verb wiring + `--dry-run` flag (wiring ticket). `Comparison.String()` (defer until `slog` consumer needs it). SemVer 2.0.0 pre-release precedence (defer until pyry ships a real pre-release).
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/179-update-version-parsing.md`](specs/architecture/179-update-version-parsing.md).

### Codebase (0.x polish, ticket #177)
- **`pyry install-service` defaults `WorkingDirectory` to the install-time cwd, with `--workdir` (now `~`-expanding) as the explicit override.** Replaces the previous hardcoded `~/pyry-workspace` (launchd) / `%h/pyry-workspace` (systemd). Surfaced 2026-05-08 setting up the Mac Claudian daemon: running install-service from the Obsidian vault root wrote a plist pointing at `~/pyry-workspace`, which doesn't exist on the Mac; `launchctl load` reported success but the daemon's `chdir` failed (exit 78) and the socket was never bound. Cwd default matches `pyry start`'s mental model ("set up the daemon HERE") and removes the silent-pre-create footnote.
- **New exported helper `install.ResolveWorkDir(flag, cwd, homeDir) (string, error)`.** Sole resolver: empty flag → cwd; `~` / `~/sub` → expand against `homeDir`; absolute path → `filepath.Clean`; relative path → `filepath.Abs` (resolves against the test process's cwd). Always returns an absolute path. The CLI is the only caller; the previous `Options.WorkDir == ""` default branch in `install.Install` is removed — passing an empty `WorkDir` to `Install` now leaves the unit's `WorkingDirectory` blank (programming error). Tests that previously relied on the implicit default now pass an explicit value.
- **CLI prints `WorkingDirectory: <resolved-path>` before any file I/O, above the existing "Inherited PATH" block.** Surfaces the effective value to the user even if `install.Install` errors. If the resolved directory does not exist on disk (`errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist)` on `os.Stat`), prints `warning: <path> does not exist; create it with: mkdir -p <path>` and continues — does NOT abort. Other Stat errors (EACCES, etc.) are silently ignored: the daemon's own runtime error will be clearer than a guess at install time.
- **Symlinks in cwd are baked verbatim.** `os.Getwd()` returns whatever the kernel reports, which may include or exclude symlinks depending on how the shell got there. Users who want the canonical path pass `--workdir "$(pwd -P)"` explicitly.
- **Out of scope.** Migrating already-installed `~/pyry-workspace`-pointing plists / unit files (separate PR or manual edit). Auto-creating the WorkingDirectory if missing (warning is enough; users may want specific perms). Multi-instance installer (`--name claudian` for a second pyry alongside the default). Foreground-mode (`pyry start`) cwd handling — already uses cwd, no change.
- **Production diff ~24 LOC `cmd/pyry/main.go` + ~38 LOC `internal/install/install.go`. Test diff +93 LOC `internal/install/install_test.go`** (`TestResolveWorkDir` table + `TestInstall_Systemd_CwdWorkDir` + `TestInstall_Launchd_CwdWorkDir`; existing `TestInstall_Systemd_BareTemplate` / `TestInstall_Launchd_BareTemplate` updated to pass explicit `WorkDir`).
- See [`docs/specs/architecture/177-install-service-cwd-workdir.md`](specs/architecture/177-install-service-cwd-workdir.md), [`docs/deployment.md`](deployment.md) (flag table + macOS section).

### Codebase (Phase 0)
- **Supervisor core** — PTY spawn via `creack/pty`, raw-mode stdin/stdout bridging in foreground mode, Bridge-mediated I/O in service mode, exponential backoff restart with stability reset, `--continue` injection on restart for session persistence
- **SIGWINCH forwarding** — terminal resizes propagate from controlling terminal to child PTY in foreground mode (`internal/supervisor/winsize.go`) and in service mode via the live-resize loop landed across #136 (`Bridge.Resize` seam) + #137 (`VerbResize` wire + server applier) + #133 (client-side `startWinsizeWatcher` in `pyry attach`)
- **Control plane** — Unix domain socket (`~/.pyry/<name>.sock`, 0600), line-delimited JSON protocol, verbs: `status`, `stop`, `logs`, `attach`
- **CLI transparency** — unknown args forward verbatim to claude; pyry's own flags use `-pyry-*` prefix; `-pyry-name` plus `PYRY_NAME` env var for named multi-instance
- **Graceful shutdown** — SIGINT/SIGTERM cancel the supervisor context, child is killed via `exec.CommandContext`, socket removed on exit
- **Service configs** — systemd user unit (`systemd/pyry.service`), macOS launchd plist (`launchd/dev.pyrycode.pyry.plist`)
- **~1700 source + ~1100 test Go lines** as of late Apr 2026, 10+ PRs merged

### Codebase (Phase 1.3c-2, ticket #158)
- **Foreground `pyry --session-id <uuid>` auto-attaches to a daemon-hosted session via stdio when the daemon hosts that UUID.** Closes the "point Claudian at pyry" loop: setting Claudian's "claude binary path" UI to `~/.local/bin/pyry` now Just Works against a running daemon, without a wrapper script and without socket-name management. The auto-attach branch is byte-identical on the wire to `pyry attach --stdio <uuid>` — same `control.AttachStdio` call, same `os.Stdin`/`os.Stdout` wiring, same `createIfMissing=false` (existence already proved via has-id), same `context.Background()`, no human-affordance stderr lines.
- **Two private helpers in `cmd/pyry/main.go`: `extractSessionID(claudeArgs)` + `tryAutoAttach(socketPath, claudeArgs)`.** No new exported surface, no new packages, no wire changes. `extractSessionID` peeks `claudeArgs` (already split out by `splitArgs` — `--session-id` is unambiguously a claude flag) for the four shapes claude itself accepts: `--session-id <v>`, `--session-id=<v>`, `-session-id <v>`, `-session-id=<v>`. First match wins; last-arg-without-value returns `""`; UUID validation is the daemon's job. `tryAutoAttach` is the foreground gate, called from `runSupervisor` after `socketPath` is resolved and before any supervisor-mode side effect (logger, ring buffer, Bridge, Pool init).
- **Conservative posture — every probe failure mode falls through.** Returns `(false, nil)` for: `PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH=1` in the env (strict equality with `"1"`, matches `GODEBUG`/`GOTRACEBACK` convention); no `--session-id` in claudeArgs; `os.Stat(socket)` returns ENOENT or any other error (EACCES, EPERM, …); dial timeout / unresponsive daemon (1s probe ctx); `SessionsHasID` returns `(_, err)` for any reason; `SessionsHasID` returns `(false, nil)`. Returns `(true, err)` only when has-id said yes — `err` is the `AttachStdio` result (nil for clean EOF detach, transport / handshake error otherwise). Existing pyry users (no daemon, or no `--session-id`) see no behavioural change.
- **AC#3 (<50ms in the no-daemon case) satisfied structurally.** `os.Stat`'s ENOENT branch returns before any dial / context allocation / goroutine. Real numbers are sub-millisecond; the 50ms ceiling is the AC contract, not the steady-state expectation. Pinned by `TestTryAutoAttach_SocketAbsent_FastPath` and `TestTryAutoAttach_NoSessionID` (both wall-clock-bounded).
- **`PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH=1` escape hatch.** First check inside `tryAutoAttach`, before `extractSessionID`, before any syscall. Strict-`"1"` semantics (env=`"true"` still probes — pinned by `TestTryAutoAttach_EnvOptOutNonOne`). Used by the e2e tests in #163/#164 that need to assert "supervised spawn fired" without first having to confirm the daemon is down, and as a debug knob for operators pinning a regression to the supervised path. No flag — env var only, matches `PYRY_NAME` precedent.
- **Reuses the existing daemon-name resolution chain (`-pyry-name` flag → `PYRY_NAME` env → `DefaultName`) verbatim.** AC's "use the same resolution chain" is load-bearing for "point Claudian at pyry" with `PYRY_NAME` set — a multi-instance setup where the operator runs separate daemons per project should auto-attach against the right one. `resolveSocketPath` is called once in `runSupervisor`; both auto-attach and supervised-spawn branches consume its result.
- **Why splice in `runSupervisor`, not `run()`.** `run()`'s top-level verb-switch dispatches on a closed set (`version`, `status`, `stop`, `logs`, `attach`, `sessions`, `install-service`, `help`, `-v`, `--version`, `-h`, `--help`); none can ever be `--session-id`. Splicing inside `runSupervisor` reuses the existing `splitArgs` + `resolveSocketPath` parse for free; splicing in `run()` would force a duplicate flag parse for socket resolution.
- **Concurrency: strictly sequential probe.** stat → dial → encode → decode → branch. No new goroutines beyond what `AttachStdio` already spawns internally (one output-copy goroutine, joined before return — see #154's spec). No new lock-order edges. Signal handling is unchanged: when we fall through, the existing `signal.NotifyContext(SIGINT, SIGTERM)` setup applies; when we attach, kernel delivers the signal to pyry's pid → `io.Copy` returns → `AttachStdio` propagates → `runSupervisor` returns → `main` wraps and exits.
- **Tests in `cmd/pyry/auto_attach_test.go` (~230 LOC).** `TestExtractSessionID` (table — 12 rows: all four flag shapes, absent, no-args, last-arg-no-value, empty-value, empty-glued-value, value-with-dashes, first-match-wins, embedded-in-args). `TestTryAutoAttach_*` exercises every fall-through arm: no-session-id (wall-clock budget pin), env opt-out under `=1`, env opt-out non-`1` value still probes, socket absent fast path (50ms budget), daemon unresponsive (listen but never accept; returns within 1.5s via the 1s probe ctx), has-id false, has-id invalid (server returns `Response.Error`). Stub server is a tiny in-test Unix-socket accept loop that decodes one Request and writes back a canned Response — no full server harness, no `internal/control` test helper extraction (the architect's preferred shape per the design doc). The attach-commit branch (has-id true → `AttachStdio` runs) is intentionally **not** unit-tested; e2e is split into siblings #163 (happy path) and #164 (fallback scenarios).
- **Production diff ~75 LOC in `cmd/pyry/main.go`** (~20 for `extractSessionID` + ~50 for `tryAutoAttach` + ~5 for the splice block). Test diff ~230 LOC (`cmd/pyry/auto_attach_test.go` new).
- **Out of scope, by design.** WS / remote attach (Phase 3 + 5 — auto-attach is local-Unix-socket only). Multi-daemon-name discovery (always single resolved name via the existing chain). A `--no-auto-attach` flag on pyry itself (env var covers the bypass case). E2E tests of the full auto-attach flow (#163 happy path, #164 fallback). Logging from the auto-attach path (foreground binary has no logger configured at the splice point; `PYRY_VERBOSE=1` could opt-in via a future ticket if a real operator asks). Telemetry counter for "auto-attach fired" — not on any observability surface today.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Foreground binary auto-attach (1.3c-2)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/158-foreground-auto-attach.md`](specs/architecture/158-foreground-auto-attach.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3c-2-e2e-happy, ticket #163)
- **`internal/e2e/auto_attach.go` + `auto_attach_happy_test.go` — e2e proof that `pyry --session-id <uuid>` (no `attach` verb) auto-attaches to a daemon-hosted session.** Sibling to #161's `StdioAttachClient`, mirrors the surface (`Write` / `ReadUntil` / `Close`). Test `TestE2E_ForegroundAutoAttach_AttachesWhenDaemonHasSession` writes a nonce-tagged line into the foreground pyry's stdin pipe, asserts the same line round-trips back through control socket → bridge → supervisor PTY → echo helper → foreground stdout pipe within 5s, **then** asserts the foreground pyry has zero direct children via `pgrep -P <pid>`. The pgrep assertion is the orthogonal check — a bug that wired auto-attach correctly *and* spawned a competing supervisor would still echo bytes (the daemon's helper returns them regardless of the foreground pid's children).
- **Argv shape is the *foreground binary* invocation, not `pyry attach --stdio`.** `pyry -pyry-socket=<sock> -- --session-id <uuid> --input-format stream-json --output-format stream-json` — no `attach` verb. `os.Args[1]` is `-pyry-socket=…`, doesn't match any verb in `run()`'s switch, so `runSupervisor(os.Args[1:])` runs and `tryAutoAttach` fires. The `--input-format`/`--output-format` flags are functionally inert (auto-attach short-circuits before any claude binary is consulted) but mirror Claudian's invocation literal so the test pins intent. The `--` separator is defensive — `splitArgs` already tips into claudeArgs at the first non-pyry flag, but `--` is forward-compatible if pyry ever adds a flag whose name overlaps.
- **#167 doesn't reach this code path.** `tryAutoAttach` calls `control.AttachStdio` *directly* from inside `runSupervisor` — no verb dispatch, no `parseClientFlags`, no `parseAttachArgs`. The `pyry attach --stdio` CLI bug (#167) blocks #161's `TestE2E_AttachStdio_BytesRoundTrip` but not this test. Confirmed against `cmd/pyry/main.go:304` (the in-process `control.AttachStdio` call).
- **`pgrepChildren(pid) ([]int, error)` is the test-side process-tree primitive — also reused by sibling #164.** `pgrep -P <pid>` is one syscall and one parse, identical surface on linux + darwin (no GOOS branch needed). Exit 1 with empty stdout means "no children" → returns `(nil, nil)` (success path for #163; failure path for #164's fallback tests). `exec.LookPath("pgrep")` failure → returns an error the caller turns into `t.Skip` (matches the precedent in `openPTYDeviceTargetsDarwin` for `lsof`). Kept in `auto_attach.go` rather than `harness.go` — co-location with the feature follows the `attach_pty.go` / `attach_stdio.go` precedent, and the architect's spec marks the "add to `harness.go` once" hint as non-binding.
- **`spawnAutoAttachDaemon` is a slim variant of `spawnAttachableDaemon`, not a verbatim reuse.** Reason: `Pool.Create` appends `--session-id <uuid>` to the supervised claude's argv on every non-bootstrap session (`internal/sessions/pool.go:852`). The Go test binary's `flag.Parse()` rejects `-session-id` and exits 2 before `TestHelperProcess` runs — `SessionsNew` produces a dead session that can't echo bytes. Workaround: a `<home>/echo-claude.sh` shell wrapper that ignores its argv and `exec`s the test binary with fixed args (`-test.run=TestHelperProcess`), mirroring `cap_test.go`'s `writeSleepClaude` pattern. Helper-mode env vars (`GO_TEST_HELPER_PROCESS`, `GO_TEST_HELPER_MODE`) and `E2E_HELPER_BIN` are preserved across the shell exec. The existing `#161` stdio harness has the same latent bug (its skipped test will fail the same way once #167 lands and the skip lifts) — left untouched here per scope discipline; resolve in #167's ticket or a follow-up.
- **`safeBuffer` (mutex-wrapped `bytes.Buffer`) for the foreground pyry's `Stderr` field.** `cmd.Stderr = &bytes.Buffer{}` races with test-goroutine reads of `.String()` because os/exec's stderr-copy goroutine writes the buffer concurrently. The race is real on `-race` even when the buffer is empty in steady state. `StdioAttachClient.Stderr` has the same latent race but is only exercised through a `t.Skip`'d test today — not refactored here per scope discipline. Two methods: `Write` (forwards under lock), `String` (snapshot under lock).
- **Test diff ~365 LOC across 2 new files** (`auto_attach.go` ~290, `auto_attach_happy_test.go` ~50). Production diff is zero. Default `go test -race ./...` unaffected; `go test -tags e2e -race ./internal/e2e/` clean.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Foreground binary auto-attach (1.3c-2)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/163-e2e-foreground-auto-attach-happy.md`](specs/architecture/163-e2e-foreground-auto-attach-happy.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3c-2-e2e-fallback, ticket #164)
- **`internal/e2e/auto_attach_fallback_test.go` + helpers in `auto_attach.go` — three e2e tests pinning `tryAutoAttach`'s fall-through arms.** Sibling to #163's happy-path test, inverse direction. `TestE2E_ForegroundAutoAttach_FallsThroughWhenSessionMissing` (daemon up, UUID not registered), `_FallsThroughWhenNoDaemon` (no daemon, no socket), `_RespectsEnvOverride` (daemon up, UUID registered, `PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH=1` in foreground env). Each asserts `pgrepChildren(c.Pid) ≥ 1` (supervised claude child exists, the inverse of #163's zero-children assertion); the daemon-running tests also snapshot `control.SessionsList` before/after the foreground run and assert byte-equivalent equality (`time.Time.Equal` for `LastActive` to absorb the JSON-roundtrip monotonic-clock strip).
- **All three tests fall through via the same gate (`os.Stat(socketPath) → ENOENT`) by design.** The forced architectural choice: after fall-through, `runSupervisor` runs `ctrl.Listen()` on `socketPath` *before* `pool.Run` spawns the supervised child. If the foreground binary shared the daemon's socket (so its `tryAutoAttach` probe really hit `SessionsHasID == false` for test #1, or skipped a probe that *would* have succeeded for test #3), `Listen` would return `bind: address already in use` and the foreground would exit before any claude child appeared — the pgrep-≥1 assertion couldn't fire. So the foreground gets its **own** socket path, distinct from any daemon's; its socket doesn't exist before its own `Listen` runs, so `tryAutoAttach`'s `os.Stat` returns ENOENT and `tryAutoAttach` falls through. The test environment differentiates (daemon present / env var set / UUID registered) but the gate exercised is always ENOENT. Adding a foreground-only `-pyry-no-listen` flag (or splitting probe-bind paths) to exercise the real `has-id-false` gate at e2e is out of scope for #164 — gate-discrimination is the unit-tier contract (six tests in `cmd/pyry/auto_attach_test.go` shipped with #158: `TestTryAutoAttach_NoSessionID`, `_EnvOptOut`, `_SocketAbsent_FastPath`, `_DaemonUnresponsive`, `_HasIDFalse`, `_HasIDInvalid`); e2e pins the orthogonal contract that fall-through, however triggered, lands the foreground in supervisor mode with a real claude child.
- **New helpers in `auto_attach.go` (additive, +199 LOC).** `ForegroundSupervisedClient` is the simpler inverse-direction sibling of `ForegroundAutoAttachClient` — no bidirectional pipes (`cmd.Stdin = /dev/null`, `cmd.Stdout = io.Discard`), only `Pid` (for `pgrepChildren`) + `Stderr` (`safeBuffer`, expected non-empty in steady state because supervisor mode emits slog lines) + `SocketPath`/`HomeDir` (diagnostics). `startForegroundSupervised(t, sessionID, extraEnv)` argv: `pyry -pyry-socket=<own-sock> -pyry-claude=<sleep-claude> -pyry-idle-timeout=0 -pyry-resume=false -- --session-id <uuid>`. Two-phase readiness — 500ms settle window (early-death detector mirroring `startForegroundAutoAttach`) + `awaitClaudeChild(pid, 5s)` polling `pgrepChildren` every 50ms (closes the race where pgrep outruns the supervisor's first `os.StartProcess` inside `Pool.Run`). `spawnDaemonWithRegisteredSession(t, label) (socket, sessionID)` wraps `spawnAutoAttachDaemon` + `waitDaemonReady` + `control.SessionsNew` for the "daemon present" tests, returning the registered id so tests can confirm the registry-unchanged invariant. Skip-on-`pgrep`-unavailability up front (sandboxed CI). Inline test helpers `mustSessionsList` / `sessionsEqual` / `newCanonicalUUID` (~25 LOC) live in the test file rather than a shared file — three tests of byte-similar duplication, no ongoing churn.
- **Sleep-claude over echo-claude for the supervised stand-in.** Reuses `writeSleepClaude` from `cap_test.go` (#116) — `#!/bin/sh\nexec sleep 99999\n` ignores the `--session-id <uuid>` that `Pool.Create` appends. The happy-path test (#163) needed echo-claude because it round-trips bytes; the fallback tests don't, and `sleep` is the simpler stand-in. Both wrappers exist for the same `Pool.Create`-appends-`--session-id` reason — see `lessons.md`.
- **`extraEnv` parameter is the env-override surface.** `extraEnv` is appended verbatim to `childEnv(home)` before exec, so test #3 injects `PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH=1` into the foreground process's env without polluting any daemon's env. `nil` for tests #1 and #2.
- **Stale-socket-file scenario (AC bullet #2 marks optional) deliberately skipped.** `TestTryAutoAttach_DaemonUnresponsive` already pins the "socket file present, dial fails" gate at unit tier; arranging the e2e fixture (manually create a socket file with no listener, hope `os.Stat` succeeds and `net.Dial` fails) would add complexity for a path the unit test already pins.
- **Cleanup ordering — LIFO via `t.Cleanup`.** Foreground tears down first (close stdin sink → `killSpawned` foreground → `os.Remove(c.SocketPath)`); SIGTERM to the foreground reaps the supervised sleep-claude child via the foreground's process group ownership through `exec.CommandContext` semantics inside the supervisor. Daemon teardown follows on tests #1 and #3.
- **Production diff is zero.** Test diff +342 LOC across 2 files: `auto_attach.go` (+199 additive) + `auto_attach_fallback_test.go` (+143 new). Default `go test ./...` unaffected; `go test -tags e2e -race ./internal/e2e/...` clean.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Sharing a socket between daemon and foreground (would conflict on bind — see "separate sockets"). Discriminating gate decisions at e2e (unit-tier contract). Stale-socket-file scenario (unit-tested as `TestTryAutoAttach_DaemonUnresponsive`).
