Latency / perf assertions (#158's unit test pins the structural fast-path). `PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH` non-`1` values (unit-tested as `TestTryAutoAttach_EnvOptOutNonOne`). Asserting on the foreground's stderr being empty (supervisor mode emits slog lines — non-empty stderr is expected, surfaced only in failure diagnostics).
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Foreground Auto-Attach Fallback Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/164-e2e-foreground-auto-attach-fallback.md`](specs/architecture/164-e2e-foreground-auto-attach-fallback.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3c-1, ticket #157)
- **`VerbSessionsHasID` + `SessionsHasIDResult` in `internal/control` — wire-only addition for one-bit UUID-existence queries.** Fifth `sessions.*` namespace member after `new`/`rm`/`rename`/`list`. New verb `"sessions.has-id"` reuses the existing `SessionsPayload.ID` field (introduced by #98 for `sessions.rm`, reused by #90 for `sessions.rename`) for "the session this verb operates on" — no new `SessionsPayload` field. Cheap focused alternative to `sessions.list` for the single-id case the 1.3c-2 foreground auto-attach path needs (~36-byte input + ~30-byte output instead of an O(N) registry table). The verb body is a pure registry read — no claude spawn, no state transition.
- **No new Sessioner sub-interface — handler reaches through the existing `SessionResolver.Lookup` seam.** Departure from the `Remover`/`Renamer`/`Lister`/`GetOrCreator` pattern of "one named sub-interface per verb embedded in `Sessioner`." For has-id, the registry-read primitive is **already** reachable via `SessionResolver.Lookup`'s `(*Session, ErrSessionNotFound)` contract: a known id returns `(*Session, nil)`, an unknown id returns `(nil, ErrSessionNotFound)`. `*sessions.Pool` already satisfies the seam through the `poolResolver` adapter. Adding a parallel `HasIDer` interface + `Pool.HasID` method would double the surface for the same map read. As a consequence, `VerbSessionsHasID` answers correctly even when `sessioner == nil`; `NewServer`'s signature is unchanged. The "one sub-interface per verb" pattern remains the right shape when the seam needs a method that doesn't already exist on the resolver — re-evaluate per future verb, not as a rule.
- **`Has bool` is deliberately NOT omitempty.** The wrapper-pointer `Response.SessionsHasID` is omitempty (so other verbs' byte-output stays unchanged); the inner `Has` is not. Reason: `omitempty` on `bool` elides the zero value, so `{Has: false}` would marshal to `{"sessionsHasID":{}}` — indistinguishable from a malformed response that forgot to populate the field. Emitting the boolean unconditionally costs ~10 bytes and produces an unambiguous shape: `{"sessionsHasID":{"has":false}}` for absent, `{"sessionsHasID":{"has":true}}` for present. Pinned by `TestProtocol_SessionsHasIDResult_HasNotOmitempty` at the marshal layer.
- **Strict-UUID validation at the seam boundary, before `Lookup`.** Two-step boundary check: missing payload / empty `ID` → `Response{Error: "sessions.has-id: missing id"}`; `!sessions.ValidID(payload.ID)` → `Response{Error: "sessions.has-id: invalid uuid"}`. `Pool.Lookup` would already return `ErrSessionNotFound` for any non-canonical string, but failing fast at the seam distinguishes "client typed garbage" from "well-formed UUID that happens to be absent" — the AC's contract. The empty-id branch could fold into `ValidID` (which also returns false on `""`); kept separate for the more useful error message, mirroring `handleSessionsRm` / `handleSessionsRename`. No prefix resolution — has-id is strict-UUID by design (the verb answers "given the canonical UUID I expect, does it exist?"; prefix ambiguity is meaningless in that context).
- **No new `ErrorCode`, no `context.WithTimeout`.** `Pool.Lookup`'s only typed error is `ErrSessionNotFound`, and that case is *not* propagated as an error — it's the absence-signal the verb returns as `Has: false`. Boundary-validation errors are plain strings; the typed-sentinel envelope #98 introduced is unused here. The handler skips `context.WithTimeout`: `Pool.Lookup` is an O(1) map read under `Pool.mu` RLock, and the conn's existing handshake deadline already bounds slow-write clients. A non-`ErrSessionNotFound` Lookup error (theoretically unreachable on `*sessions.Pool` today) is surfaced verbatim as `Response{Error: "sessions.has-id: <err>"}` — defensive against future Pool.Lookup error growth.
- **Client wrapper `SessionsHasID(ctx, sock, id) (bool, error)` mirrors `SessionsList`'s shape.** Single result + error, no typed-sentinel switch. Server-side validation errors flow through `Response.Error` verbatim. Empty-response guard returns `errors.New("control: empty sessions.has-id response")` for symmetry with the other client wrappers. The 1.3c-2 foreground auto-attach path is the intended in-process consumer; no CLI verb exists today (out of scope by AC).
- **Concurrency: `Pool.mu` (RLock) only.** Handler runs on the per-conn goroutine; no new goroutines, no `Session.lcMu` involvement, no new lock-order edges. Read consistency: a session minted between the handler's read and the client's decode will not appear; one removed will still appear. Acceptable for a yes/no query — the caller (1.3c-2's startup detection) treats the answer as a decision input, not a durable contract. Any acted verb (rm/new) serializes against this read through `Pool.mu`.
- **Backward-compat: existing verbs' wire output is byte-identical.** `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat` extended with a `SessionsList` row (the new `SessionsHasID` field's omitempty pin) plus reaffirmed `Response{}` and `Response{OK: true}` rows. Existing rows pass unmodified.
- **Test coverage in `sessions_has_id_test.go` (~378 LOC).** Reuses `startServerWithSessioner` and `fakeResolver` verbatim — no `fakeSessioner` extension (the verb does not consult the sessioner). `fakeResolver` extended with a `present map[SessionID]bool` field for the present/absent split. Mandatory tests: present (Lookup recorded, `Has: true`); absent (`ErrSessionNotFound` → `Has: false`, no error — pins the AC's "well-formed but absent → false, not error"); missing ID (zero Lookup calls); invalid-UUID guard (zero Lookup calls — pins fast-fail at the boundary); non-`ErrSessionNotFound` Lookup error (defensive contract for future Pool.Lookup growth); client wire shape (hand-rolled `net.Listen` captures `{"verb":"sessions.has-id","sessions":{"id":"..."}}\n` exactly — pins omitempty on `Label`/`JSONLPolicy`/`NewLabel`); empty-response-as-error; `Has`-not-omitempty pin.
- **Production diff ~106 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go` ~34 for `VerbSessionsHasID` + `SessionsHasIDResult` + `Response.SessionsHasID`; `internal/control/server.go` ~43 for dispatch + `handleSessionsHasID`; `internal/control/client.go` ~29 for `SessionsHasID`). Test diff ~389 LOC (`sessions_has_id_test.go` +378 + `sessions_new_test.go` +11 for the back-compat row). CLI surface unchanged; runtime wiring is implicit (`s.sessions` already non-nil by `NewServer` precondition).
- **Out of scope, by design.** The 1.3c-2 foreground auto-attach detection that consumes this verb. A `pyry sessions has-id` CLI verb (AC scopes the caller to a Go in-process client wrapper). Prefix resolution / loose-input acceptance. A `Pool.HasID` primitive or `HasIDer` interface.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Sessions: has-id seam (1.3c-1)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/157-control-sessions-has-id.md`](specs/architecture/157-control-sessions-has-id.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3b, ticket #155)
- **`pyry attach --create-if-missing <uuid>` + `Pool.GetOrCreate` — take-or-create attach for SDK consumers.** New flag on `pyry attach` that lets Claudian / `@anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk` issue one attach call instead of two (`pyry sessions new --id <uuid>` + `pyry attach <uuid>`). The SDK mints UUIDv4 per chat upstream and passes it through; pyry must accept the SDK's id even when it has never seen it before. Composes orthogonally with `--stdio`; the SDK's primary invocation is `pyry attach --stdio --create-if-missing <uuid>`. Without the flag, attach against an unknown id continues to fail with the existing `"sessions: session not found"` — opt-in semantics, no behaviour change for existing callers.
- **`Pool.GetOrCreate(ctx, id, label) (SessionID, error)` — take-or-create primitive (over `CreateWithID` insert-or-error).** Returns the canonical SessionID whether the session already existed or this call created it. The handler treats both branches identically from the call site onward (`Lookup → Activate → Attach`). Insert-or-error would force a follow-up `Lookup` after `ErrIDInUse`, re-introducing a TOCTOU window — see [ADR 014](knowledge/decisions/014-get-or-create-take-or-create.md). Pairs with `Pool.Lookup` and `Pool.Create`.
- **`ValidID(s string) bool` next to `NewID` in `id.go`.** Canonical UUIDv4 validator: 36 chars, lowercase hex, dashes at 8/13/18/23, version-4 nibble at 14, RFC 4122 variant at 19. Empty input → false. `GetOrCreate` rejects non-canonical input with `ErrInvalidSessionID` before any Pool state is touched. Validation lives at the Pool boundary so all future callers (direct Go consumers, test harnesses, future verbs) pick it up adapter-free. Belt-and-suspenders version + variant check is free; SDK-produced UUIDs are uuidv4 by construction.
- **Atomic registration — the load-bearing change.** Unlike `Pool.Create` (which releases `p.mu` between persist and supervise), `GetOrCreate` holds `p.mu` across **all five** of: duplicate-id short-circuit → registry-map insert → `saveLocked()` → `registerAllocatedUUIDLocked(id)` → `g.Go(sess.Run)`. Without holding the lock across the schedule, a concurrent same-id observer could see the registered entry under `if existing, ok := p.sessions[id]`, return id, call `Activate`, and block ~30s until ctx times out (the winner's lifecycle goroutine hasn't parked on `activateCh` yet). Race detector cannot catch it; failure mode is "long hangs at attach time on the loser." `g.Go` is non-blocking — the spawned goroutine parks on `activateCh` / `runCtx.Done()` before doing any pool work — so holding `p.mu` across it is safe. `Activate(ctx)` happens AFTER `p.mu` is released; its `capMu`/`lcMu` discipline would deadlock under `p.mu`.
- **Helper extraction shared with `Pool.Create`.** Two new private helpers: `buildSession(id, label) (*Session, error)` constructs the per-session supervisor + Session (touches no Pool state); `registerAllocatedUUIDLocked(id)` is the lock-held variant of `RegisterAllocatedUUID`. `Pool.Create` is updated to call `buildSession` (replacing its inlined block) and `RegisterAllocatedUUID` delegates to `registerAllocatedUUIDLocked`. `Pool.Create`'s body shrinks; behaviour byte-identical.
- **Wire field: `AttachPayload.CreateIfMissing bool` (`json:"createIfMissing,omitempty"`).** Omitempty is load-bearing for the same v0.5.x byte-identical contract that pins `SessionID`'s tag. Pinned by `TestAttach_CreateIfMissingOnWire` (companion to the existing `TestAttach_EmptySessionIDOmittedOnWire`).
- **Server-side branch + `GetOrCreator` 1-method interface.** `handleAttach` gains one branch at the front of the resolve step: with the flag set, dispatch to `s.sessioner.GetOrCreate` (validates UUIDv4, skips ResolveID's prefix logic — a "prefix that doesn't match" being interpreted as a fresh UUID would create non-canonical ids). Without the flag, today's two-step `ResolveID → Lookup` path. The 30s `activateCtx` is built earlier so `GetOrCreate`'s internal `Pool.Activate` shares the budget; the existing `sess.Activate` below the branch reuses it. New `GetOrCreator` interface mirrors the `Remover`/`Renamer`/`Lister` pattern, embedded into `Sessioner`. `*sessions.Pool` satisfies it structurally; tests fake it directly.
- **Skipping ResolveID's prefix path under the flag is a deliberate hazard guard.** The flag's intended caller is the SDK, which always passes a full UUID. Prefix-resolution is a human affordance not relevant to that path. A typo registering as a fresh non-canonical id (`b`, `0d1`) would corrupt the registry and `pyry sessions list` rendering.
- **CLI flag: `parseAttachArgs(args) (sessionID, stdio, createIfMissing, err)`.** `--create-if-missing` registered alongside `--stdio` on the same `flag.NewFlagSet("pyry attach", flag.ContinueOnError)`. `--create-if-missing` with no positional does NOT error at parse time — empty SessionID flows through to the server, where `GetOrCreate`'s empty-id rejection produces `ErrInvalidSessionID`. Parse-time vs. semantic boundary: parsing is purely about shape; semantic rejection lives at the Pool. Both `control.Attach` and `control.AttachStdio` extend their signatures with `createIfMissing bool` — single edit each, single production call site each.
- **Concurrent same-UUID safety.** Two `GetOrCreate(sameID)` callers race. One wins the lock, registers, persists, schedules `sess.Run`, releases the lock, proceeds to `Activate`, returns id. The other acquires the lock, observes the now-registered session via the duplicate-id short-circuit, releases the lock, returns id (no error). Both then `Lookup → Activate → Attach`; `Activate` is idempotent. Net result: exactly one registry entry, exactly one supervised child, exactly one rotation skip-set entry. AC #4 falls out of the atomic critical section.
- **Tests** (in `internal/sessions/pool_get_or_create_test.go`, ~406 LOC; `internal/control/attach_create_if_missing_test.go`, ~226 LOC; `cmd/pyry/args_test.go` extension; existing `attach_stdio_client_test.go` and `sessions_new_test.go` updates for the new wire field): `TestValidID` (table — empty/short/long/wrong-dash/non-hex/v3/non-RFC-4122-variant + canonical-NewID-output); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_Take_ReturnsExisting` (existing label preserved on take); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_Create_Persists` (caller's id written verbatim, claude spawned); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_PersistsPostDetach` (AC #1 — the test that surfaced ticket #169's persist-ordering race against `-race`); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_InvalidID`; `TestPool_GetOrCreate_PoolNotRunning`; `TestPool_GetOrCreate_ConcurrentSameID` (AC #4 — N=8 goroutines racing on one id, exactly one entry, label is one of the inputs, `-race`-clean); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_HonorsCap` (cap=1; bootstrap evicted via `Pool.Activate`'s cap-aware path); wire/dispatch/no-sessioner/invalid-id end-to-end via fakeSessioner.
- **Out of scope, by design.** E2E coverage of `pyry attach --stdio --create-if-missing` against a real daemon is deferred to a sibling Phase 1.3 ticket that wires up the broader stdio harness — same posture as #161 / #162 sit alongside #154's unit tests. Foreground auto-attach (Phase 1.3c) is independent. `pyry sessions new --id <uuid>` (the alternative two-call shape) is a separate ticket and does not exist today.
- **Production diff ~129 LOC across 8 files** (`internal/sessions/get_or_create.go` ~104 new + `internal/sessions/id.go` ~37 for `ValidID` + `internal/sessions/pool.go` ~83 net for helper extraction + `internal/control/protocol.go` ~7 + `internal/control/server.go` ~73 + `internal/control/attach_client.go` ~9 + `internal/control/attach_stdio_client.go` ~8 + `cmd/pyry/main.go` ~34 across `parseAttachArgs` + `runAttach` + help text). Test diff ~700+ LOC. PTY-mode `pyry attach` without `--create-if-missing` is byte-unchanged.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md § Pool.GetOrCreate (1.3b)](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md), [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Attach: --create-if-missing (1.3b)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [ADR 014](knowledge/decisions/014-get-or-create-take-or-create.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/155-attach-create-if-missing.md`](specs/architecture/155-attach-create-if-missing.md).

### Codebase (race fix, ticket #169)
- **`Session.Evict` / `Session.Activate` wait for the registry persist before returning.** `transitionTo` previously closed the per-direction wake channel under `lcMu` before calling `pool.persist`, so `Evict`/`Activate` waiters could observe the post-transition in-memory state and read **pre**-transition state from disk. Surfaced by `TestPool_GetOrCreate_PersistsPostDetach` (#155, PR #166) — that test polls `LifecycleState() == stateEvicted`, then reads the registry, and intermittently sees the pre-eviction state. Fix reorders `transitionTo` into three phases: (1) flip `lcState` + allocate the *opposite-direction* wake channel under `lcMu`; (2) release `lcMu` and run `pool.persist`; (3) re-acquire `lcMu` to close the *current-direction* channel. The persist now runs strictly between the state flip and the wake. New invariant: **`activeCh` is closed iff `lcState == stateActive` AND the persist for that transition has completed**; same for `evictedCh`. Cold-start init in `Pool.New` / `Pool.Create` already encoded this; no init change needed.
- **`Activate` / `Evict` lose their already-in-target-state early-return; always wait on the channel.** When fully transitioned, `<-ch` on a closed channel returns immediately (same wall-clock as the old short-circuit); mid-transition (state flipped, persist still running), the receive correctly blocks. Eliminates a second-shape race where a caller short-circuits on `lcState == stateActive` from a *prior* transition whose persist is still in flight.
- **Lock-order rule (`Pool.mu → Session.lcMu`) preserved.** `lcMu` is released before `pool.persist`; the post-persist re-acquire is sequential, not nested. The old comment at `session.go:347-349` ("releases lcMu before calling pool.persist so saveLocked's per-session lcMu re-acquire doesn't deadlock") still holds. Approach (1) from the ticket (move persist inside `lcMu`) was rejected for this reason; approach (3) (serialise transitions through a goroutine) was rejected as overkill — `Session.Run` is already the sole caller of `transitionTo`, transitions are already serialised by construction.
- **Channel close fires even on persist failure.** A permanently-stuck waiter is a worse failure mode than waking to stale disk. `Run` already treats persist failure as fatal (`return fmt.Errorf("persist evicted: %w", err)`), terminating the lifecycle goroutine — operator sees the failure via the errgroup's first-error propagation.
- **`Pool.Activate`'s cap path is unchanged.** Calls `sess.LifecycleState()` (in-memory) and `sess.touchLastActive()` (in-memory). No disk read at this caller; no race; no fix needed. The fix is local to three methods of `Session`.
- **Production diff ~60 LOC `internal/sessions/session.go`. Test diff ~191 LOC new file `internal/sessions/session_persist_test.go`.** Three regression tests: `TestSession_EvictBlocksUntilPersisted` (immediate `loadRegistry` shows `"evicted"`, no poll), `TestSession_ActivateBlocksUntilPersisted` (warm-start in `stateEvicted`, `Activate`, immediate disk read shows post-active state), and a stress wrapper looping 20 evict↔activate transitions asserting disk consistency at each step. Pass deterministically under `go test -race -count=20 ./internal/sessions/...`.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Other lifecycle transitions beyond `stateActive ↔ stateEvicted`. The un-skip of `TestPool_GetOrCreate_PersistsPostDetach` is part of #155's PR #166 rebase (its `t.Skip("blocked on #169")` line is removed when #166 lands on the new `main`).
- See [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md § Persist seam](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [ADR 013](knowledge/decisions/013-evict-activate-persist-ordering.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/169-evict-activate-persist-ordering.md`](specs/architecture/169-evict-activate-persist-ordering.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3a, ticket #154)
- **`pyry attach --stdio [<id>]` + `control.AttachStdio` — no-PTY byte forwarding for SDK consumers.** New flag on the existing `pyry attach` verb (not a new verb — see [ADR 012](knowledge/decisions/012-attach-stdio-flag-vs-verb.md)) and a sibling client function in `internal/control/attach_stdio_client.go`. Reuses `VerbAttach` unchanged: handshake sends `Cols=0, Rows=0`, `omitempty` drops both fields off the wire so the bytes are byte-indistinguishable from a v0.5.x client; the existing `payload.Cols > 0 && payload.Rows > 0` guard in `handleAttach` (#136) skips the resize seam. Server side is **byte-identical-input**, zero changes. Client side is straight `io.Copy(out, conn)` (output goroutine, joined via `done chan`) + `io.Copy(conn, in)` (main) — no `term.MakeRaw`, no SIGWINCH, no `copyWithEscape` state machine. EOF on `in` returns nil (clean detach; lazy-eviction semantics — detach ≠ destroy); server hangup after ack returns nil via the existing `writerErr` coercion.
- **Output goroutine is joined, not fire-and-forget.** Small upgrade over `Attach`'s shape — `Attach` can fire-and-forget because `defer term.Restore` doesn't depend on the goroutine completing; `AttachStdio` has no terminal state to restore but joining gives the caller a deterministic "all server bytes flushed to `out`" guarantee, useful for SDK consumers reading `out` until the spawned process closes the pipe. Closing `conn` is the cross-goroutine wake-up — no channels-with-cancel.
- **Sibling functions, not a shared core.** `Attach` and `AttachStdio` share the dial-and-handshake prologue (~10 lines); the diverging tails (raw mode + SIGWINCH watcher + `copyWithEscape` vs. plain `io.Copy`) are large enough that an attempted shared core would be a sea of `if stdio { … }` branches. Two functions, one wire protocol. If a third transport ever lands, factor at that point.
- **Flag-set parsing in `parseAttachArgs(args) (sessionID, stdio, err)`.** Fresh `flag.NewFlagSet("pyry attach", flag.ContinueOnError)` for `--stdio` after `parseClientFlags` peels globals; positionals routed through the existing `attachSelectorFromArgs`. Mirrors `runSessionsNew`'s precedent (ADR 010). Flag-ordering rule: `--stdio` must precede the positional — Go's `flag` package stops at the first non-flag arg, so `pyry attach <id> --stdio` is rejected as `errTooManyAttachArgs` (pinned in `cmd/pyry/args_test.go:TestParseAttachArgs`). The unit-testable helper avoids dialling the socket.
- **Affordance stderr lines suppressed under `--stdio`.** `"pyry: attached. Press Ctrl-B d to detach."` and `"pyry: detached."` are noise on a programmatic parent's stderr channel. One-line `if !stdio { … }` guards. No flag, no env var — the mode is the signal.
- **Rejected: auto-detect via `term.IsTerminal`.** Implicit mode switching is hostile in both directions — a test suite running `pyry attach` under a captured stdin would silently produce stream-json behaviour; an operator piping a heredoc into `pyry attach` would silently lose the escape-key surface. The flag is the explicit signal: SDKs pass it, humans don't, nothing changes accidentally.
- **Wire byte-shape pinned by `TestAttachStdio_NoGeometryOnWire`.** Captures raw bytes off the conn before decode and asserts neither `"cols"` nor `"rows"` nor `"sessionID"` appears — a future change that sets `Cols: 0` explicitly via a struct literal would still pass an `encoded.Cols == 0` check but break the wire-bytes promise this test enforces. Foreground-mode wire string flows through verbatim — `TestAttachStdio_AckErrorPropagates` pins parity with `TestServer_AttachOnForegroundSession`.
- **Production diff ~135 LOC** (`internal/control/attach_stdio_client.go` ~80 new + `cmd/pyry/main.go` ~55 for `parseAttachArgs` + `runAttach` dispatch + help text). Test diff ~500 LOC (`internal/control/attach_stdio_client_test.go` ~460 + `cmd/pyry/args_test.go` ~40). PTY-mode `pyry attach` is byte-unchanged when `--stdio` is absent.
- **Out of scope for #154**: E2E process-level harness driving `pyry attach --stdio` against a real daemon (#161); no-PTY-in-fd-table assertion via `lsof` / `/proc/<pid>/fd` (#162). `--create-if-missing` semantics is Phase 1.3b (#155); foreground-binary auto-attach is Phase 1.3c-2 (#158).
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Attach: stdio mode (1.3a)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [ADR 012](knowledge/decisions/012-attach-stdio-flag-vs-verb.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/154-attach-stdio-mode.md`](specs/architecture/154-attach-stdio-mode.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #161)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_stdio.go` + `attach_stdio_test.go` — stdio-attach test harness + byte-flow proof-of-life.** Sibling to #125's PTY-mode `AttachHarness`. New `StdioAttachClient` struct + `startStdioAttach(t, label) *StdioAttachClient` constructor under `//go:build e2e` (no installer-test consumer; gate is `e2e`-only, narrower than the PTY harness's `e2e || e2e_install`). Reuses `spawnAttachableDaemon` and `waitDaemonReady` from `attach_pty.go` verbatim — the supervised claude is the same e2e test binary running `TestHelperProcess` in echo mode (line-buffered). Two test files compile into one test binary and share the helper; only one `TestHelperProcess` in the package. Creates a fresh session via in-process `control.SessionsNew(label)` (same shape as every other e2e test in the package — spawning a third subprocess for one wire call is pure cost), then spawns `pyry attach -pyry-socket=<sock> --stdio <id>` with stdin/stdout wired to plain `os.Pipe()` ends — **no PTY anywhere on the client side**, exactly the SDK consumer shape Claudian / `@anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk` exercise in production.
- **Public API: `Write`, `ReadUntil(needle, deadline)`, `Close(t) int`.** `Write` writes to the parent's `inputW`; the child's stdin is `inputR`. `ReadUntil` reads from `outputR` in a background goroutine and selects against a deadline — `os.Pipe` ends share the no-`SetReadDeadline` trait with PTY masters on darwin (`lessons.md § PTY master fds on darwin do not support SetReadDeadline` is the adjacent shape), so the timeout is enforced caller-side. Returns `(seen []byte, err error)` with seen populated regardless of outcome. `Close(t) int` closes `inputW` (delivering EOF to the child's `AttachStdio` input loop), waits up to ~2s for the child, returns its exit code; idempotent via `sync.Once` with `t.Cleanup`.
- **Pipe-handle ownership and EOF discipline.** After `attachCmd.Start()`, the kernel has dup'd `inputR` and `outputW` into the child. The parent's copies must be closed: `inputR.Close()` so EOF flows from `inputW` alone, `outputW.Close()` so `outputR.Read` sees EOF when the child closes its stdout. Skipping either silently breaks the EOF semantics. Documented in `attach_stdio.go` next to the `Start` call.
- **Cleanup ordering — load-bearing.** `sync.Once`-wrapped: (1) `inputW.Close()` → child stdin EOF → clean detach → exit 0; (2) wait `attachDone` ≤ 2s, escalate via `killSpawned` (SIGTERM → grace → SIGKILL) on timeout; (3) `outputR.Close()` *after* the child has exited (don't race the child's stdout writes); (4) `killSpawned(daemonCmd)`; (5) `os.Remove(socket)` defensive against the SIGKILL escape. Mirrors the PTY harness's discipline minus the master/slave close pair.
- **Skip-on-no-pipe at `os.Pipe()`, not at handshake.** AC#3 ("CI hosts without spawn capability skip cleanly") is gated structurally — `os.Pipe()` exercises kernel fd allocation directly, faster than spawning pyry and tearing it down. Never fires on the project's CI matrix; defensive against future restrictive sandboxes. `t.Skipf` shape mirrors #125's `pty.Open` skip.
- **Handshake-failure detector mirrors `attach_pty.go:137-146`.** After `attachCmd.Start()`, the harness selects on `attachDone` vs `time.After(500ms)`: if the child exits within 500ms, `t.Fatalf` with the captured exit code + `Stderr` buffer + daemon stderr. Catches "no attach provider configured" if the daemon somehow landed in foreground mode, wire-decode errors if the protocol shifted, and (today) the #167 CLI-parse failure.
- **`os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-as-*")` for HOME.** Same `sun_path` budget rationale as the restart / rotation / attach harnesses — long test names + `t.TempDir()` overflow macOS's 104-byte limit. Short prefix keeps the socket path well under.
- **Round-trip test currently `t.Skip`'d on #167.** `TestE2E_AttachStdio_BytesRoundTrip` is **the harness's first consumer** but is `t.Skip("blocked on #167 — pyry attach --stdio rejected by parseClientFlags")`. The harness body works end-to-end against `internal/control` and the daemon; the bug surfaces at `parseClientFlags`, which rejects `--stdio` *before* `parseAttachArgs` ever sees it. Existing unit tests (`internal/control/attach_stdio_client_test.go`, `cmd/pyry/args_test.go`) bypass `parseClientFlags` so they didn't catch it. The harness was the surface that surfaced the bug. Once #167 lands, removing the `t.Skip` should make the test pass against the harness body unchanged.
- **No new harness API on the daemon side.** `spawnAttachableDaemon` already does what stdio needs (helper-as-claude, echo mode, idle timeout off, `-pyry-resume=false`). Reuse without parameter growth — no options struct, no shared `AttachHarness` interface across PTY/stdio modes (the surfaces differ in a load-bearing way: PTY exposes a `*os.File` master; stdio exposes line-aware `Write`/`ReadUntil`).
- **Out of scope, by design.** No-PTY-fd assertion (`/proc/<pid>/fd` Linux / `lsof -p` macOS) → #162. Foreground auto-attach scenarios → 1.3c-2-e2e-*. Multi-attach exclusivity, server-initiated detach, binary-safe transport for arbitrary byte sequences → unit boundary in `internal/control/attach_stdio_client_test.go`.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~321 LOC across 2 new files** (`attach_stdio.go` ~265, `attach_stdio_test.go` ~56). Default `go test ./...` unaffected; `go test -tags e2e -race ./internal/e2e/...` clean.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Stdio-Attach Harness Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Attach: stdio mode (1.3a)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/161-e2e-stdio-attach-harness.md`](specs/architecture/161-e2e-stdio-attach-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #162)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_stdio_no_pty_test.go` — binary-level no-PTY-fd assertion for `pyry attach --stdio`.** Sibling consumer of #161's `startStdioAttach` harness. Asserts the *negative* property the byte-flow test cannot: while attached, the attach client process holds zero PTY-device fds (`/dev/ptmx`, `/dev/pts/*` on linux, `/dev/ttys*` on darwin, `/dev/tty` on both). Unit tests in `internal/control/attach_stdio_client_test.go` already prove the client function imports no `creack/pty`; this is the binary-level defence — a future refactor that pulls a `pty.Open` into `cmd/pyry/runAttach`'s `--stdio` branch (or a "wrap stdio in a pty for raw-mode safety" helper) would slip past every unit boundary, and this test catches it. A regression that allocates a useless PTY but still passes bytes through fails only here, not `…_BytesRoundTrip`.
- **`runtime.GOOS` dispatch over build-tagged `_linux.go` / `_darwin.go` files.** One file, two helpers (`openPTYDeviceTargetsLinux` reads `/proc/<pid>/fd/`, `openPTYDeviceTargetsDarwin` shells out to `lsof -p <pid> -Fn`), one shared matcher (`isPTYDevicePath`). Build-tagged platform files would force the matcher into a third shared file or duplicate it; `runtime.GOOS` keeps everything in ~110 LOC. `unsupported GOOS` (and any inspection-mechanism failure: missing `/proc`, missing `lsof`, ESRCH from a raced child exit) returns an error which the test treats as `t.Skipf` per AC#2.
- **Matcher set is conservative + explicit.** Matched: `/dev/ptmx` (PTY master multiplexer — canonical "this process allocated a PTY" signal, both platforms), `/dev/pts/*` (linux PTY slaves), `/dev/ttys*` (darwin PTY slaves — `exec.Cmd` with explicit Stdin/Stdout/Stderr does not propagate the parent's tty fds, so any `/dev/ttysNNN` in the child's table was opened by the child), `/dev/tty` (controlling-terminal device, both platforms — a `--stdio` client with stdio wired to pipes has no business opening it; surfaces terminal-mode dispatch on the wrong code path). Not matched: `/dev/null` / `/dev/urandom` (not PTYs), BSD-legacy `/dev/pty[m-z]*` / `/dev/tty[m-z]*` (unreachable on supported macOS). Extend the matcher if a real regression escapes it; do not pre-enumerate hypothetical kernel device paths.
- **Probe runs immediately on harness return, no extra wait.** The harness's 500ms early-exit detector means `startStdioAttach` only returns once the child is past handshake, so any PTY allocation during init is already visible by probe time. Probe is a synchronous call from the test goroutine — no new goroutines, no channels, no deadlines. Linux symlink-read race (fd closes between `ReadDir` and `Readlink`) is silently dropped via `continue` — biases toward false-negative on a closing fd, acceptable; a stable PTY fd would not race a single-pass directory read.
- **No helper extraction, no shared matcher package.** `isPTYDevicePath` is 6 lines of pure string matching; `openPTYDeviceTargets{Linux,Darwin}` are thin syscall / `lsof` wrappers — mocking the filesystem or `lsof` would test the mock, not the behaviour. The test *is* the strategy: one assertion against one running binary. YAGNI per CLAUDE.md "simplicity first."
- **Carries the same `t.Skip("blocked on #167 — pyry attach --stdio rejected by parseClientFlags")` as `…_BytesRoundTrip`.** Both skips lift in one commit when #167 lands.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Stress / repeated-spawn / fd-leak testing (one-shot inspection at one moment is sufficient — the matcher would still trip on at least some runs of an intermittent regression). Daemon-side PTY assertions (the supervised claude runs under a PTY by design — this test inspects only the attach client's pid). Windows. A dedicated `pyry debug fds` verb (would expose internal state for one test's benefit, inspect the wrong process, and `/proc` + `lsof` are stable and well-known).
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~110 LOC, one new file** (`internal/e2e/attach_stdio_no_pty_test.go`). Default `go test ./...` unaffected; `go test -tags e2e -race ./internal/e2e/...` clean.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § No-PTY-fd assertion](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/162-e2e-stdio-attach-no-pty.md`](specs/architecture/162-e2e-stdio-attach-no-pty.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1b-B2, ticket #88)
- **`pyry sessions list [--json]` operator-facing CLI verb.** Final read-side member of the Phase 1.1 `sessions.<verb>` family (rounds out `new`, `rm`, `rename`). Plugs into the `runSessions` router (#76) as `case "list":` and consumes the `sessions.list` wire layer (#87) via `control.SessionsList`. First text-table sink in `cmd/pyry`: `text/tabwriter` (stdlib, no deps) renders a four-column table — `UUID`, `LABEL`, `STATE`, `LAST-ACTIVE` — with two-space padding (Go-CLI convention; matches `go list -m`/`go env`). UUIDs render in their full 36-character canonical form (no truncation — operators copy/paste them); `LAST-ACTIVE` formats as RFC3339 in the table. `--json` swaps the renderer for a single object with a top-level `"sessions"` array (intentionally not a bare array — leaves room for future top-level fields like `generated_at` without a breaking change). Per-element shape is `control.SessionInfo` JSON-encoded verbatim — no second timestamp conversion. The renderer re-sorts by `LastActive` desc with `ID` asc tiebreak (defensive against future wire changes; `Pool.List` already returns this order). 5s timeout (matches `runStatus`/`runLogs`; in-memory server-side handler, no `Pool.mu` waiting). Production diff ~75 LOC in `cmd/pyry/main.go`; test diff ~430 LOC across 2 files (`cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go` ~250 LOC unit; `internal/e2e/sessions_list_test.go` ~210 LOC e2e). Existing `TestSessionsNew_E2E_UnknownVerb` switched its placeholder unknown verb from `list` to `bogus` in the same edit (one-line conceptual change).
- **JSON envelope — anonymous struct, not `control.SessionsListPayload`.** Locally-declared `struct { Sessions []control.SessionInfo \`json:"sessions"\` }` documents the CLI presentation intent without coupling stdout shape to the wire payload type — adding CLI-only top-level fields later (e.g. `"generated_at"`) won't touch `protocol.go`. Wire bytes are identical either way; the cost is one struct declaration and the win is clean separation between "what the wire returns" and "what we print to stdout".
- **No retry, no `--state`/`--label` filters, no relative timestamps, no colour.** Snapshot read; user re-runs to refresh. `--json | jq` covers filtering today. Locale-aware "3m ago" formatting deferred — RFC3339 is unambiguous across timezones and across log-paste-into-issue boundaries; revisit on operator feedback. ANSI colour for STATE could land later as `--color=auto` if asked.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Sessions: list CLI renderer](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/88-cli-sessions-list.md`](specs/architecture/88-cli-sessions-list.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1a-B2, ticket #76)
- **`pyry sessions <verb>` sub-router + `pyry sessions new [--name LABEL]` first verb.** Operator-facing CLI surface for the `sessions.*` namespace. The top-level switch in `cmd/pyry/main.go run()` gains exactly one case (`case "sessions": return runSessions(os.Args[2:])`); `runSessions` peels global pyry flags via `parseClientFlags("pyry sessions", args)`, then dispatches on the first positional. Phase 1.1b (#61), 1.1c (#63), 1.1d (#65), and 1.1e (#49) each plug in as one switch case + one `runSessions<Verb>` helper + one token in `sessionsVerbList` + one word in help text — no top-level switch edit. `runSessionsNew` opens a `flag.NewFlagSet("pyry sessions new", flag.ContinueOnError)` (mirrors `runInstallService`'s precedent) for `--name`, then calls `control.SessionsNew(ctx, socketPath, label)` with a 30s `context.WithTimeout` matching the server-side ceiling in `handleSessionsNew`. Stdout is exactly `<uuid>\n` per AC#1 — `fmt.Println(id)` produces a canonical UUIDv4 + single newline, no surrounding text.
- **Sub-router takes a parsed `socketPath`, not raw args** — load-bearing for the global-flags-first convention. Two reasons: (1) one canonical parse path for every future `sessions.*` verb, with the existing helper's error wording; (2) structurally enforces "globals before sub-verb" — a `-pyry-name` placed *after* the sub-verb reaches `runSessionsNew`'s own `FlagSet` and produces "flag provided but not defined" instead of silently shadowing. Pinned by `TestRunSessions_GlobalFlagAfterSubcommand_FailsCleanly`. Mirrors the pre-existing top-level "pyry flags before claude args" rule (`splitArgs` lines 184-196).
- **`sessionsVerbList` is a constant, not a derived list.** A `map[string]func` would force a sort (map iteration is randomised) and an iteration cost that only amortises at ≥3 verbs. With one verb today and four 1-line additions in 1.1b/c/d/e, the duplication is one token per verb in two places (switch case + constant). Dead-simple beats indirection here. The 1.1b ticket extends both in the same edit — no new pattern, no map. The "one line per future verb" invariant the issue calls out is satisfied by structure, not by discipline.
- **`parseSessionsNewArgs(args) (label, err)` extracted from `runSessionsNew`** — keeps `cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go` table-driven over flag forms (`--name`, `-name`, `--name=`, `--name=glued`, extra positional, unknown flag) without dialling the socket. Mirrors `attachSelectorFromArgs`'s split (1.1e-D). The arity rule itself is trivial (zero positionals); the helper exists for the unit-test target, not for arity complexity.
- **AC#3 ("unknown sub-verb does not fall through to claude") satisfied structurally.** `runSessions` is reached from the top-level switch and returns through `errSessionsUsage` — control never falls through to `runSupervisor`. Pinned by `TestRunSessions_UnknownVerb` (unit, error-message check) and `TestSessionsNew_E2E_UnknownVerb` (e2e, registry session count unchanged before/after — proves the daemon's pool was not touched).
- **AC#4 ("activation failure leaves the registry entry in place") satisfied server-side.** `Pool.Create` (#73) saves the registry entry inside its critical section *before* `Pool.Activate` is called; an activation failure surfaces as `Response.Error` over the wire, but the entry persists for a future `pyry attach <uuid>` retry once 1.1e ships. The CLI is a 4-line synchronous wrapper; activation-vs-create error distinction is not visible at the wire boundary by design (the wire has no separate "id valid despite error" channel).
- **No retry / activation poll on transient dial failure.** `pyry status` / `pyry stop` / `pyry logs` don't retry; "no daemon" is a clean failure for the operator to act on. The no-daemon error surfaces as `pyry: sessions new: dial /path/sock: connect: no such file or directory` — same shape as `pyry status` against a stopped daemon. Pinned by `TestSessionsNew_E2E_NoDaemon` (asserts non-zero exit, non-empty stderr, no `panic`/`goroutine `/`runtime/` substrings — clean error, not a crash).
- **No new `--workdir` / `--cwd` / `-pyry-active-cap` flags.** `Pool.Create` inherits the daemon's bootstrap workdir; per-session workdir is Phase 2.x. `-pyry-active-cap` already shipped in #116 — defaults to `0` (uncapped) and stays a daemon-startup flag, not a `sessions new` argument.
- **Production diff ~82 LOC** (`cmd/pyry/main.go`: top-level switch case + `sessionsVerbList` + `errSessionsUsage` + `runSessions` + `parseSessionsNewArgs` + `runSessionsNew` + reserved-verb comment + help text). Test diff ~270 LOC across 2 files (`cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go`: ~100 LOC unit; `internal/e2e/sessions_new_test.go`: ~165 LOC e2e under `//go:build e2e` reusing `writeSleepClaude` / `newRegistryHome` / `readRegistry` / `waitForBootstrap` from #116). Default `go test ./...` runs unit tests only; e2e gated by build tag.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Sessions: CLI Router (1.1a-B2)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [ADR 010](knowledge/decisions/010-sessions-cli-sub-router.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/76-cli-sessions-new.md`](specs/architecture/76-cli-sessions-new.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.0, tickets #28 + #29)
- **`internal/sessions` package** — `SessionID` (UUIDv4 via `crypto/rand`, stdlib only), `Session` (wraps one `*supervisor.Supervisor` + optional `*supervisor.Bridge`), `Pool` (single-bootstrap registry with `RWMutex`-protected map). Sentinel errors `ErrSessionNotFound`, `ErrAttachUnavailable`. `Pool.Lookup("")` resolves to the bootstrap entry — the seam Phase 1.1's `Request.SessionID` plugs into.
- **Production consumers wired (#29)** — `cmd/pyry/main.go` constructs `*sessions.Pool` (with the supervisor.Config template inside `SessionConfig`); `internal/control` consumes a single `SessionResolver` interface (replaces Phase 0's `StateProvider` + `AttachProvider` pair). A 5-line `poolResolver` adapter in `cmd/pyry` bridges `Pool` → `SessionResolver` (covariant-return workaround). Wire protocol unchanged; `pyry status`/`stop`/`logs`/`attach` byte-identical to Phase 0. Foreground-mode attach error string preserved verbatim via `errors.Is(err, sessions.ErrAttachUnavailable)` mapping in `handleAttach`.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md), [knowledge/features/control-plane.md](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), and [ADR 003](knowledge/decisions/003-session-addressable-runtime.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #116)
- **`internal/e2e/cap_test.go` — `TestE2E_ActiveCap_EvictsLRU` + `TestE2E_ActiveCap_IdleInterleave`.** Two tests under `//go:build e2e` close the binary-boundary gap on the concurrent active cap (#41). The package-level race test had to switch to Bridge mode to avoid PTY contention; #116 verifies the LRU policy at the binary boundary against real PTY-backed children, plus the cap+idle interleave that two policies sharing `Session.Evict` couldn't otherwise exercise together. `EvictsLRU` runs cap=2, mints α/β/γ via `control.SessionsNew` (`Request{Verb:"sessions.new", Sessions:&SessionsPayload{Label}}`) with 50ms gaps so `lastActiveAt` timestamps are distinguishable for `pickLRUVictim`, asserts each new spawn cap-evicts the LRU peer (bootstrap → α). `IdleInterleave` adds idle=2s, 1s wait between α and β activations: Phase 1 asserts cap-evict of bootstrap with α/β still active; Phase 2 asserts α idle-evicts ~2s after its own activation while β is still active; final β idle-evict pins absence of state-machine wedge.
- **Three production wirings closed by this ticket** (all `cmd/pyry/main.go`, ~7 production LOC): (1) `-pyry-active-cap=N` flag (default `0` = uncapped) flowing into `sessions.Config.ActiveCap` — negative values map to "unset" via `Pool.New`'s `<=0` contract, no validation in `runSupervisor`; (2) registration in `pyryFlagValues` so `splitArgs` keeps the flag on pyry's side instead of forwarding to claude; (3) `pool` wired as `control.NewServer`'s `Sessioner` argument (was `nil` after #75's wire-only slice — `*sessions.Pool` satisfies `Sessioner` directly because `Pool.Create` returns `sessions.SessionID`, no adapter needed).
- **Tiny shell-script claude stand-in over extending fakeclaude.** `Pool.Create` constructs new-session args as `append(slices.Clone(tpl.ClaudeArgs), "--session-id", string(id))`. With the harness default `claudeBin=/bin/sleep` + `claudeArgs=["99999"]`, the new-session exec is `/bin/sleep 99999 --session-id <uuid>` — both BSD and GNU `sleep(1)` reject the unknown arg. Lifecycle state would still flip to `stateActive` (Pool tracks lifecycle independently of supervisor health), so cap-evict logic uncouples from this — but it generates noisy stderr and risks flakiness on backoff timing. Solution: a two-line `#!/bin/sh\nexec sleep 99999\n` script written to `<home>/sleep-claude.sh`, made executable, passed via `-pyry-claude=<path>` through `StartIn`'s variadic `extraFlags`. Both bootstrap (`<script> 99999`) and new sessions (`<script> 99999 --session-id <uuid>`) ignore positional args and `exec sleep`. Preferred over extending `internal/e2e/internal/fakeclaude` with a "no-rotation" mode (rotation-test binary, mixing concerns).
- **Four file-local helpers, no harness-side changes.** `writeSleepClaude(t, home)` writes the script. `waitForBootstrap(t, regPath, timeout)` discovers the bootstrap id by polling for `Bootstrap == true` (tolerates the registry file not yet existing — Pool's first save races the readiness gate). `waitForSessionState(t, regPath, id, want, timeout)` polls for a *known* id to reach `"evicted"` or `"active"` (the active arm tolerates either empty/missing or literal — same convention as `waitForBootstrapState` from #115). `assertActive(t, regPath, id)` is a one-shot checkpoint; fails if the session is `"evicted"` *right now*. Distinct from `waitForSessionState(..., "active", ...)` which returns on first observation; `assertActive` is "X must be true at this exact moment", used in the interleave test's gate between Phase 1 and Phase 2 to catch a session that flips active then evicts before the next poll. None promoted to `harness.go` — rule of three; one consumer.
- **Three `sessions.new` calls (four sessions total) instead of two in `EvictsLRU`.** AC asks "creates three sessions"; bootstrap is the fourth. The third call (γ) is the one whose LRU pick is non-trivial — it must skip β (just activated) and evict α (older). Two calls would only test "the new session evicts the oldest active peer once"; three exercises the LRU comparison across two non-bootstrap sessions, the regression-shaped failure mode the package-level race test (Bridge mode, no PTY) couldn't hit at the binary boundary.
- **Interleave timing: 1s gap between idle fires.** Idle timers are one-shot, armed at `runActive` entry (effectively at Activate moment); the 1s wait between α and β activations becomes a 1s gap between their idle fires. That window is the CI slack — bigger than typical Go scheduler jitter (~100ms) and registry poll cadence (50ms). 2s is the minimum useful idle timeout per the AC ("wait past idleTimeout"); if CI flakes, raise to idle=3s + wait=1.5s.
- **No `pyry status` cross-check.** `VerbStatus` resolves to the bootstrap session today (`Lookup("")`). For `EvictsLRU` the bootstrap is cap-evicted, so `pyry status` reports a non-running phase — same shape as #115. Including it would re-test the same surface as the registry assertion; skipped.
- **Production diff ~7 LOC; test diff ~204 LOC, single new file.** Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Active-Cap Eviction Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Server Construction](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), `lessons.md § Pool.Create appends --session-id, breaking naive claude stand-ins`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #126)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_pty_test.go` — `TestE2E_Attach_HandlesSIGWINCH`.** End-to-end cover for the live-resize chain through compiled `pyry` and `pyry attach` binaries. Reuses #125's `AttachHarness` + `StartAttach(t, "")` with no harness-side changes. Test resizes the harness's client-side master via `pty.Setsize(a.Master, &pty.Winsize{Rows:42, Cols:117})`, then `readUntilContains` matches the literal `winsize rows=42 cols=117\n` line emitted by the helper. Path under test: `pty.Setsize(master) → kernel SIGWINCH on attach client process group → startWinsizeWatcher (#133) → SendResize → handleResize (#137) → Session.Resize → Bridge.Resize (#136) → pty.Setsize(supervisor.ptmx) → kernel SIGWINCH on helper → helper emits the marker`. If any of the four halves regresses (client watcher, wire, server applier, supervisor seam), the test fails.
- **`TestHelperProcess` echo mode gains a SIGWINCH watcher.** Pattern mirrors `internal/supervisor/winsize.go`: `signal.Notify` + buffered `chan(1)` + goroutine + `pty.GetsizeFull(os.Stdin)` guarded by `term.IsTerminal`. On every signal, emits `fmt.Fprintf(os.Stdout, "winsize rows=%d cols=%d\n", size.Rows, size.Cols)` — single `Write` per emission, so `poll.FD.fdmu` serialises with the echo loop's writes (no byte interleaving). No teardown plumbing — helper exits on stdin EOF / `__EXIT__`, which terminates the goroutine implicitly. Watcher installed *between* `MakeRaw`+`PYRY_E2E_STARTED` bootstrap and the input loop, so by the time `StartAttach` returns the watcher is wired.
- **Extend the existing helper rather than add a second mode.** Per ticket: "reuse the harness's stub-claude program rather than introducing a second one." The new `winsize …\n` line is purely additive. Sibling tests are insulated by their match shape: `TestE2E_Attach_RoundTripsBytes` (#125) uses `bytes.Contains` for a nonced payload; `TestE2E_Attach_DetachesCleanly` (#127) drains master and asserts on `attachDone`; `TestE2E_Attach_SurvivesClaudeRestart` (#128) regex-matches `PYRY_E2E_STARTED pid=(\d+)\n` and a nonce. None collide with `winsize rows=N cols=M\n`. A second mode would force `spawnAttachableDaemon` to grow a "which mode?" parameter for no reuse benefit.
- **Dimensions chosen to avoid handshake collision.** `Rows: 42, Cols: 117` are deliberately distant from any sane terminal default. If the handshake's initial `Bridge.Resize` ever fires (slave default ≠ 0×0), the helper emits a winsize line for the default size *before* the test's resize — `readUntilContains` accumulates and matches the second emission. The test does not care which size came first.
- **Bursts coalesce.** Two SIGWINCH delivered before the watcher goroutine processes the first collapse to one queued event in the buffered `chan(1)`. On wake, `pty.GetsizeFull` returns the *current* (most recent) dimensions — the test's target. Same coalescing posture as the daemon-side watcher.
- **Skip-on-no-PTY inherited from the harness.** `StartAttach` calls `pty.Open` first and `t.Skip`s on failure (AC#4 satisfied without re-probing).
- **What the test deliberately does not pin.** Multi-SIGWINCH burst (covered by `TestStartWinsizeWatcher_SIGWINCHEmitsResize` from #133); detach-cancels-watcher (`TestStartWinsizeWatcher_StopIsSynchronousAndLeakFree` from #133); server clamps oversize dims (`TestServer_Resize_ClampsOversizeDims` from #137); foreground-mode silent resize (`TestServer_Resize_ForegroundSessionSilent` from #137 — the harness only runs bridge mode).
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~64 LOC, single file** (`internal/e2e/attach_pty_test.go`: helper extension + new test function + two new imports `os/signal`/`syscall` + the `creack/pty` import). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Attach SIGWINCH Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #68)
- **`internal/e2e` harness — spawn + cleanup primitive** — build-tag-isolated package (`//go:build e2e`, invoked via `go test -tags=e2e ./internal/e2e/...`) that builds pyry once per test process (`sync.Once`; `PYRY_E2E_BIN` short-circuits for CI), spawns it in a `t.TempDir()` `$HOME` with `/bin/sleep infinity` as the supervised "claude" and `-pyry-idle-timeout=0`, polls the Unix socket via `os.Stat` + `net.Dial` (5s deadline, 50ms gap, doneCh short-circuit on early exit), and tears down via `t.Cleanup`: SIGTERM → 3s grace → SIGKILL → 1s grace → `os.Remove(socket)`. Three exported names: `Harness`, `Start(t)`, plus the struct fields (`SocketPath`, `HomeDir`, `PID`, `Stdout`, `Stderr`).
- **`HOME` redirection contains every ~-relative path with one env var** — pyry resolves the socket, registry, and claude sessions dir all under `os.UserHomeDir()`, so `t.TempDir()` as `$HOME` isolates the daemon completely. Belt-and-suspenders `-pyry-socket=<HomeDir>/pyry.sock` flag for the load-bearing path; no new `-pyry-registry` flag needed. `PYRY_NAME` is stripped from the child env so the operator's shell alias can't leak in.
- **Failure-injection verification via test-binary re-exec** — `t.Fatal` in a same-process `t.Run` subtest propagates to the parent and ends the test before it can inspect leak state. `TestHarness_NoLeakOnFatal` re-execs `os.Args[0] -test.run=^TestInnerFatalChild$` with `PYRY_E2E_INNER_FATAL_OUT=<state-file>` so the failing path runs in a fresh process; the child writes (pid, socket) before `t.Fatal`; the parent reads the state file and asserts `processAlive(pid)` is false (`os.FindProcess` + `Signal(syscall.Signal(0))`, the POSIX zero-signal probe) and the socket is `fs.ErrNotExist`.
- **No `Option`s yet, no CLI-driver wrappers** — `Start(t)` is the only constructor; AC's "or equivalent" parenthetical covers the fail-fast `t.Fatalf` shape. `Harness.Status()`/`Stop()`/`Attach()`/`Run(args...)`, options, the first feature e2e, and CI wiring are deferred to the #51 follow-up. Build-tag isolation means existing `go test ./...` CI keeps passing untouched.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #81)
- **`internal/e2e/install_darwin_test.go` — `pyry install-service` × launchd `gui/<uid>` round-trip on macOS.** Three tests under `//go:build darwin && e2e_install`, mirroring #80's Linux shape: `TestE2EInstall_RoundTrip_macOS` writes the plist via `install.Install` → `launchctl bootstrap gui/<uid>` → `waitForRunning` (polls `launchctl print` for `state = running`, 10s deadline, 100ms gap) → `pyry status -pyry-name=<name>` (asserts exit 0 + `Phase:` in stdout) → `launchctl bootout` → `waitForUnloaded` → cleanup; `TestE2EInstall_PathInheritance_macOS` extracts `EnvironmentVariables.PATH` via `plutil -extract ... raw` and asserts each non-empty `$PATH` entry appears verbatim — note **no `$HOME/` → `%h/` substitution** (`derivePathEnv` gates the rewrite on `PlatformSystemd`); `TestE2EInstall_CleanupOnFatal_macOS` re-execs `TestInstallFatalChild` (same name as the Linux file, non-overlapping build tags) which installs + bootstraps + `t.Fatal`s, parent verifies `stat(plistPath)` is `ErrNotExist` and `launchctl print gui/<uid>/<label>` exits non-zero.
- **Same `e2e_install` build tag as the Linux sibling.** Single `go test -tags=e2e_install ./internal/e2e/...` invocation covers both platforms in CI when intended. Default `go test ./...` compiles neither file.
- **Plist parsing via Apple's `plutil`, not Go's `encoding/xml`.** The plist's key/value alternation pattern is awkward to walk with the stdlib XML decoder. `plutil -extract EnvironmentVariables.PATH raw -o - <plist>` returns just the PATH string — one shell-out, fails loudly on missing keys, no XML parser. `plutil` is part of `/usr/bin` on macOS; absence is a broken host, not a skip condition. ~30 lines of Go XML walking rejected as anti-simplicity.
- **`launchctl bootstrap` is async — poll `launchctl print` for `state = running`.** Bootstrap returns once launchd has *accepted* the request; the job transitions to `state = running` asynchronously. Polling loop is 100ms-gap, 10s-deadline; failure dumps the last `print` output for diagnosis. `launchctl print` is a debug command whose format Apple has reserved the right to reformat — `state = running` has been stable since macOS 10.10; if it ever breaks, the test fails loudly with a clear diagnostic.
- **Cannot isolate `$HOME` for the round-trip — same shape as Linux.** `launchctl bootstrap gui/<uid>` runs services in the user's GUI domain with `HOME` inherited from the GUI session, not from the test process. Round-trip and cleanup-on-fatal use the operator's real `~/Library/LaunchAgents/`; `PathInheritance` (no launchd dependency) keeps `t.TempDir()` isolation. Cleanup helper is idempotent best-effort (`bootout` + `os.Remove(plist)`) and additionally wipes runtime artefacts: `~/.pyry/<name>` registry dir, `<name>.sock` socket file, and the launchd template's hardcoded `/tmp/pyry.<name>.{out,err}.log` log files (unlike systemd which streams to journald).
- **Skip discipline.** `skipIfNoLaunchctl` (defensive — should never fire on macOS), `skipIfRoot` (`gui/<uid>` is non-root only; system-domain bootstrap requires root and is out of scope), `os.UserHomeDir()` failure → `t.Skip` (CI without HOME set).
- **Helper identifiers (`uniqueName`, `fatalNameEnv`, `fatalOutEnv`, `TestInstallFatalChild`) duplicated across the Linux and Darwin files with identical bodies.** The two files have non-overlapping build tags (`linux && e2e_install` vs `darwin && e2e_install`) so they never compile together — duplicate identifiers are legal and the simplest path. Names mirror exactly so a reader switching between files relies on muscle memory. Extracting into a third platform-neutral file deferred until a third platform appears.
- **Open question — headless macOS CI.** `gui/<uid>` requires a logged-in GUI session for that uid. GitHub `macos-latest` runners do have one; if not, the fallback is `launchctl bootstrap user/<uid>` (background-only domain). Defer until observed on real CI — AC specifies `gui/<uid>`.
- See [knowledge/features/install-e2e.md](knowledge/features/install-e2e.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #80)
- **`internal/e2e/install_linux_test.go` — `pyry install-service` × systemd `--user` round-trip on Linux.** Three tests under `//go:build linux && e2e_install`: `TestE2EInstall_RoundTrip_Linux` writes a unit via `install.Install` → `daemon-reload` → `start` → `waitForActive` (10s deadline, 100ms gap) → `pyry status -pyry-name=<name>` (asserts exit 0 + `Phase:` in stdout) → `stop` → `waitForInactive` → cleanup; `TestE2EInstall_PathInheritance_Linux` reads back the rendered unit and asserts each non-empty `$PATH` entry appears in `Environment="PATH=..."` with `$HOME/` → `%h/` substitution (bug-#19 regression guard, no real systemd needed); `TestE2EInstall_CleanupOnFatal_Linux` re-execs `TestInstallFatalChild` which installs + starts + `t.Fatal`s, parent verifies `stat(unitPath)` is `ErrNotExist` and `is-active` is not `"active"` externally — same shape as #68's `TestHarness_NoLeakOnFatal`.
- **Tag is `e2e_install`, separate from `e2e`.** Default e2e CI runs (using `e2e`) don't need a running user-systemd. `harness.go`'s build tag widened to `//go:build e2e || e2e_install` so the install tests reuse `ensurePyryBuilt` / `binPath` / `childEnv` without duplicating boilerplate. `runTimeout` (the CLI driver's 10s wrapper budget) is reused for the direct `pyry status` invocation in the round-trip test.
- **`install.Install` called directly, not via the CLI binary.** `install.Install` defaults `Options.Binary` to `os.Executable()` — for a test process, that's the test binary. The CLI exposes no `--binary` override; rather than add a hidden `PYRY_INSTALL_BINARY` env-var test seam (the pattern #34/#38/#69 rejected), the tests import `internal/install` and call `install.Install(opts)` with `opts.Binary = bin` set explicitly. The CLI mapping is unit-tested in `install_test.go`; the e2e value here is in the systemd round-trip and the rendered PATH line, not in re-testing flag parsing. `Options.EnvPath` (already exposed for testing) is reused as the path-inheritance test seam — no new seam invented.
- **Cannot isolate `$HOME` for the round-trip.** `systemctl --user` runs unit files in the operator's real session, not the test's redirected HOME. The round-trip and cleanup-on-fatal tests use the operator's real `~/.config/systemd/user/`; `PathInheritance` (no systemd dependency) keeps `t.TempDir()` isolation. Mitigations: unique `pyry-e2e-<pid>-<unixnano>` unit names guard collision; `t.Cleanup` registered *before* the state-changing `install.Install` so a failure between there and the end of the test still removes the unit; the cleanup helper is idempotent best-effort (`stop`/`disable`/`remove`/`daemon-reload` each ignore errors and `t.Logf`); also wipes runtime artefacts (`~/.pyry/<name>` registry dir + `<name>.sock` socket file).
- **`pyry status` invoked directly in the round-trip, not via `Harness.Run`.** The harness auto-injects `-pyry-socket=<h.SocketPath>`, but here the systemd-spawned daemon's socket is at `~/.pyry/<name>.sock`, derived by `resolveSocketPath` from `-pyry-name`. Direct `exec.CommandContext(ctx, bin, "status", "-pyry-name="+name)` exercises the same machinery the operator uses on a real install.
- **Skip discipline.** `skipIfNoUserSystemd` checks `systemctl` on PATH, then runs `systemctl --user is-system-running`. Skips on `offline` (no manager) / `unknown` (no D-Bus, the `ubuntu-latest`-runner shape) / empty + non-zero exit. Other non-zero states (`degraded`, `maintenance`, `starting`, `stopping`) are usable — proceed. Service accounts may need `loginctl enable-linger <user>` once.
- See [knowledge/features/install-e2e.md](knowledge/features/install-e2e.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #69)
- **`Harness.Run(t, verb, args...) RunResult` CLI driver** — invokes the cached pyry binary with `<verb> -pyry-socket=<h.SocketPath> <args...>`, waits for it to exit (10s `context.WithTimeout`), returns `RunResult{ExitCode int, Stdout, Stderr []byte}`. Auto-injects the socket flag after the verb so callers don't thread it through; reuses `binPath` (set by `ensurePyryBuilt` under `sync.Once`) and `childEnv(h.HomeDir)`. Verb is positional because pyry dispatches subcommands on `os.Args[1]` — encoding that into the signature prevents the `h.Run(t, "-pyry-socket=other", "status")` footgun. Caller-side override is naturally available via Go `flag`'s "last value wins" rule, no special case in the harness.
- **Failure asymmetry: non-zero exit returned, exec/timeout fatal** — `*exec.ExitError` populates `RunResult.ExitCode` for the caller to assert on; non-`ExitError` exec failure (binary missing, fork error) and 10s deadline expiry both `t.Fatalf` because there's no useful test recovery. The 10s wrapper budget is comfortably above `pyry status`'s own 5s socket-dial timeout (`runStatus` → `control.Status`). No regression test for the deadline branch — constructing a daemon that hangs `pyry status` for >10s requires real-claude unresponsiveness or test-only socket injection, both more invasive than the safety net buys; per evidence-based fix selection, defer until observed.
- **Struct over tuple for the result type** — `RunResult` future-proofs for `Duration`/`Combined`/`OOMed` additions without call-site churn; named fields prevent the `[]byte` mix-up between stdout and stderr that a positional tuple invites. Cost is one type declaration; worth it.
- **`TestStatus_E2E` — first feature-flavoured e2e** — spawns the daemon, runs `pyry status`, asserts exit 0 + `bytes.Contains(r.Stdout, []byte("Phase:"))`. `"Phase:"` is the leading literal in `runStatus`'s output (`fmt.Printf("Phase:         %s\n", resp.Phase)`) and is stable across phase values, restart counts, and future field additions; asserting on the *value* would couple the test to claude-child startup timing, which is exactly what `/bin/sleep infinity` was chosen to avoid. `pyry version` was rejected as the proof-of-life verb because it short-circuits in `main.go` before parsing flags — wouldn't exercise the socket plumbing the harness sells.
- **Package doc updated with copy-pasteable CLI-driver example** — replaces the bare smoke pattern from #68; godoc now surfaces a `Start(t) → Run(t, "status") → assert` recipe that downstream session-verb tickets (#52, #54, #55, #56) can copy.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § CLI Driver](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #52)
- **`internal/e2e/cli_verbs_test.go` — e2e coverage for the remaining shipped non-interactive verbs.** Four tests under `//go:build e2e`: `TestStop_E2E` spawns the daemon, runs `pyry stop`, asserts exit 0 + `bytes.Contains(r.Stdout, []byte("stop requested"))`, then bounded-polls (3s deadline, 50ms gap) until both `!processAlive(pid)` AND `os.Stat(sock)` returns `fs.ErrNotExist` — both conditions in the same iteration so the test doesn't race the supervisor's deferred socket cleanup. `TestStatus_E2E_Stopped` uses `RunBare("status", "-pyry-socket="+bogusSock)` against a fresh `t.TempDir()` non-existent path: exit != 0, non-empty stderr, no `panic` / `goroutine ` / `runtime/` substrings (clean error, not a crash). `TestLogs_E2E` runs `pyry logs` against a healthy daemon and asserts exit 0 + non-empty `bytes.TrimSpace(r.Stdout)` — the supervisor's in-memory ring captures startup lines, no specific wording asserted. `TestVersion_E2E` uses `RunBare("version")`: exit 0, output starts with literal `"pyry "` prefix, remaining token non-empty (`dev` in test builds, real version under `-ldflags`).
- **`RunBare(t, args...) RunResult` — daemon-free sibling of `Harness.Run`.** Same binary cache (`ensurePyryBuilt`), same `runTimeout` (10s), same exit-code mapping — but no daemon spawn, no auto-injected `-pyry-socket`, no `childEnv(h.HomeDir)` HOME redirection. Two motivated cases: verbs that don't touch the socket (`version` short-circuits in `main.go` before flag parsing), and negative tests against a known-bad socket path (avoids the spawn-then-stop-then-race-the-teardown ordering glue). The *only* harness API added in #52 — `Harness.Stop()` mid-test, typed `Status()`/`Logs()` wrappers, etc. were explicitly declined to keep the harness surface minimal.
- **Bogus-socket vs. spawn-then-stop for stopped-status.** Spawn-then-stop-then-status needs the test to wait for the daemon to actually shut down (otherwise status hits a still-listening socket and succeeds, defeating the test). That's the same poll loop as `TestStop_E2E`, plus ordering glue, plus a second `Run` call. Bogus-socket exercises the same code path (`net.Dial` fails → error surfaces clean to stderr → non-zero exit) without any timing dependency. Strictly simpler, strictly more deterministic.
- **Negative-assertion vocabulary for "clean error, not a crash".** Three conservative substrings — `panic`, `goroutine ` (Go's stack-trace header `goroutine N [state]:`), `runtime/` (Go runtime frames in tracebacks) — catch panics and stack traces without coupling to the exact dial-failure wording (today: `pyry: status: ... connect: no such file or directory`; allowed to evolve). Same pattern fits any "verify the failure is clean" assertion across future verbs.
- **File split: `cli_verbs_test.go` vs. appending to `harness_test.go`.** New file. `harness_test.go` is about *harness behaviour* (smoke, no-leak-on-fatal, the canonical `TestStatus_E2E` proof-of-life); `cli_verbs_test.go` is about *CLI surface coverage*. `processAlive` stays in `harness_test.go` and is reused via package scope (no duplication, no move). Build tag identical: `//go:build e2e` (not `e2e_install`).
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~155 LOC across 2 files** (`harness.go`: +42 for `RunBare`; `cli_verbs_test.go`: +112 new file). Default `go test ./...` is unchanged — both files are gated by build tags.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Bare CLI Driver](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #106)
- **`internal/e2e` restart primitive — `StartIn` + `Stop`.** `StartIn(t, home)` is the new workhorse: same body as the old `Start`, but uses the caller-supplied directory instead of allocating `t.TempDir()`. `Start(t)` becomes a one-line `return StartIn(t, t.TempDir())` — every existing call site unchanged. `Stop(t)` is a public wrapper around the internal `teardown` (name kept private to make the public/private split obvious); `cleanupOnce` (existing `sync.Once`) makes it idempotent with `t.Cleanup` — whichever fires first wins, the other is a no-op. Two ~10-line additions in `harness.go`; net public surface grew by exactly two names. No `Options` struct, no "respawn-in-place" method on `Harness` — adding either today would be speculative; struct migration is mechanical and non-breaking when a second knob lands.
- **`TestE2E_Restart_PreservesActiveSessions` — Phase 1.2's restart-survival proof at the binary boundary.** Pre-writes a registry with two `lifecycle_state: active` entries (one bootstrap, one non-bootstrap, hand-written canonical UUIDv4-shaped strings) → `StartIn` → `Stop` → `StartIn` against the same HOME → asserts `version` field, session count, per-session `lifecycle_state` and `bootstrap` flag preserved. Deliberately *not* asserted: byte-identity of the file (`MarshalIndent` output is allowed to evolve), `LastActiveAt` equality (would couple to today's no-save invariant in a way that breaks the moment a benign state-change ships).
- **Why this works against today's pyry without code changes.** Restart-time path against a pre-populated registry: `loadRegistry` reads → `pickBootstrap` selects the lone `bootstrap: true` entry; non-bootstrap entries are *not* materialised into `Pool.sessions` → `reg != nil` skips the cold-start save → `reconcileBootstrapOnNew` no-ops because `~/.claude/projects/<encoded-cwd>` doesn't exist under the test HOME → bootstrap enters `runActive`, idle timer disabled (`-pyry-idle-timeout=0`) → SIGTERM cancels ctx → `runActive` returns `ctx.Err` *before* `transitionTo(stateEvicted)`, no terminal save fires. Net: nothing in pyry calls `saveLocked` between pre-write and the second `loadRegistry` — the on-disk file is byte-stable across the restart. The non-bootstrap entries persist *because pyry doesn't touch them*, not because pyry materialises them. The test locks in the no-save-without-state-change invariant; future tickets that materialise non-bootstrap entries will need to preserve their lifecycle state across restart explicitly, and this test will catch any regression in either direction.
- **`os.MkdirTemp` over `t.TempDir()` for the HOME — Unix-socket `sun_path` budget.** `sun_path` caps at 104 bytes on macOS (108 on Linux). `t.TempDir()` embeds the test name into its path; `TestE2E_Restart_PreservesActiveSessions` + `pyry.sock` overflows the macOS budget. `os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-rs-*")` + `t.Cleanup(os.RemoveAll)` keeps the prefix tiny. Tests with short names are unaffected; only path-budget-tight cases need to switch. See `lessons.md § Unix-socket sun_path limits and t.TempDir()`.
- **Same socket path across both spawns is the realistic case.** Both `StartIn` calls derive `socket := filepath.Join(home, "pyry.sock")`. The second daemon's `Server.Listen` handles a stale socket file via dial-probe → ECONNREFUSED → `os.Remove` → `net.Listen`; no test-level coordination needed. By the time `Stop` returns, `cmd.Wait` has reaped the first process and the listener fd is closed; ECONNREFUSED is deterministic. The defensive `os.Remove(h.SocketPath)` in teardown belt-and-suspenders the SIGKILL path. Two harnesses (`h1`, `h2`) own independent `cleanupOnce`/`doneCh`/`cmd`; `t.Cleanup`'s LIFO order means `h2.teardown` fires first against the live second daemon, then `h1.teardown` no-ops.
- **File split: `restart_test.go`, not extending `cli_verbs_test.go`.** The latter is *CLI surface coverage* (one test per shipped verb); this is *daemon-level disk-state survival* and doesn't drive a CLI verb. Mirrors the `harness_test.go` (mechanics) vs. `cli_verbs_test.go` (verb surface) split #52 established. Local `registryFile`/`registryEntry` mirror types are duplicated intentionally — `internal/sessions`'s on-disk types are unexported, and exporting them solely for one test would invert the dependency direction. Schema is small and stable; if a field is added, the mirror grows it too.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~184 LOC across 2 files** (`harness.go`: +44 for `StartIn` + `Stop` + package doc; `restart_test.go`: +140 new file). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Restart Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #107)
- **Two more restart-survival e2e tests on top of #106's `StartIn` + `Stop` primitive — no new harness API.** `TestE2E_Restart_PreservesEvictedSessions` pre-writes a registry with a bootstrap-active anchor + a non-bootstrap `lifecycle_state: "evicted"` entry + a non-bootstrap-active control, cycles `StartIn → Stop → StartIn`, and asserts the evicted entry is *still* `"evicted"` on disk after the second daemon is ready (catches silent warm-promotion to active during bootstrap — the property `parseLifecycleState` and `pool.New` rely on for #38's warm-start semantics). `TestE2E_Restart_LastActiveAtSurvives` pre-writes three sessions whose `lastActiveAt` values are spread by 10 min and 1 hour, restarts, asserts every value roundtrips via `time.Time.Equal` (catches a re-stamp to `time.Now()` during bootstrap that would silently break the cap-policy LRU order from #41). Both tests scoped to non-bootstrap survival; bootstrap-evicted (warm-starting the bootstrap *itself* in `stateEvicted`) deferred to its own ticket — functionally distinct path (`runEvicted` instead of spawning the child).
- **`newRegistryHome(t)` file-local helper — rule of three.** With three restart-survival tests sharing the same four-line HOME bootstrap (`os.MkdirTemp` for sun_path safety, `t.Cleanup(RemoveAll)`, `mkdir -p <home>/.pyry/test`), #107 extracted the prefix into a file-local helper and refactored `TestE2E_Restart_PreservesActiveSessions` to call it. Intentionally not promoted to `harness.go`'s public surface — three callers ≠ a public API. `registryEntry` / `registryFile` mirror types and `writeRegistry` / `readRegistry` / `mustReadFile` from #106 stay file-local and unchanged.
- **Equality, not byte-identity, for `LastActiveAt`.** `time.Time.Equal` per entry, not byte-equal on the file. `Equal` accepts today's exact roundtrip *and* tolerates a future re-encode through `time.Now().UTC()` (strips monotonic, preserves wall-clock — the AC's "tight tolerance"); rejects loudly when the value is re-stamped to `time.Now()` because the 10-min / 1-hour spread dwarfs any plausible JSON-roundtrip drift. Asserting on byte-identity of the file would couple to `MarshalIndent` formatting (brittle); per-field `Equal` is durable.
- **Monotonic-clock trap: capture "want" via the same JSON trip the daemon takes.** `time.Time` written via `MarshalIndent` retains monotonic-clock state in the original Go value but strips it after the JSON unmarshal trip. Comparing pre-write in-memory vs. post-restart parsed would diverge on monotonic alone *even when bytes on disk are identical* — masquerading as a real timestamp regression. `TestE2E_Restart_LastActiveAtSurvives` re-reads the file with `readRegistry` immediately after `writeRegistry` and uses *that* parsed value as the expectation. New lessons.md entry: § JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state from time.Time.
- **Why this works against today's pyry without code changes — same chain as #106.** `loadRegistry` reads → `pickBootstrap` selects bootstrap, non-bootstrap entries not materialised → `reg != nil` skips cold-start save → `reconcileBootstrapOnNew` no-ops (no `~/.claude/projects/<encoded-cwd>` under test HOME) → bootstrap enters its lifecycle goroutine; SIGTERM cancels ctx → goroutine returns `ctx.Err` *before* `transitionTo`, no terminal save. The on-disk bytes for non-bootstrap entries are byte-stable across restart because pyry reads but does not rewrite. The two new tests lock in the no-save-without-state-change invariant alongside #106; future tickets that materialise non-bootstrap entries or re-stamp `lastActiveAt` during bootstrap will have to update production and these tests in lockstep.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~140 LOC, single file** (`internal/e2e/restart_test.go`: helper extraction + two new tests + refactor of the existing test to use the helper). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Restart Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), `lessons.md § JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state from time.Time`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #111)
- **`internal/e2e/startup_test.go` — `TestE2E_Startup_CorruptRegistryFailsClean`.** Single test under `//go:build e2e`: seeds `<home>/.pyry/test/sessions.json` with `{not valid json` via `newRegistryHome` (reused from `restart_test.go`), calls `StartExpectingFailureIn`, asserts `ExitCode != 0`, `bytes.Contains(res.Stderr, []byte("registry"))`, and `bytes.Equal(diskBytes, corruptBytes)`. The byte-equal assertion is the load-bearing one — catches the worst-possible regression ("corrupt file → empty registry → drop everything") without depending on JSON-parsing the corrupt input. Substring `registry` chosen over the absolute path or `sessions.json`: path varies per run and `sessions.json` is just the filename, while "registry" is the operator-facing domain concept; production chain happens to contain it twice (`pool init: sessions: load registry: registry: parse <path>: <unmarshal err>`) so the assertion is robust to wrap-chain refactors.
- **`StartExpectingFailureIn(t, home) RunResult` — failed-start sibling of `StartIn`.** The harness extension this ticket adds: spawns pyry against the caller-supplied HOME, expects it to exit before `readyDeadline`, returns the captured `RunResult`. No `Harness` returned — there is no live daemon to drive, no socket to clean up. Caller pre-populates HOME (corrupt registry, missing claude binary in future tickets, …) and asserts on the streams. Two defensive `t.Fatalf` branches — "daemon unexpectedly came up" and "neither exit nor readiness within `readyDeadline`" — fire only on production regression or a hung test environment; both tear the daemon down via `killSpawned` (SIGTERM → `termGrace` → SIGKILL → `killGrace`, mirroring `Harness.teardown`) before failing.
