- **Internal refactor: shared `spawn(t, home)` helper.** Extracted from `StartIn`'s body. `spawn` does fork + wait-goroutine + child-env wiring; deliberately does **not** register `t.Cleanup`, build the `Harness`, or call `waitForReady` — each caller owns those policies. `StartIn` becomes `spawn` → build `Harness` → register cleanup → `waitForReady`; `StartExpectingFailureIn` becomes `spawn` → select-driven loop over `(net.Dial, doneCh, time.After(readyPollGap))`. Reuses existing `readyDeadline = 5s` and `readyPollGap` constants — the corrupt-registry path exits in milliseconds (synchronous JSON parse), so 5s is generous. No new constants.
- **Why an alternate constructor (not Options on `StartIn`).** The ticket forbids "unused API surface" and "parallel implementation". `Options` field on `StartIn` would force a polymorphic return (`*Harness` doesn't fit the failure path); a lower-level public `spawn` helper would be bigger surface than the one test needs; the alternate constructor keeps the surface minimal, mirrors `Run`/`RunBare`, and shares the body via the private `spawn`. `StartExpectingFailure(t)` (zero-arg) declined: the failure path always wants caller-supplied HOME to seed the on-disk failure state, so the no-`In` form would be unused.
- **File split: `startup_test.go`, not extending `restart_test.go`.** Domain is *startup failure*, not *restart survival*. Future failed-start e2e tests (missing claude binary, unreachable workdir, port-in-use socket) have a natural home next to it; `StartExpectingFailureIn` is the primitive they reuse.
- **Coverage of the helper's defensive branches.** Only the success path of `StartExpectingFailureIn` is exercised (child exits before ready). The two `t.Fatalf` branches earn their keep as crash-loud guards, not as covered behaviours — per the ticket's "exercised exclusively by this test" constraint, no unit tests added for them. Future failed-start tests provide implicit coverage as they land.
- **Production diff is zero.** The corrupt-registry failure path already exists (`loadRegistry` → `json.Unmarshal` returns `registry: parse %s: %w`; `Pool.New` wraps as `sessions: load registry: …`; `runSupervisor` wraps as `pool init: …`; `main` prints + `os.Exit(1)`). Test diff: ~70 LOC across 2 files (`harness.go`: +60 for `StartExpectingFailureIn` + `spawn` extraction + `killSpawned`; `startup_test.go`: +35 new file). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Failed-Start Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/sessions-registry.md § Load semantics](knowledge/features/sessions-registry.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1+ resize seam, ticket #136)
- **`Bridge.Resize(rows, cols uint16) error` + `Bridge.SetPTY(*os.File)` — the typed supervisor-side resize seam.** `Bridge` gains a leaf-only `ptyMu` mutex over a per-iteration `*os.File`. `runOnce` calls `SetPTY(ptmx)` after `pty.Start`, then `SetPTY(nil)` **before** `EndIteration` so an in-flight `Resize` racing iteration teardown sees nil rather than a closed fd. `Resize` is a no-op (returns nil) when no PTY is registered (between iterations / foreground mode). `pty.Setsize` errors are wrapped + returned for the caller to log. The seam landed on `*Bridge` (not `*Supervisor` and not a `Run`-wired callback) because the `Session → Bridge` chain already exists for `Attach` and `BeginIteration`/`EndIteration` already brackets every iteration — see [ADR 008](knowledge/decisions/008-bridge-resize-seam.md).
- **`Session.Resize(rows, cols uint16) error` — one-line delegator.** Returns `ErrAttachUnavailable` when the session has no bridge (foreground mode). No `lcMu` taken, no `lastActiveAt` bump, no interaction with the active↔evicted state machine. Pure pass-through to `Bridge.Resize`, whose own internal mutex handles the iteration-boundary race.
- **`internal/control.Session` interface gains `Resize(rows, cols uint16) error`.** Two implementers updated: `*sessions.Session` (production) and `*fakeSession` (tests). `handleAttach` calls `sess.Resize` between `Activate` and `Attach`, guarded by `payload != nil && payload.Cols > 0 && payload.Rows > 0`; `clampUint16(int) uint16` clamps pathological client sizes silently. The wire's cols-then-rows order is swapped at this single boundary site to match `Bridge.Resize`'s rows-then-cols (which mirrors `pty.Winsize` field order).
- **Resize errors do NOT fail the attach.** `pty.Setsize` failure is logged at Warn and the attach proceeds. Geometry is best-effort; a stale window size is recoverable on the next keystroke. `ErrAttachUnavailable` from a foreground-mode session is also swallowed — foreground has its own SIGWINCH watcher in `winsize.go`.
- **Caveats rewritten in `protocol.go` and `supervisor.go`.** `AttachPayload`'s "server discards Cols/Rows" sentence dropped (kept the live-resize / SIGWINCH paragraph, cleared by #137). The Phase-0 caveat at `supervisor.go` lines 248-250 rewritten to reflect the new reality (handshake geometry now applied; live SIGWINCH still belongs to whichever client attaches). `attach_client.go:25-27` caveat untouched (cleared by #133).
- **Test coverage.** Control side: `TestServer_AttachAppliesHandshakeGeometry` + `TestServer_AttachZeroGeometryNoOp` (table-driven over four nil/zero combos) + `TestServer_AttachResizeErrorDoesNotFailAttach` against an extended `fakeSession` recording `resizeCalls`. Supervisor side: `TestBridge_ResizeAppliesToPTY` opens a real `pty.Open()` master/slave pair and asserts `pty.Getsize` reports the new dimensions; `TestBridge_ResizeNoPTYRegistered` and `TestBridge_ResizeAfterClearPTY` cover the silent no-op branches. Sessions package has no new tests — `Session.Resize` is a one-line delegator already implicitly covered by the bridge tests + the existing nil-bridge `Attach` test.
- **Production diff ~95 LOC across 5 files** (`internal/supervisor/bridge.go` +30 for `SetPTY`/`Resize` + ptyMu field; `internal/supervisor/supervisor.go` runOnce +5 for `SetPTY`/`SetPTY(nil)` ordering; `internal/sessions/session.go` +15 for `Session.Resize`; `internal/control/server.go` +20 for `Session.Resize` interface method + `handleAttach` resize block + `clampUint16`; `internal/control/protocol.go` caveat rewrite). Test diff ~270 LOC (`bridge_test.go` +66; `attach_test.go` +160; `server_test.go` +33).
- **Stacks under #137 and #133 (both shipped).** The wire-protocol resize message (#137) consumes `Bridge.Resize` for live SIGWINCH propagation; the client-side SIGWINCH emitter (#133, `startWinsizeWatcher`) produces the message. Live-resize loop is closed end-to-end as of #133.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Attach: Handshake Geometry](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [knowledge/decisions/008-bridge-resize-seam.md](knowledge/decisions/008-bridge-resize-seam.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1+ resize wire + applier, ticket #137)
- **`VerbResize` + `ResizePayload` + `handleResize` — live SIGWINCH propagation rides a side-channel one-shot conn, not a framed escape in the attach byte stream.** New verb on the JSON protocol; client dials a *fresh* control connection per resize, sends one `Request{Verb:"resize", Resize:&ResizePayload{SessionID, Cols, Rows}}`, reads one `Response{OK:true}` ack, closes — same lifecycle as `VerbStatus`/`VerbStop`/`VerbLogs`. Independent of the long-lived attach conn so a malformed resize cannot tear down the attach session — the property is **structural** (two `net.Conn`s, two independent handler goroutines), not coded. See [ADR 009](knowledge/decisions/009-resize-wire-shape.md) for the full trade-off matrix vs. framed-escape and against a *persistent* second connection.
- **`handleResize` mirrors `handleAttach`'s handshake-geometry block, minus connection handoff.** Resolve via `s.sessions.ResolveID(payload.SessionID)` → `Lookup` → swap (`rows = clampUint16(payload.Rows)`, `cols = clampUint16(payload.Cols)`) → `sess.Resize(rows, cols)` → encode `OK:true`. Cols-then-rows on the wire (mirroring `AttachPayload`); rows-then-cols at the seam (mirroring `pty.Winsize`); the swap is local to `handleResize`. Zero in either dim is the "don't touch" sentinel — same rule as the handshake path.
- **Best-effort posture: OK ack even when the seam errors.** `pty.Setsize` failure is logged at Warn and the client gets `OK: true`. `ErrAttachUnavailable` (foreground session) is silently swallowed — foreground has its own SIGWINCH watcher in `winsize.go`. The only error responses are pre-seam routing failures (`payload == nil` → `"resize: missing payload"`; `ResolveID`/`Lookup` errors → `"resize: <err>"`). The client has nothing useful to do with a "resize failed" response — the next SIGWINCH will re-emit; the user's terminal already shows the new size locally.
- **Session-must-be-attached is NOT enforced.** A resize can arrive between `pyry attach` and the actual bridge handshake completing, or after a transient detach during a SIGWINCH burst. `Bridge.Resize` already silently no-ops when `ptmx` is nil. Letting the resize through unconditionally is simpler and matches `pty.Setsize`'s own semantics.
- **No new mutexes, channels, or goroutines.** The accept loop's existing one-goroutine-per-conn pattern absorbs resize handlers; each completes in ~1ms (one resolver lookup + one `pty.Setsize`). `Bridge.ptyMu` (#136) serialises concurrent resizes; last-write-wins matches the kernel's `ioctl(TIOCSWINSZ)`.
- **`SendResize(ctx, socketPath, sessionID, cols, rows) error` — client helper next to `Status`/`Stop`/`Logs`, reusing `request()`.** A successful return means the server received and dispatched; the seam's own success is best-effort and not visible to the client. Defined here, consumed by #133's SIGWINCH handler in `pyry attach`.
- **Caveat status.** `internal/control/protocol.go` Phase-0 caveat (was lines 49-55) **rewritten** in #137 — points to `VerbResize`/`ResizePayload`. The "(deferred to #133)" parenthetical was cleared in #133. `internal/control/attach_client.go:25-27` caveat **rewritten** in #133 (was: "Subsequent live resize events are not propagated in Phase 0 — detach and reattach to update.").
- **Test coverage.** `internal/control/resize_test.go` (~290 LOC, single new file) reuses the existing `fakeSession` (already records `resizeCalls` from #136) + `fakeResolver` — no test infra changes. Coverage: applies-to-seam end-to-end, table-driven zero-dim no-op (`{0,0}, {0,40}, {120,0}` plus `nil` payload), unknown-session error, seam-error-returns-OK, foreground-session-silent, oversize-dim clamp, `SendResize` round-trip + server-error wire string. The structural "decoding errors do not tear down the attach session" property is intentionally **not** unit-tested — falls out of conn independence; documented in `handleResize`'s godoc instead (per CLAUDE.md "evidence-based fix selection").
- **Production diff ~95 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go` +25 for `VerbResize` + `ResizePayload` + caveat rewrite; `internal/control/server.go` +42 for `handleResize` + dispatch; `internal/control/client.go` +26 for `SendResize`). Test diff ~290 LOC, single new file. No supervisor changes.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Resize: Live Wire Message and Applier](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [knowledge/decisions/009-resize-wire-shape.md](knowledge/decisions/009-resize-wire-shape.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1+ live-resize client trigger, ticket #133)
- **`startWinsizeWatcher` + `readTerminalSize` inside `internal/control/attach_client.go` — closes the live-resize loop end-to-end.** `Attach` installs a SIGWINCH watcher *after* the handshake ack succeeds; the watcher converts each `SIGWINCH` into a `SendResize(ctx, socketPath, sessionID, cols, rows)` on a fresh control conn (independent of the long-lived attach conn). With #136 (`Bridge.Resize` seam) and #137 (`VerbResize` wire + server applier) already shipped, the full path is now: terminal resize → kernel SIGWINCH → watcher reads `pty.GetsizeFull(os.Stdin)` → `SendResize` → `handleResize` → `Session.Resize` → `Bridge.Resize` → `pty.Setsize` → child redraws. No more "detach and reattach to update."
- **No new exported type, no new file in `internal/control` for the watcher itself.** `startWinsizeWatcher` is a package-internal helper next to `Attach`; the watcher's lifetime is exactly `Attach`'s stack frame, so a struct receiver would inflate the change for no benefit. The helper takes its dependencies as function parameters (`read terminalSizeReader`, `send func(ctx, cols, rows) error`) — keeps `os` and the network out of the watcher body, and lets unit tests inject stubs without a package-level `var` indirection (which would couple test substitution to global state shared with sibling tests).
- **Synchronous teardown is the load-bearing guarantee for AC#3.** `stop` does (1) `signal.Stop(sigCh)` to unsubscribe, (2) `close(done)` to wake the goroutine's `select`, then (3) blocks on `<-gone` until the goroutine has actually exited. No goroutine or signal subscription outlives the `defer stopWinsize()` call site — leak-freeness is *structural*, not *eventual*. If `SendResize` is in flight when `stop` fires, `<-gone` waits out the in-flight call: detach cannot race a half-completed resize.
- **No initial-size priming after the handshake.** AC#2 prohibits regressing the handshake `AttachPayload.Cols`/`Rows` path; the first SIGWINCH (or, in the absent-resize case, the next one) covers any change between handshake and first event. Window is microseconds; priming would push a duplicate resize in the steady-state-no-change case for no benefit.
- **`os.Stdin` directly, not a fresh `*os.File` wrapper around `os.Stdin.Fd()`.** Same convention `internal/supervisor/winsize.go` follows for the same reason: a wrapper `*os.File` is finalizable, and finalizer-driven `close(2)` racing a subsequent `open(2)` is the classic fd-reuse race that makes `pty.Setsize` target the wrong file. Lessons.md § Closing a fd to interrupt a goroutine's Read requires O_NONBLOCK has the adjacent shape; this case is its read-side cousin.
- **Best-effort posture, no logging.** `SendResize` errors silently dropped via `_ = send(ctx, cols, rows)`; the next SIGWINCH retries. Mirrors `SendResize`'s godoc and `handleResize`'s OK-on-seam-error posture (#137). The watcher logs nothing — the package is library-level, and SendResize errors are uninteresting in practice (either "daemon went away" — already surfaced by the attach conn dropping — or transient hiccup — corrected by the next resize).
- **Burst coalescing falls out of the buffered-cap-1 sigCh.** SIGWINCH arrivals during a `SendResize` collapse to one queued event; after `SendResize` returns, the goroutine reads the queued one and emits a *fresh* resize with the current size (re-read at signal time, not stale). Same coalescing shape as `supervisor/winsize.go`. Server-side `Bridge.ptyMu` serialises and last-write-wins matches `ioctl(TIOCSWINSZ)`'s native semantics.
- **Concurrency: three goroutines inside `Attach`, none share state.** Output copier (existing), input pump (calling goroutine, in `copyWithEscape`), and the new watcher. Watcher does NOT touch the attach `conn` — each SIGWINCH is its own short-lived dial via `SendResize`. A malformed resize, daemon-side seam error, or transient dial failure lives entirely on the resize conn and never disturbs the byte stream on the attach conn (the property is structural, mirroring #137's design).
- **`defer stopWinsize()` ordering vs. `defer conn.Close()`.** `defer conn.Close()` is registered first (top of `Attach`), `defer stopWinsize()` second (after handshake ack). LIFO: stop the watcher first, then close the conn. Operationally irrelevant since resize uses its own conn anyway, but documents intent.
- **Caveat rewrite.** `internal/control/attach_client.go:25-27` Phase-0 sentence ("Subsequent live resize events are not propagated in Phase 0 — detach and reattach to update.") **rewritten** to identify the SIGWINCH watcher as the live producer and `Bridge.Resize` as the seam. `internal/control/protocol.go` line 62 parenthetical updated from "deferred to #133" to point at `startWinsizeWatcher`.
- **Test coverage.** Two tests in new `internal/control/attach_winsize_test.go` (build tag `//go:build unix`, since `syscall.SIGWINCH` is unix-only and the project excludes Windows): `TestStartWinsizeWatcher_SIGWINCHEmitsResize` (hand-rolled `net.Listen` server, stub `read` returns `(120, 40, true)`, `syscall.Kill(syscall.Getpid(), syscall.SIGWINCH)` delivers the signal, server records the decoded `Request{Verb: VerbResize, Resize: &ResizePayload{Cols:120, Rows:40, SessionID:"abc"}}`); `TestStartWinsizeWatcher_StopIsSynchronousAndLeakFree` (50 iterations of start + Kill SIGWINCH + stop + cancel, samples `runtime.NumGoroutine()` before/after with small slack — per-iteration leakage would dwarf any noise budget). Both tests run **without** `t.Parallel()`: `syscall.Kill(SIGWINCH)` is process-wide, so any concurrent test subscribing to SIGWINCH would race. Audit confirms no other test in `internal/control` does so today.
- **End-to-end coverage deferred to #126.** The CLI driver (`internal/e2e`) is the right home for full-Attach-with-real-PTY end-to-end resize coverage; #126 is the open ticket.
- **Production diff ~95 LOC across 2 files** (`internal/control/attach_client.go`: +75 for `startWinsizeWatcher` + `readTerminalSize` + `terminalSizeReader` type + `Attach` wiring + caveat rewrite; `internal/control/protocol.go`: -1/+1 line for the parenthetical). Test diff ~125 LOC, single new file.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Resize: Live SIGWINCH Watcher (#133)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #128)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_restart_test.go` — `TestE2E_Attach_SurvivesClaudeRestart`.** Drives an attached `pyry attach` client across a forced supervised-claude restart and asserts: pre-restart byte round-trip, two distinct startup-marker PIDs (proves respawn), post-restart byte round-trip within 5s (proves the bridge re-bound to the new PTY), attach client process still alive after the respawn (`select { case <-a.attachDone: t.Fatalf(...); default: }`). Builds on #125's `AttachHarness` with no new harness API; reuses `tinyNonce` and `readUntilContains` verbatim. Build tag `//go:build e2e`; default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- **Architect's spec was billed as test-only; implementation surfaced a real production bug.** The supervisor's bridge input pump (`io.Copy(ptmx, bridge)` over an `io.Pipe`-backed `Bridge.Read`) blocked indefinitely after `cmd.Wait` + `ptmx.Close`, then raced with the *next* iteration's input goroutine for queued attach-client bytes. The leaked goroutine would consume bytes, write them to a closed ptmx, fail, and silently lose them. Symptom against the original code: post-restart `"post-restart-XXXXXXXX\n"` arrived at the test as `"restart-XXXXXXXX\n"` — a 5-byte prefix consumed by the leak. **Production fix shipped in this ticket:** `*supervisor.Bridge` rewritten to use `chan []byte` + per-iteration cancel signal (`BeginIteration` / `EndIteration`); `runOnce` brackets the iteration and waits for both `io.Copy` goroutines to drain (was: one-of-two with a 250ms timeout). Net: ~140 production LOC across `bridge.go` (+124) and `supervisor.go:runOnce` (+18). See [ADR 007](knowledge/decisions/007-bridge-iteration-boundaries.md).
- **`TestHelperProcess` `echo` mode extended (#125 sibling) — startup marker + two control lines.** On startup emits `PYRY_E2E_STARTED pid=<pid>\n` once before reading any input — two distinct PIDs prove the supervisor restarted the helper. `__EXIT__\n` exits non-zero before echoing (drives the supervised crash); `__PID__\n` re-emits the marker without echoing the probe. The probe gates around a subtle race: the *first* startup marker writes before the attach client connects, so the bridge's `Write` discards it (no attached output sink). The probe captures pid1 deterministically once the attach is wired. Body is line-buffered (per-byte scan, `\n`-terminated branch on `string(line)`); preserves byte-exact contract for #125's round-trip test.
- **`-pyry-resume=false` on the attach harness daemon spawn.** `Config.ResumeLast` defaults to true, prepending `--continue` on every respawn after the first. The e2e helper is a Go test binary (`-test.run=TestHelperProcess`); it doesn't recognise `--continue` and exits with a flag-parse error on the first respawn. The fix is a one-line addition in `spawnAttachableDaemon`. #125 and #127 didn't need it because they never restarted the child.
- **`os.MkdirTemp` HOME for sun_path budget — three callers now.** `TestE2E_Attach_SurvivesClaudeRestart` is a long test name; `t.TempDir()` would push `<home>/pyry.sock` past macOS's 104-byte limit. `StartAttach` now allocates HOME via `os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-at-*")` + `t.Cleanup(os.RemoveAll)` — third occurrence of the pattern (after #106's restart tests and #123's rotation primitive). Existing `TestE2E_Attach_RoundTripsBytes` and #127's detach test benefit transparently.
- **`readStartupMarker` — file-local helper, regex-match shape.** Same caller-side timeout pattern as `readUntilContains` (PTY master fds on darwin reject `SetReadDeadline`, so timeouts run in user space via `time.After`). Reads in a goroutine, accumulates into `seen []byte`, matches `regexp.MustCompile(\`PYRY_E2E_STARTED pid=(\d+)\n\`)`. Reader goroutine left running on timeout is drained by the harness's teardown closing `Master`. ~40 LOC; not lifted to public surface — single-file consumer, not yet a pattern.
- **Production diff is NOT zero (this ticket is the exception).** ~140 LOC of supervisor / bridge production code + 5 LOC of `lessons.md`. Test diff: ~190 LOC across `attach_pty.go` (+12), `attach_pty_test.go` (+58), and `attach_restart_test.go` (+123 new file). The fix is the ticket's primary deliverable; the test is what surfaced it and what guarantees it stays fixed.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Attach Restart Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/decisions/007-bridge-iteration-boundaries.md](knowledge/decisions/007-bridge-iteration-boundaries.md), `lessons.md § Bridge input pump must be scoped per-iteration to survive child restart`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #120)
- **`internal/e2e/rotation_test.go` — `TestE2E_RotationWatcher_DetectsClear`.** Closes the binary-boundary gap on Phase 1.2b-B's live `/clear` rotation watcher (#39). Drives a real `pyry` daemon through one rotation against the real platform probe (`/proc/<pid>/fd` on Linux, `lsof` on macOS) using #122's `fakeclaude` binary via #123's `StartRotation` primitive — production code (watcher, real probe, `Pool.RotateID`, `saveLocked`, `reconcileBootstrapOnNew`) exercised exactly as it ships; only the supervised child is replaced. Pre-creates `<initialUUID>.jsonl` in the encoded sessions dir → `StartRotation` (reconcile rotates bootstrap to `initialUUID` synchronously inside `Pool.New`, before the readiness gate) → poll registry until bootstrap id == `initialUUID` (5s deadline, 25ms cadence) → drop trigger → poll until id changes → assert UUIDv4 stem + `lastActiveAt` strictly advances + 200ms-sleep re-read still shows the new id. Build tag `//go:build e2e`; default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- **No harness changes.** All primitives needed already shipped in #122 (fakeclaude binary) and #123 (`StartRotation` + `ClaudeSessionsDir` field + fake-claude env wiring). #120 is a pure consumer ticket — single new file, ~155 LOC. The "always split new package + first consumer" pattern (#122 → #123 → #120) keeps each slice's AC count inside budget; the original combined ticket (#55, #119) hit `max_turns` twice.
- **Local one-liner copies of two unexported helpers — `encodeWorkdir` and `uuidStemPattern`.** `internal/sessions.encodeWorkdir` (replaces `/` AND `.` with `-` — naive `/`→`-` silently looks in the wrong dir; doubled dash for paths under `.pyrycode-worktrees`) and `internal/sessions/rotation.uuidStemPattern` are unexported. The test file copies each verbatim rather than reaching into the package or adding test-only exported accessors. Spec explicitly recommended this; review confirmed it.
- **Pre-create the initial JSONL before `StartRotation`, not from inside fakeclaude.** `reconcileBootstrapOnNew` runs synchronously inside `Pool.New`, before the control socket starts listening. Pre-creating `<initialUUID>.jsonl` makes "registry reflects initialUUID" deterministic by the time `StartRotation` returns; otherwise fakeclaude's first open races pyry startup and reconcile may see an empty dir. fakeclaude opens with `O_APPEND|O_CREATE`, so writing to an already-existing file is harmless.
- **Poll the registry, not the JSONL dir or trigger file.** The registry write is the production-side observable this test exists to verify. `readBootstrapIfPresent` treats "file missing, parse error, no bootstrap entry" as keep-polling (first iteration may fire before `RotateID → saveLocked` produced the file; `saveRegistryLocked`'s temp+rename makes torn reads unreachable in practice). 25ms cadence × 5s = 200 reads — well within budget.
- **AC#3 (`pyry list`) intentionally skipped.** The verb does not exist in `cmd/pyry/main.go` (`pyry sessions list` is tracked in #87 / #88, not yet shipped under that single-word form). Adding it would be a production change forbidden by the ticket. The on-disk registry assertions (AC#1/#2) already exercise every link in the chain end-to-end against the real probe; the control-plane re-check naturally lives in the e2e test for `pyry sessions list` itself once that ships. In-file comment references the architect's spec at `docs/specs/architecture/120-e2e-clear-rotation-watcher.md`.
- **5s deadline = ~10× headroom.** Watcher worst case is `probeRetryDelays {0, 50ms, 200ms}` ≈ 250ms + fsnotify (<50ms) + `saveLocked` rename (<10ms) + fakeclaude 50ms trigger poll — round trip well under 500ms. Same "generous safety net, not steady-state expectation" tradeoff as the rest of the e2e suite.
- **Failure-mode visibility.** Every failure (reconcile misses initial jsonl, watcher misses CREATE, probe path mismatch, `RotateID` errors, fakeclaude misses trigger, stray second rotation) surfaces as a deterministic timeout with the latest registry contents printed via `mustReadFile`. No silent passes possible.
- **Supplements `TestPool_Run_StartsWatcher`; retirement deferred.** The unit test at `internal/sessions/pool_test.go:785` substitutes the real probe with a `dirProbe` test double and has been observed flaky under `-count=N` (2026-05-02). #120 closes the binary-boundary gap; retiring the unit is a follow-up contingent on multiple stable CI invocations of this e2e replacement.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~155 LOC, single new file.** Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Rotation Watcher Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md § Testing](knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #123)
- **`Harness.StartRotation(t, home, sessionsDir, initialUUID, trigger) *Harness` — wires the #122 fake-claude binary as pyry's supervised child.** Builds pyry, builds fakeclaude (`ensureFakeClaudeBuilt` mirrors `ensurePyryBuilt`: `sync.Once` + `os.MkdirTemp`-cached binary, `PYRY_E2E_FAKE_CLAUDE_BIN` short-circuit for CI prebuild), `os.MkdirAll(sessionsDir, 0o700)`, and spawns pyry with `-pyry-claude=<fakeBin>`, `-pyry-workdir=<home>`, and the three `PYRY_FAKE_CLAUDE_*` env vars set on `cmd.Env`. The supervisor inherits them via `os.Environ()` (`internal/supervisor/supervisor.go:234`) and propagates them to the supervised PTY child unchanged — no `helperEnv` knob, no supervisor changes. New `Harness.ClaudeSessionsDir` field is populated to `sessionsDir`; left empty for `Start` / `StartIn`. Ten exported names now (was nine). Used today only by `TestE2E_StartRotation_PrimitiveWiresFakeClaude`; the next consumer ticket drives pyry's rotation watcher against this primitive.
- **Internal refactor: `spawn` is now a thin wrapper over a shared `spawnWith(t, home, spawnOpts)` core.** `spawnOpts{claudeBin, claudeArgs, extraEnv, extraFlags}` zero-value reproduces the historical `/bin/sleep 99999` shape, so `spawn(t, home, extraFlags...)` becomes a one-liner; `StartRotation` populates `spawnOpts` to swap in fake-claude + the three env vars. Existing call sites (`StartIn`, `StartExpectingFailureIn`) untouched. `spawnOpts` is unexported — generalises cleanly when a third caller appears, without committing to a public-surface shape today. The ticket body offered `spawnRotation` as a sibling alternative; the architect chose `spawnWith` for the shared-core path.
- **`-pyry-workdir=<home>` pinned on the rotation spawn.** Without it, pyry's supervisor inherits the test process's cwd; `home` keeps the test's view of the supervised child's rooted-at directory aligned with pyry's. Flag exists today (`cmd/pyry/main.go:174-180`); no production change.
- **`TestE2E_StartRotation_PrimitiveWiresFakeClaude` — primitive-only smoke test, deliberately does NOT touch `internal/sessions/rotation`.** `//go:build e2e` in `internal/e2e/fakeclaude_test.go`. Phases: `StartRotation` → assert `h.ClaudeSessionsDir == sessionsDir` → poll (5s deadline, 50ms gap) for `<sessionsDir>/<initialUUID>.jsonl` → drop trigger via `os.WriteFile(trigger, nil, 0o600)` → poll for a *different* `<uuid>.jsonl` (matching the canonical v4 stem regex) in the same dir → assert `os.Stat(rotated).Size() > 0` (combined with #122's strict close-OLD-before-open-NEW invariant, implies the initial fd is no longer being written). No assertion about pyry's session registry, no `/proc/<pid>/fd` probe, no watcher driving — that's the next consumer ticket. When the consumer fails, it fails for one reason at a time.
- **`os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-fc-*")` over `t.TempDir()` for HOME — same `sun_path` budget rationale as the restart tests.** `TestE2E_StartRotation_PrimitiveWiresFakeClaude` is a long test name; `t.TempDir()` would push `<home>/pyry.sock` past macOS's 104-byte limit. `os.MkdirTemp` + `t.Cleanup(os.RemoveAll)` keeps the prefix tiny.
- **Always-split "new package AND its first consumer" pattern continues.** #122 shipped the binary in isolation; #123 wires it into the harness; the rotation-watcher driver test is the next slice. The original combined ticket (#55, then #119) hit AC-count and "and"-in-title red lines on every recovery attempt — three split slices keep each AC count inside budget.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~130 LOC across 2 files** (`harness.go`: ~85 for `StartRotation` + `ensureFakeClaudeBuilt` + `spawnWith` extraction + `ClaudeSessionsDir` field; `fakeclaude_test.go`: ~105 new file). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Rotation Primitive](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/fakeclaude-binary.md](knowledge/features/fakeclaude-binary.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #122)
- **`internal/e2e/internal/fakeclaude/main.go` — test-only `package main` that mimics claude's on-disk fd behaviour for rotation tests.** Opens `<dir>/<initialUUID>.jsonl` (`O_WRONLY|O_APPEND|O_CREATE 0o600`, `WriteString("{}\n")`, `Sync()`), then polls a trigger file every 50ms. On first appearance: closes the OLD fd, mints `uuidV4()`, opens `<dir>/<newU>.jsonl` (write+fsync), removes the trigger, idles forever. Subsequent triggers ignored via a `rotated bool` guard. SIGTERM kills via Go's runtime default (no signal handler); the OS auto-closes the fd. ~90 LOC, env-only configuration (`PYRY_FAKE_CLAUDE_SESSIONS_DIR` / `_INITIAL_UUID` / `_TRIGGER`) — no flags, no stdin. Inline `uuidV4()` mirrors `internal/sessions/id.go` byte-for-byte to avoid pulling production surface into a test binary for one function.
- **Strict close-OLD-before-open-NEW order is the load-bearing invariant.** What makes the *consumer* slice's exact-match probe check (`watcher.go:167`) deterministic: at the instant the watcher's CREATE-driven probe runs, only the new path is on the PID's fd table. If the binary kept both fds open across the rotation, the probe could match either path and the watcher's gate would race. Order enforced by code review of `main.go` (one `f.Close()` line, then one `openSession`); not directly observable from the in-isolation test (would race the 50ms poll).
- **`internal/e2e/internal/fakeclaude/main_test.go` — single test, `//go:build e2e`, exercises the binary end-to-end without the harness or pyry.** `go build`s into `t.TempDir()`, `exec`s with the env vars set, polls until the initial JSONL appears (3s deadline), drops the trigger, polls until a fresh `<uuid>.jsonl` appears in the same dir whose stem matches `uuidStemPattern` and isn't the initial UUID, asserts the trigger is gone, sends SIGTERM, asserts `WaitStatus.Signaled() && Signal()==SIGTERM` within 3s. Hermetic — no network, no writes outside tmp; defensive `t.Cleanup` SIGKILLs on early-fatal so a leaked process doesn't survive the test holding an fd in the now-deleted tmp dir.
- **`internal/e2e/internal/` nesting visibility-fences the binary** so only e2e-package code can import it. Mostly moot for `package main`, but the path signals intent. The binary itself has **no** build tag — a tiny `package main` is essentially free to compile under `./...`, and not gating it means the test (and the next-ticket harness) can `go build` it without `-tags`. The *test* is gated by `e2e` so default `go test ./...` doesn't pay the build cost.
- **Always-split "new package AND its first consumer" pattern.** The harness consumer (`Harness.StartRotation`, `Harness.ClaudeSessionsDir`, `ensureFakeClaudeBuilt`) is the next ticket; the rotation-watcher driver test is the one after that. The original combined ticket (#55, then #119) hit AC-count and "and"-in-title red lines on every recovery attempt. Mirrors the introduce-then-rewire slicing pattern (#28 → #29).
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~215 LOC, two new files** (`main.go` ~90 + `main_test.go` ~125). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/fakeclaude-binary.md](knowledge/features/fakeclaude-binary.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #115)
- **`internal/e2e/idle_test.go` — `TestE2E_IdleEviction_EvictsBootstrap` + `TestE2E_IdleEviction_LazyRespawn`.** Two tests under `//go:build e2e` close the binary-boundary gap on Phase 1.2c-A's idle-eviction state machine and lazy respawn (#40). Idle eviction itself is exercised today only by package-level integration tests in `internal/sessions/` against in-process pool primitives — neither the assembled `pyry` binary, the real on-disk `sessions.json`, nor the control-plane Activate-before-Attach call are exercised. #115 adds: (1) start pyry with `-pyry-idle-timeout=1s`, poll the registry file for the bootstrap entry's `lifecycle_state == "evicted"`, cross-check via `pyry status` (asserts negation: NOT `Phase: running`); (2) after eviction, dial the control socket directly and issue a raw `VerbAttach` (importing `internal/control`'s public types), assert the session returns to active and the supervisor reaches `Phase: running` while the conn is held open.
- **Variadic `extraFlags ...string` on `spawn` and `StartIn`.** The minimal harness extension AC#4 asks for. The standard flag set is built into a slice, `extraFlags` are appended, then `--` and the claude args. Go's `flag` package is left-to-right last-wins, so a caller passing `-pyry-idle-timeout=1s` overrides the harness default `=0`. Existing call sites (`Start(t)`, `StartIn(t, home)`, three restart tests, the corrupt-registry and missing-projects-dir tests) all unchanged — variadic is backwards-compatible at every site. `StartExpectingFailureIn` was deliberately *not* extended (no failed-start test in #115 needs flags; one-line change when one does). No new exported names; net public API delta is zero.
- **Raw `VerbAttach` over `pyry attach` as a subprocess.** Determinism. `pyry attach` enters a stdin-byte loop (`copyWithEscape`) requiring careful pipe management to keep the conn alive while assertions run; closing stdin too early ends the attach before the next idle eviction fires. A `net.Dial("unix", ...)` + `json.NewEncoder.Encode(control.Request{Verb: VerbAttach, Attach: ...})` + `defer conn.Close()` lets the test own the timeline exactly. The control protocol's `Request` / `Response` / `AttachPayload` types are public on `internal/control`; importing them from `internal/e2e` is in-module and intended.
- **Sleep arg flipped from `infinity` → `99999`.** Pre-#115 the harness passed `infinity` to `/bin/sleep`. GNU coreutils accepts it; macOS BSD sleep does not — exits immediately with the usage banner. Tests that don't depend on the supervised child surviving (`TestStatus_E2E`, the restart suite, etc.) didn't notice — readiness gates on the control socket, not the child. Lazy respawn surfaces it: the test waits for `Phase: running` after a respawn, but if the child exits immediately the supervisor enters perpetual backoff and `Phase: running` is never observed. `99999` (a plain integer in seconds, ~27h) is portable across both Linux GNU sleep and macOS BSD sleep — the only argv form that actually works on both. New lessons.md entry: § Test helpers across packages, third bullet.
- **Poll registry first, `pyry status` as cross-check.** The registry is the load-bearing AC ("registry state observable"); `pyry status` is the cross-check, asserting *negation* (`!Contains "Phase:         running"`) so the test isn't coupled to which non-running phase shows up (`PhaseStopped` today, sibling tomorrow). The new file-local `waitForBootstrapState` helper polls the registry for `"evicted"` or `"active"` (the active arm tolerates either an empty/missing field — today's `omitempty` default — or the literal string, decoupling the test from a future toggle that writes the field explicitly).
- **Hold the conn open across the assertion phase.** `handleAttach` writes the OK ack and binds the bridge to the conn; the conn now streams PTY bytes from `/bin/sleep 99999` (which writes nothing) and back. The test never reads after the ack — `defer conn.Close()` keeps `attached > 0` so the next idle eviction is deferred while the assertions run; bridge teardown fires server-side on test return.
- **Production diff is zero.** `-pyry-idle-timeout` already existed (`cmd/pyry/main.go:257`); the state machine, persistence, and Activate-before-Attach all shipped in #40. Test diff: ~125 LOC in `idle_test.go` plus the variadic-flags signature change in `harness.go` (~10 LOC). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Idle-Eviction + Lazy-Respawn Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md § Testing](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), `lessons.md § Test helpers across packages`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #125)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_pty.go` + `attach_pty_test.go` — PTY-simulation harness for `pyry attach` + first round-trip-bytes test.** Sibling to the existing daemon `Harness` in the same package and build tag (`e2e || e2e_install` for the harness, `e2e` for the test). New `AttachHarness` struct + `StartAttach(t *testing.T, sessionID string) *AttachHarness` constructor owns three OS resources: (1) a `pyry` daemon spawned in bridge mode whose `-pyry-claude=os.Args[0]` re-execs the e2e test binary as `TestHelperProcess` in echo mode (`GO_TEST_HELPER_PROCESS=1` + `GO_TEST_HELPER_MODE=echo`); (2) a `creack/pty` master/slave pair (`pty.Open` is the skip gate — `t.Skip` on failure satisfies AC#5); (3) a `pyry attach` subprocess with `attachCmd.Stdin/Stdout/Stderr = slave` and `SysProcAttr{Setsid: true, Setctty: true}` so the slave is its controlling terminal. `TestE2E_Attach_RoundTripsBytes` writes a nonced payload to `Master`, reads back via `readUntilContains` (5s deadline), pre-payload banner bytes from the attach client are swallowed naturally.
- **Helper "claude" via `TestHelperProcess` re-exec, not a separate binary.** Echo is `term.MakeRaw(0); io.Copy(os.Stdout, os.Stdin)` — one line of meaningful work. The test-binary re-exec pattern (already proven in `internal/supervisor/supervisor_test.go`) is the simplest fit: no second binary to build, no second `internal/e2e/internal/<name>` subdir, no `sync.Once` go-build cache to maintain. Coexists with #122's separate `package main` fakeclaude (rotation behaviour requires a stable build target the harness hands to pyry; echo doesn't). The test binary's `os.Args[0]` is unique per test binary — patterns can't be shared across packages.
- **ECHO must be killed in the helper itself.** Bridge mode does NOT put the supervisor's PTY into raw mode (verified in `internal/supervisor/supervisor.go:226-268`); kernel line discipline runs with default ECHO on. Without `term.MakeRaw(stdin)` in the helper, the kernel reflects every input byte to the master *before* `io.Copy` runs, and the test sees each byte twice. The attach client's existing `term.MakeRaw(slave)` (`internal/control/attach_client.go:68-74`) silences the slave side; the helper's `term.MakeRaw` silences the supervisor's slave (which is the helper's stdin). Two MakeRaw calls, two distinct line disciplines.
- **Daemon env flows through to the supervised helper.** `supervisor.runOnce` does `cmd.Env = append(os.Environ(), s.cfg.helperEnv...)`, so env vars set on the daemon's `cmd.Env` (`GO_TEST_HELPER_PROCESS=1`, `GO_TEST_HELPER_MODE=echo`) reach the helper unchanged. New `lessons.md` entry pinning this contract.
- **Setsid + Setctty so the slave becomes the attach client's controlling terminal.** Without these, the attach client inherits the test process's controlling terminal; `IsTerminal(0)` may return true on the slave fd but kernel writes go to the *test's* tty, not the slave. `Setsid` puts the attach client in a fresh session; `Setctty` makes the slave its tty. Now `term.MakeRaw(slave)` runs against the right fd and the round-trip is deterministic.
- **`SetReadDeadline` does not work on PTY masters on darwin.** The runtime poller reports `ErrNoDeadline` for PTY master fds on macOS, so per-read deadlines via `r.SetReadDeadline(time.Time{...})` cannot enforce the test's overall budget. `readUntilContains` enforces the timeout in the *caller* via `select { case <-readCh: ... case <-time.After(...) }` instead, leaving the reader goroutine running on timeout — the harness's teardown closes `Master`, which unblocks the `Read` with EOF. New `lessons.md` entry: § PTY master fds on darwin do not support SetReadDeadline.
- **Cleanup ordering: master → slave → SIGTERM attach → SIGTERM daemon → socket remove → term.Restore.** The harness's slave fd and the slave fds dup'd into `attachCmd.Stdin/Stdout/Stderr` are independent — closing the harness's slave does NOT SIGHUP the attach client. The kill sequence does that explicitly. `killSpawned` from `harness.go` is reused. `term.Restore` on the parent's stdin state is defensive only (no path in this harness mutates it; AC#4 requires the safety net). Idempotent via `sync.Once`.
- **Skip-on-no-PTY at `pty.Open`, not at `IsTerminal(os.Stdin)`.** Some hosts (sandboxed CI, minimal containers) lack a usable `/dev/ptmx`; `pty.Open` exercises that gate directly. GitHub Actions `ubuntu-latest` lacks a *controlling* terminal but `pty.Open` works (see `lessons.md § PTY Testing`). Probing before spawning the daemon avoids a spawn-then-skip-then-teardown round-trip.
- **`SocketPath` exposed for follow-up tickets.** Field is public so #127's clean-detach test can drive a second `pyry attach` against an already-bound bridge to assert `ErrBridgeBusy`. The current test attaches to the bootstrap session (`sessionID == ""`) — the only session this harness creates. Fresh-session creation deferred until a follow-up needs it.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~351 LOC, two new files** (`attach_pty.go` ~232, `attach_pty_test.go` ~119). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Attach PTY Harness Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), `lessons.md § PTY master fds on darwin do not support SetReadDeadline`, `lessons.md § Daemon env flows through to the supervised child via supervisor.runOnce`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #127)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_detach_test.go` — `TestE2E_Attach_DetachesCleanly` proves the triple invariant of `Ctrl-B d` detach at the binary boundary.** Build tag `e2e`. Builds on #125's `AttachHarness`: writes bytes `0x02 0x64` into the PTY master, then asserts (1) the attach client exits 0 within a 5s deadline, (2) the daemon survives (`pyry status` against the same socket exits 0), (3) the supervised child is still alive (`pyry status` stdout contains the literal `Phase:         running` — multi-space gap is significant; mirrors `idle_test.go`).
- **Two new methods on the existing `*AttachHarness` (`internal/e2e/attach_pty.go`, +32 LOC).** No new exported types, no new fields. `WaitDetach(t, timeout) int` blocks on the existing `attachDone` channel (closed by the wait goroutine after `attachCmd.Wait()` returns), reads `attachCmd.ProcessState.ExitCode()`, `t.Fatalf`s on timeout. `AttachHarness.Run(t, verb, args...) RunResult` mirrors `Harness.Run` against the attach harness's own `SocketPath` + `HomeDir`.
- **`runVerb` extracted as the shared body of `Harness.Run` and `AttachHarness.Run` (`internal/e2e/harness.go`, ~12 LOC of motion).** Package-private free function; both methods become 2-line wrappers (`return runVerb(t, h.SocketPath, h.HomeDir, verb, args...)`). `Harness.Run` had no callers outside the harness package, so the rename is private and `gofmt`-clean. Behaviour for existing `Harness.Run` callers is unchanged.
- **Master-drain goroutine in the test, not the harness.** `pyry attach`'s post-detach stderr write (`fmt.Fprintln(os.Stderr, "pyry: detached.")` with `cmd.Stderr = slave`) goes through the kernel PTY into the master buffer; with no consumer the buffer fills and the slave write blocks, so the attach client never returns from `runAttach` and `cmd.Wait()` never fires. The fix is one anonymous goroutine in the test that loops `Master.Read` until EOF (teardown closes Master, Read errors out, goroutine returns). The #125 round-trip test got away without one because `readUntilContains` consumed the master continuously through the assertion phase. Documented in `lessons.md § PTY master backpressure stalls slave-side process exit`.
- **Channel close as the happens-before edge for `ProcessState`.** `attachDone` is closed exactly once by the wait goroutine in `StartAttach` (`attach_pty.go:120-124`), after `attachCmd.Wait()` returns. After the receive on `attachDone`, reads of `attachCmd.ProcessState` from the test goroutine see the writes performed by `Wait()` in the closing goroutine — no extra locking. Subsequent calls to `WaitDetach` return the same exit code (channel stays closed; ProcessState stays set).
- **Generous 5s timeout is a safety net, not a steady-state expectation.** Steady-state detach is single-digit ms (no I/O between `Ctrl-B d` recognition and process exit). The budget gives 1–2 orders of magnitude of headroom; a tight deadline would convert scheduler jitter into intermittent failures without catching real regressions earlier.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~99 LOC across two files** (`attach_detach_test.go` ~55, `attach_pty.go` +32, `harness.go` shared-body refactor ~12). `pyry attach`, `control.Attach`'s prefix-key state machine, and the detach handshake all shipped pre-#127.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § Attach Detach Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), `lessons.md § PTY master backpressure stalls slave-side process exit`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #112)
- **`internal/e2e/startup_test.go` extended with `TestE2E_Startup_MissingClaudeProjectsDir`.** Positive-outcome sibling of #111's corrupt-registry test, same file, opposite verdict. Asserts the binary-boundary contract for the first-run case: a `HOME` whose `.claude/projects/` does not exist must produce a daemon that comes up cleanly, answers `pyry status` with exit 0, and shuts down via `Stop` without error. The `MissingDir` branch in `internal/sessions/pool.go` already swallows `os.Stat` returning `fs.ErrNotExist`; this ticket pins it at the assembled-binary level (was unit-only).
- **No harness changes — uses `StartIn` + `os.MkdirTemp`, not `Start(t)`.** `Start(t)` would suffice in principle (a fresh `t.TempDir()` HOME has no `.claude/projects/` by construction). Two reasons to use `StartIn(t, home)` with `os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-mp-*")` + `t.Cleanup(os.RemoveAll)` instead: (1) `sun_path` budget — the long test name overflows macOS's 104-byte socket-path limit when embedded into `t.TempDir()`'s path (same lesson as the restart tests); (2) structural parity with the failed-start sibling next door, which already uses `os.MkdirTemp` for the same reason. Net public API delta: zero.
- **Sanity check on the missing dir before spawning.** Three lines (`os.Stat` + `errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist)`) before `StartIn` to guarantee the test premise: if a future harness change pre-creates `.claude/projects/`, this test fails loudly instead of silently passing on a different code path than the one it claims to cover. Cheap insurance.
- **Explicit `h.Stop(t)` despite `t.Cleanup`.** `StartIn` registers teardown via `t.Cleanup`, which handles process liveness and socket removal. But cleanup runs after the test function returns, so any `t.Logf` about a stuck shutdown gets attributed "after the test." Calling `h.Stop(t)` inside the test body makes "shuts down cleanly" a verdict-bearing step. `cleanupOnce` (existing `sync.Once`) makes this idempotent — second fire is a no-op.
- **No log-line assertion on the missing-dir no-op.** Production may or may not log it; either is fine, and tying the test to a specific line would lock production into emitting it. Per ticket guidance, the contract is "comes up, is responsive, shuts down," not "logs X."
- **Why not a table-driven combination with the corrupt-registry test.** The two startup tests assert opposite outcomes (ready+responsive vs. exit-before-ready), use different harness entry points (`StartIn` vs. `StartExpectingFailureIn`), and return different types (`*Harness` vs. `RunResult`). A table that switches on outcome shape is more code than two flat tests. Keep them flat.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~25 LOC, single file** (`internal/e2e/startup_test.go`: one new test). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md § `startup_test.go` — `TestE2E_Startup_MissingClaudeProjectsDir`](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (supervisor fix, ticket #78)
- **Foreground-mode stdin reader leak fixed** — `runOnce` now opens `/dev/tty` (`os.O_RDONLY|syscall.O_NONBLOCK`) as a side fd for the input bridge instead of reading `os.Stdin`. On child exit, the per-cycle `input.Close()` wakes the in-flight `Read` via the Go runtime poller; the goroutine drains; nothing accumulates on `os.Stdin`'s `fdMutex`. Drain semantics flip from "drain one of two with timeout" to "drain both with timeout"; total worst-case `runOnce` return latency is `2 × goroutineDrainTimeout` (~200ms). Bridge-mode branch (`Config.Bridge != nil`) is unchanged.
- **`openTTYInput` + `stdinFallback`** — unexported, internal to `internal/supervisor`. Fallback path (`stdinFallback{}` — `Read` from `os.Stdin`, no-op `Close`) is taken when `/dev/tty` cannot be opened (headless containers, etc.); preserves the legacy leak in that environment by design rather than breaking the process by closing `os.Stdin`. Foreground mode is TTY-only by construction (`term.MakeRaw(stdinFd)` already early-returns on a non-TTY), so the fallback is a defensive seam, not the production path.
- **Why O_NONBLOCK is load-bearing.** Plain `os.OpenFile("/dev/tty", os.O_RDONLY, 0)` produces a blocking fd; `internal/poll.(*FD).Read` calls `syscall.Read` directly and parks in the kernel, where POSIX `close(2)` on another goroutine is a no-op for the in-flight read. With `O_NONBLOCK`, `Read` returns `EAGAIN`, the runtime parks the goroutine on the poller, and `Close` calls `runtime_pollUnblock` to wake it with `os.ErrClosed`. Drop the flag and the leak comes back.
- **Targeted test** — `TestSupervisor_Foreground_NoStdinReaderLeak` runs ~3 child-restart cycles and asserts `runtime.NumGoroutine()` does not grow by more than 2; skips with `t.Skipf("no controlling tty: %v", err)` when `/dev/tty` cannot be opened (CI without a TTY). Verified clean under `go test -race -count=20`.
- **Unblocks the flake stack.** The leak was the root cause of `TestPool_ActiveCap_RaceConcurrentActivate` deadlock (#41), `TestPool_Run_StartsWatcher` flake (#39), and `TestPool_New_Reconciles_ColdStart_PicksNewestImmediately` flake (#73). Bridge-mode-fixture migration in session tests is now belt-and-suspenders rather than required.

### Codebase (Phase 1.1e-D, ticket #102)
- **`pyry attach [<id>]` CLI positional + help text** — the operator-facing CLI surface for Phase 1.1e multi-session attach. `pyry attach` (no args) is byte-identical to v0.5.x: empty `SessionID` flows through `omitempty` → server's `Pool.ResolveID` resolves to bootstrap. `pyry attach <full-uuid>` and `pyry attach <prefix>` pass the selector verbatim through `AttachPayload.SessionID`; full-UUID and unique-prefix both attach. Ambiguous prefix / unknown id / `ErrBridgeBusy` / daemon-not-running propagate the existing wire-string error to stderr with exit 1; extra positionals (`pyry attach a b`) emit a usage line and `os.Exit(2)`. Closes Phase 1.1e end-to-end CLI surface.
- **`parseClientFlags` returns `rest []string`.** The shared CLI helper now surfaces `fs.Args()` as a third return so `runAttach` can read the post-flag positional. `runStatus` / `runLogs` / `runStop` bind to `_` — same silent-ignore-of-stray-positionals behaviour as Phase 0; opportunistic "reject extra args" for sibling verbs intentionally deferred (out of scope per AC).
- **`attachSelectorFromArgs(rest []string) (string, error)` unit-testable seam.** Empty rest → `""`; one arg → verbatim; >1 → `errTooManyAttachArgs`. Lets the table test cover the argument-shape rule without intercepting `os.Exit(2)`. The exit lives inline in `runAttach` — matches the file convention that runtime errors return up (exit 1) and usage errors exit directly (exit 2) so the two failure classes stay visually distinct.
- **`control.Attach` extended in place from `(ctx, socketPath, cols, rows)` to `(ctx, socketPath, cols, rows, sessionID)`.** Single external caller — adding a sibling `AttachWithID` would split the call surface for no benefit. Empty `sessionID` produces `AttachPayload{Cols, Rows, SessionID:""}` which under `omitempty` (1.1e-C's load-bearing decision) marshals to `{"cols":80,"rows":24}` — byte-identical to Phase 0. Pinned by `TestAttach_WireBackCompat_EmptySessionID` from #101.
- **No prefix matching, UUID parsing, or trimming on the client side.** The CLI is transport, not lint. `pyry attach " "` reaches the server's `Pool.ResolveID` which responds `ErrSessionNotFound`. Reviewer regression guard: `grep -rn 'HasPrefix\|uuid.Parse' cmd/pyry/ internal/control/attach_client.go` should be empty.
- **Production diff ~30 LOC across 2 files** (`cmd/pyry/main.go`: helper signature, new `attachSelectorFromArgs`, `runAttach` body, help text; `internal/control/attach_client.go`: signature + payload field). Tests carry the bulk: `args_test.go` extends with `TestParseClientFlags_ReturnsRest`; `internal/control/attach_test.go` gains `TestAttach_PassesSessionID_OnWire` proving no-arg / full-UUID / unique-prefix all reach the server with the expected `AttachPayload.SessionID`.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Attach: CLI Surface](knowledge/features/control-plane.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1e-C, ticket #101)
- **`AttachPayload.SessionID string` (`json:"sessionID,omitempty"`) + `handleAttach` routes via `Pool.ResolveID`** — wire + server half of Phase 1.1e multi-session attach. `omitempty` is load-bearing: empty-`SessionID` payloads marshal byte-identically to v0.5.x output (`{"cols":80,"rows":24}`), so a v0.5.x client keeps working against a v0.7.x server during the rollover. `handleAttach` resolves `req.Attach.SessionID` through `Pool.ResolveID` BEFORE any bridge work, then re-fetches the session via `Pool.Lookup`. `nil req.Attach` is treated identically to empty `SessionID` — both resolve to bootstrap. CLI surface (`pyry attach <id>`) intentionally deferred to 1.1e-D; the new field is reachable only via hand-crafted JSON or the test harness this slice.
- **`SessionResolver` interface gained `ResolveID(arg string) (sessions.SessionID, error)`.** Three implementations updated with 1-line passthroughs: `cmd/pyry/main.go` `poolResolver`, plus `fakeResolver` and `recordingResolver` in `internal/control/server_test.go`. No other call sites consume `SessionResolver` (verified by grep across `internal/control` and `cmd/pyry`).
- **Two-step ResolveID-then-Lookup, two sequential RLocks.** Honours #66's choice to return `SessionID` (not `*Session`) — the second `Lookup` is the lock-clean guard against a session being removed between resolve and use. Race window is microseconds; `Lookup` returns `ErrSessionNotFound`, which encodes to the same `"attach: sessions: session not found"` wire string the resolver itself produces — identical operator diagnostic. No new locking; concurrent attaches against different sessions remain fully parallel.
- **Errors encode as `"attach: <err>"` verbatim via `fmt.Sprintf("%v", err)`.** `ErrSessionNotFound` → `"attach: sessions: session not found"`; `ErrAmbiguousSessionID` flows through with its full multi-line `<uuid> (<label>)` match list. Bridge state is **untouched** on the error path — `ResolveID` and `Lookup` both return before `conn.SetDeadline(time.Time{})`, before `Activate`, before `Attach`. Asserted in tests via `fakeSession.attachCalls == 0`, not just response-string match. Existing `sessions.ErrAttachUnavailable` mapping (foreground-mode wire string) untouched — runs after `Attach`, no collision with the new error encoding.
- **Production diff ~10 LOC across 3 files** (`protocol.go`: one field; `server.go`: interface method + dispatcher pass-through + handler swap; `cmd/pyry/main.go`: 3-line resolver passthrough). Tests carry the bulk: `attach_resolve_test.go` (~400 LOC) covers all five AC cases plus the v0.5.x byte-identical baseline.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Attach: ResolveID-then-Lookup](knowledge/features/control-plane.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1e-A, ticket #66)
- **`Pool.ResolveID(arg string) (SessionID, error)` prefix resolver + `ErrAmbiguousSessionID` sentinel** — typed loose-input resolver pairing with `Pool.Lookup` (full id only). Empty arg → bootstrap (same seam as `Lookup("")`); exact full-UUID match short-circuits via single map lookup (no extra scan cost beyond the existing lookup); otherwise `strings.HasPrefix` scan over `p.sessions` collects candidates. Zero matches → `ErrSessionNotFound` (reused); unique → that id; ≥2 → `ambiguousError(matches)` returning `fmt.Errorf("%w:\n%s", ErrAmbiguousSessionID, lines)` with each `<uuid> (<label>)` pair on its own line, sorted by `SessionID` asc. The internal seam Phase 1.1e-B's `pyry attach <id>` wire + CLI surface (and any future verb taking a session selector) consumes; 47-B / 48-B may opportunistically refactor onto it when next touched.
- **Sentinel + `fmt.Errorf("%w: …")` over a struct error type.** AC required "no new exported types beyond the new typed error" + "errors.Is matching cheap." Struct error with `Matches []SessionRef` would expose a second exported type and force CLI consumers to type-assert or duplicate the formatting. Sentinel-wrap gives one pointer compare via the wrapped chain and a verbatim-printable message in one syscall — strictly simpler under the AC's exported-surface budget.
- **Synthetic `"bootstrap"` substitution mirrored in the formatter.** When the bootstrap entry's on-disk label is empty, the formatter writes `<uuid> (bootstrap)` rather than `<uuid> ()`. Mirrors `Pool.List`'s rule one-for-one — divergence would surface as operator confusion (`pyry sessions ls` saying one name, the disambiguation prompt saying another) before it surfaced as a bug report. Same precedent as the `List` substitution: substitute at the read primitive, not at the renderer.
- **Pool.mu (RLock) only; no `Session.lcMu`.** Reads `id` (mutated by `RotateID` under `Pool.mu` write — invariant documented at that site) and `label` (mutated by `Pool.Rename` under `Pool.mu` write). Both already in the `Pool.mu`-reader set. `lcState` and `lastActiveAt` are NOT consulted — `ResolveID` does not filter by lifecycle state (an evicted session must still be resolvable for `pyry sessions rename <prefix>` / `pyry sessions rm <prefix>`). Lock-order graph (`Pool.capMu → Pool.mu → Session.lcMu`) unchanged.
- **Returns `SessionID`, not `*Session` / `SessionInfo`.** Smallest possible surface, symmetric with the wire/CLI flow: 1.1e-B unmarshals the id, calls `ResolveID`, then routes to `Lookup`/`Activate`/`Remove` with the resolved id. Returning `*Session` would tempt callers to skip the second lookup — but the second lookup is the lock-clean way to guard against a session being removed between resolve and use. No CLI policies enforced at this layer (no minimum prefix length, no whitespace trimming) — same posture as `Pool.Rename`/`Pool.Create` declining to validate `label`.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md § Pool.ResolveID](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1d-A1, ticket #94)
- **`Pool.Remove(ctx context.Context, id SessionID) error` write primitive + `ErrCannotRemoveBootstrap` sentinel** — terminates a session's claude process and drops its registry entry. The on-disk JSONL is **not** touched (disposition lands in 64-A2 / #95). Bootstrap is rejected via the new sentinel; unknown ids reuse `ErrSessionNotFound`. The internal seam the future `pyry sessions rm` CLI verb (#65) consumes instead of touching processes or `sessions.json` directly.
- **Delete-then-evict ordering is the load-bearing invariant.** `Pool.mu` covers the in-memory `delete(p.sessions, id)` + `saveLocked()`, then is released **before** calling `sess.Evict(ctx)`. The alternative (holding `Pool.mu` across `Evict`) deadlocks: the lifecycle goroutine's `transitionTo` reacquires `Pool.mu` via `Pool.persist`. Releasing `Pool.mu` after the in-memory delete commits is safe — concurrent `Lookup`/`Activate`/`Rename`/`List` callers see the session as gone from that moment on, so no observer can witness a half-removed state and no re-spawn race exists. Same outer-mutex pattern as the cap-policy eviction (#41), here resolved by holding `Pool.mu` only during the cheap mutate phase rather than introducing a new outer lock.
- **Save-failure rollback mirrors `Pool.Rename`.** If `saveLocked` fails after the in-memory delete, restore `p.sessions[id] = sess` before unlocking. Disk and memory remain consistent at every observable point. `saveRegistryLocked`'s temp+rename discipline makes partial writes unreachable; the rollback is belt-and-suspenders for "destination dir vanished" / `ENOSPC`.
- **Termination reuses `Session.Evict`.** `Pool.Remove` does not re-implement SIGTERM/SIGKILL/grace logic — `Session.Evict` already drives the supervisor's child via `exec.CommandContext` cancel ⇒ SIGKILL ⇒ `cmd.Wait` returns. The supervisor today does not have a SIGTERM grace window; SIGKILL is uncatchable, so no fallback path is needed (the AC's "SIGKILL fallback when child ignores SIGTERM" maps to "the existing kill-on-cancel terminates uncooperative children deterministically", verified in `TestPool_Remove_TerminatesUncooperativeChild` with a `trap "" TERM INT HUP; sleep 86400` shell child).
- **Lifecycle goroutine survives until pool shutdown.** After `Pool.Remove` returns, `sess.Run`'s loop transitions to `runEvicted` and parks on `activateCh` / `ctx.Done()`. The session is no longer reachable via `Pool.sessions`, so no caller can signal `activateCh`; the goroutine survives until `Pool.Run`'s `runCtx` cancels at pool shutdown. Bounded resource cost (one orphan goroutine + ~1KB `*Session` per `Remove` per pool lifetime) — operationally invisible for pyrycode's expected workload. Per evidence-based fix selection, no per-session terminate signal until observed.
- **No `Session.lcMu` taken; lock order unchanged.** `Pool.Remove` does not read `lcState` / `lastActiveAt` / `attached`. Lock-order graph (`Pool.capMu → Pool.mu → Session.lcMu`) is unchanged. Empty-id is *not* the bootstrap shorthand it is in `Pool.Lookup` — empty falls through to "not in map" and returns `ErrSessionNotFound`; destructive operations require an explicit id.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md § Pool.Remove](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1d-A2, ticket #95)
- **`Pool.Remove` signature evolves to `(ctx, id, opts RemoveOptions) error` + `JSONLPolicy` enum** (`JSONLLeave` / `JSONLArchive` / `JSONLPurge`). Zero-value `RemoveOptions{}` preserves 1.1d-A1 behaviour byte-for-byte (JSONL untouched). `JSONLArchive` moves the live JSONL into `<pyry-data-dir>/archived-sessions/<uuid>.jsonl` (data-dir = parent of `registryPath`; subdir auto-created; errors wrapping `fs.ErrExist` if destination exists; source-absent is a no-op). `JSONLPurge` deletes the JSONL (source-absent is a no-op). The internal seam the future `pyry sessions rm --archive` / `--purge` CLI surface (#65) consumes.
- **Disposition runs under `Pool.mu` after `saveLocked`.** Single critical section, single observable transition: a concurrent `Pool.List` either sees the session present (registry + JSONL both untouched) or absent (registry + JSONL both at their final state). The held-lock window grows by one stat + one rename or unlink — well inside the existing `saveLocked` envelope. Failure ordering: on `saveLocked` failure the in-memory delete rolls back and the JSONL is untouched; on disposition failure the registry is already committed and `Session.Evict` *still* runs (the registry says the session is gone, the child must follow), with the disposition error returned to the caller — disposition error wins over Evict error.
- **Enum (not two booleans) and options struct (not a positional policy parameter).** The enum makes "exactly one disposition" type-level (zero value well-defined as Leave, switch is exhaustive, no representable-but-illegal `(true, true)`). The struct keeps future fields (`Force`, `Reason`, …) additive at zero call-site churn.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md § Pool.Remove JSONL disposition](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1b-B1, ticket #87)
- **`VerbSessionsList` + `Lister` seam in `internal/control` — wire-only addition that completes the fourth `sessions.*` namespace member and the first read-side member.** New verb `"sessions.list"`; the verb carries **no request payload** (`Request.Sessions` stays nil), so `SessionsPayload` gains no new field — the verb name alone is the dispatch token. Server adds `handleSessionsList`; client `SessionsList(ctx, sock) ([]SessionInfo, error)` mirrors `SessionsRename`'s shape using the `request()` helper. CLI subcommand (`pyry sessions list`) is sibling ticket 61-B; the wire surface is reachable today only via the typed client.
- **`Lister { List() []sessions.SessionInfo }` is the fourth sub-interface embedded into `Sessioner` — `NewServer` signature unchanged.** `*sessions.Pool` already satisfies the embedded shape via `Pool.List` (#60) — no adapter, no `cmd/pyry/main.go` change. Continues the post-#98/#90 pattern: one named per-verb sub-interface embedded into the aggregate `Sessioner` facade rather than a new constructor parameter. `Lister` does NOT take `context.Context` — `Pool.List`'s signature is `() []SessionInfo` and the operation is bounded by `Pool.mu` (RLock) + each `Session.lcMu` briefly; mirroring that shape keeps satisfaction adapter-free (same rationale as `Renamer` in #90).
- **New wire-level `Response.SessionsList *SessionsListPayload` (omitempty) + new wire-level `SessionInfo` struct in `protocol.go`.** `SessionInfo` is defined alongside the verbs rather than re-exporting `sessions.SessionInfo` so external Go callers / future hand-written wire clients don't transitively import `internal/sessions` for the package-private `lifecycleState` enum. Fields: `ID string`, `Label string`, `State string` (`"active"` / `"evicted"`), `LastActive time.Time` (RFC3339Nano on the wire), `Bootstrap bool` (omitempty). `protocol.go` import set gains stdlib `time` only — the "import-free by design" rule from the wire-enums lesson is specifically about not dragging in `internal/sessions`; `time` is fine.
- **No new `ErrorCode` constants.** `Pool.List` does not return errors. The seam's only failure path is the nil-sessioner branch (`"sessions.list: no sessioner configured"`); the typed-sentinel envelope #98 introduced is unused on this verb. The empty-response client guard returns `"control: empty sessions.list response"` for symmetry with `SessionsNew`'s empty-result branch.
- **`State` encoded as a self-documenting string via `lifecycleState.String()` — the same encoding the on-disk registry uses, so wire and registry agree on token spelling without a parallel translation table.** `parseLifecycleState` (the inverse) is NOT exported on the wire; the CLI consumes the string verbatim for display. The translation site is the seam (`handleSessionsList`), not the renderer — the future 61-B renderer receives wire-level types and does not import `internal/sessions`.
- **`LastActive` encoded as `time.Time`, not a pre-formatted string.** Distinct from `StatusPayload`'s pre-formatted "310ms"/"1.5s" durations, which are display-only. `LastActive` is data 61-B's renderer does math on (relative-time formatting needs `time.Now().Sub(...)`); going string would force every consumer to re-parse RFC3339Nano. Marshal/unmarshal via `encoding/json` produces RFC3339Nano on the wire — jq-debuggable, byte-stable. Tests that round-trip `LastActive` MUST use `time.Equal` (not `==` or `reflect.DeepEqual`) per the existing monotonic-clock-stripping lesson.
- **Sort order: pass-through.** The seam returns whatever order `Pool.List` returned (LastActiveAt desc, SessionID asc tiebreak). Final user-facing ordering is 61-B's responsibility; this layer does not re-sort — `TestServer_SessionsList_PreservesPoolOrder` pins the contract by feeding the fake a deliberately out-of-order slice and asserting the wire response preserves it verbatim.
- **Backward-compat: `sessions.new` / `sessions.rm` / `sessions.rename` byte-identical post-`SessionsList` field addition.** `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat` extended from a Request-only table into a (Request | Response) table covering `Response{}`, `Response{OK: true}`, and `Response{SessionsNew: &SessionsNewResult{SessionID: "abc"}}` — the new omitempty `SessionsList` field's tag is the load-bearing invariant under test. The existing Request rows assert the no-payload-for-`sessions.list` shape is byte-stable.
- **Test coverage in `sessions_list_test.go` (~458 LOC).** `fakeSessioner` (in `sessions_new_test.go`) gained a `List` method on the existing struct + a FIFO of canned snapshots + a call counter — no new fake type. Mandatory tests: success (full round-trip with `time.Equal` on `LastActive`); preserves-pool-order (asserts pass-through); nil-Sessioner branch; empty-state (zero entries decode to non-nil empty slice, no error); state encoding (`stateActive` → `"active"`, `stateEvicted` → `"evicted"`); bootstrap omitempty pinning at the marshal layer; extended back-compat byte-equality table; client wire shape (hand-rolled `net.Listen` captures `{"verb":"sessions.list"}\n` exactly — no `Sessions` payload); empty-response-as-error; server-error verbatim propagation.
- **Production diff ~170 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go`: +61 for `VerbSessionsList` + `SessionsListPayload` + wire-level `SessionInfo` + `Response.SessionsList` + stdlib `time` import; `internal/control/server.go`: +78 for `Lister` + `Sessioner` embed + dispatch + `handleSessionsList`; `internal/control/client.go`: +31 for `SessionsList`). Test diff ~500 LOC. CLI surface unchanged; runtime wiring is implicit because `*sessions.Pool` already satisfied the extended `Sessioner` (Pool.List shipped in #60).
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Sessions: list seam (1.1b-B1)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/87-control-sessions-list.md`](specs/architecture/87-control-sessions-list.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1c-B1, ticket #90)
- **`VerbSessionsRename` + `Renamer` seam in `internal/control` — wire-only addition that completes the third `sessions.*` namespace member.** New verb `"sessions.rename"`; `SessionsPayload` extended with one further `omitempty` field `NewLabel` (existing `sessions.new` and `sessions.rm` requests stay byte-identical, pinned by extending `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat` with a `sessions.rm` row). Server adds `handleSessionsRename`; client `SessionsRename(ctx, sock, id, newLabel) error` mirrors `SessionsRm`'s shape using the `request()` helper. CLI subcommand (`pyry sessions rename`) is a sibling ticket (63-B2); the wire surface is reachable today only via the typed client.
- **`Renamer { Rename(id sessions.SessionID, newLabel string) error }` is the third sub-interface embedded into `Sessioner` — `NewServer` signature unchanged.** `*sessions.Pool` already satisfies the embedded shape via `Pool.Rename` (#62) — no adapter, no `cmd/pyry/main.go` change. Continues the post-#98 pattern: one named per-verb sub-interface embedded into the aggregate `Sessioner` facade rather than a new constructor parameter.
- **`Renamer` does NOT take `context.Context`.** `Pool.Rename`'s signature is `(id, newLabel) error` (no ctx — the operation is bounded by a single `Pool.mu` critical section + `saveLocked`). Three options were weighed (seam takes ctx and discards; seam takes ctx with 30s `WithTimeout` and discards; seam mirrors `Pool.Rename`); option three was chosen to keep satisfaction adapter-free and avoid lying about cancellability. `handleSessionsRename` correspondingly skips the 30s `context.WithTimeout` that `handleSessionsNew` / `handleSessionsRm` use; the conn's existing 5s `handshakeTimeout` covers the realistic blocking budget.
- **No new `ErrorCode` constants.** `Pool.Rename`'s only typed sentinel is `ErrSessionNotFound`, already pinned to `ErrCodeSessionNotFound` by #98. The `Response.ErrorCode` envelope and the token are reused verbatim — the intended dividend of #98's wire-error infrastructure landing first.
- **Empty `NewLabel` is forwarded unchanged (clears the label).** Empty `NewLabel` serialises absent (omitempty), the server decodes it as the zero value `""`, and `Pool.Rename` treats `""` as "clear the on-disk label" per #62. No special-casing at any layer. Distinct from `Label` (used by `sessions.new`) at the field level: empty-string semantics differ per verb (sessions.new `""` → store empty, let `List` synthesize "bootstrap"; sessions.rename `""` → deliberate write of empty over a previously non-empty value), and the verb-family-payload pattern keeps per-verb intent explicit at every reading site.
- **Empty `ID` rejected at the handler boundary.** Server-side guard returns `"sessions.rename: missing id"` (no `ErrorCode`). Mirrors `handleSessionsRm`'s missing-ID guard for consistency — passing `""` through to `Pool.Rename` would also work but produces the wrong `ErrorCode` (an empty ID is a malformed-input condition, not a "not found" condition).
- **Test coverage in `sessions_rename_test.go` (~280 LOC).** `fakeSessioner` (in `sessions_new_test.go`) gained one `Rename` method on the existing struct + a `recordedRenames()` helper — no new fake type. Mandatory tests: byte-equality back-compat (extended `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat` with a `sessions.rm` row to assert the new `NewLabel` omitempty tag holds); success path; empty-`NewLabel` forwarding (verifies `""` is forwarded unchanged through wire's omitempty + handler's no-guard path); typed `ErrSessionNotFound` round-trip (asserts `errors.Is` against the bare sentinel); other-pool-error untyped path (`errors.Is` against the typed sentinel returns false); nil-Sessioner branch; missing-ID guard (zero `Rename` calls on fake); wire shape (hand-rolled `net.Listen` captures the JSON line for two `(id, newLabel)` cases including empty-label omitempty); empty-response-as-error.
- **Production diff ~135 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go`: +27 for `VerbSessionsRename` + `SessionsPayload.NewLabel`; `internal/control/server.go`: +76 for `Renamer` + `Sessioner` embed + dispatch + `handleSessionsRename`; `internal/control/client.go`: +32 for `SessionsRename`). Test diff ~313 LOC. CLI surface unchanged.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Sessions: rename seam (1.1c-B1)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/90-control-sessions-rename.md`](specs/architecture/90-control-sessions-rename.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1c-B2a, ticket #92)
- **`pyry sessions rename <id> <new-label>` CLI verb shipped (full UUID only).** Adds one `case "rename":` to `runSessions`, bumps `sessionsVerbList` from `"new, rm"` to `"new, rm, rename"`, updates `printHelp`'s sessions line and the top-level reserved-verb comment to match. Two new helpers in `cmd/pyry/main.go`: `parseSessionsRenameArgs` (flag-parse + arity, two positionals; mirrors `parseSessionsNewArgs`/`parseSessionsRmArgs`) and `runSessionsRename` (parse → `control.SessionsRename`, single typed-error branch). Consumes #90's `sessions.rename` wire and `Renamer` seam; plugs into #76's `runSessions` router. ~73 LOC production, ~72 LOC unit tests, ~163 LOC e2e.
- **The simplest `runSessions<Verb>` so far — no prefix resolution in this slice.** `<id>` is forwarded verbatim to `control.SessionsRename`; AC#4 explicitly forbids prefix support. Non-UUID input falls through to the server's `ErrSessionNotFound` mapping. Rationale: the CLI-side prefix helper (`resolveSessionIDViaList` in #99) is currently a single-caller helper; adding rename as a second caller doesn't yet meet the "rule of three" extraction threshold. The follow-up ergonomic slice (sibling of #99's prefix slot) lifts the helper into shared code when the third caller (`pyry attach <id>` in 1.1e) arrives.
- **One typed-sentinel branch only — no bootstrap-rejection.** `Pool.Rename` (#62) has no bootstrap special-case (renaming the bootstrap is allowed and useful — operators may want to rename it to e.g. "primary"). #90's wire surface only propagates `ErrCodeSessionNotFound` for rename. The matched case prints `no session with id "<id>"` to stderr (no `pyry:` prefix) and `os.Exit(1)`; everything else flows through `fmt.Errorf("sessions rename: %w", err)` to main's top-level `pyry: ` printer. The `<id>` echoed in the message is the operator's input (today identical to canonical UUID; preserves message format when prefix resolution arrives).
- **Empty `<new-label>` is a valid value, not an arity hole.** `parseSessionsRenameArgs` checks `fs.NArg() == 2` (positional count), not "two non-empty values" — so `pyry sessions rename <uuid> ""` parses as `(uuid, "")` and forwards through. `Pool.Rename` treats `""` as "clear the on-disk label" per #62. AC#1 explicitly requires this; no separate `--clear` flag.
- **Exactly 2 positionals (not "≥2"); two-arg shape over `--name` flag.** Three or more positionals is rejected as a usage error so multi-word labels must be quoted: `pyry sessions rename <uuid> "hello world"`.
