Same shape as `git config` / `kubectl label`; prevents silent token loss like `pyry sessions rename <uuid> hello world` discarding `world`. `<old> <new>` mirrors `git mv` / `kubectl rename`; reusing `--name` (the create-time label flag on `pyry sessions new`) on rename would conflate two distinct semantics across verbs.
- **One `errSessionsRenameUsage` sentinel covers every parse-time failure.** Mirrors `errSessionsRmUsage`'s shape exactly. `runSessionsRename` matches with `errors.Is`, exits 2, prints `pyry sessions rename: <wrapped-msg>`. The FlagSet has no flags today — exists for symmetry with `new` and `rm` so a future flag slots in mechanically.
- **No new ADR — design follows #99's verbatim conventions.** Per-verb `flag.NewFlagSet`, usage-sentinel → exit 2, typed-sentinel → AC-prescribed plain-message + exit 1, other errors flow through `fmt.Errorf("sessions <verb>: %w", err)`.
- **Test coverage spans `cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go` (extended) + `internal/e2e/sessions_rename_test.go` (new file).** Unit: `TestParseSessionsRenameArgs` table covers no-args, only-`<id>`, `<id> <label>`, `<id> ""` (empty-label clear), trailing positional (rejected), label-with-embedded-space (single token — passes), unknown flag. `TestRunSessions_RenameDispatch` pins router wiring against a bogus socket. E2E: five tests covering happy-path rename, empty-label clear, unknown UUID typed-error mapping, no-daemon dial failure, wrong-arity exit-2.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § `runSessionsRename` handler (1.1c-B2a → -B2b)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/92-cli-sessions-rename.md`](specs/architecture/92-cli-sessions-rename.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1c-B2b, ticket #93)
- **`pyry sessions rename <id> <new-label>` lifts to UUID-or-prefix.** Surgical edit to `runSessionsRename` (`cmd/pyry/main.go`): one call to `resolveSessionIDViaList` (the helper #99 introduced for `rm`) inserted above the wire call, plus a parallel `errors.Is(err, errAmbiguousPrefix)` branch in the existing error switch. The handler is now line-for-line `runSessionsRm`'s shape minus the bootstrap-rejection branch (renaming bootstrap is allowed per #62). No new helper, no new sentinel, no wire work — `resolveSessionIDViaList` and `errAmbiguousPrefix` already exist because #99 shipped first.
- **The wire receives the canonical UUID; stderr echoes the operator's typed `<id>`.** `control.SessionsRename` is called with the resolver's output; the not-found / ambiguous / race-window stderr lines all use the original input string so `pyry sessions rename ab1 …` doesn't surprise the operator with an expanded `ab1c2d34-…` in the failure message. Same shape as `runSessionsRm`.
- **Two `ErrSessionNotFound` paths collapse to one stderr line.** Resolver-side (prefix matched nothing) and wire-side (TOCTOU: resolver matched, then concurrent `rm` landed before our rename) both render `no session with id "<input>"` + exit 1. Distinguishing them buys nothing operationally — the operator's reaction is identical.
- **Confirms ADR 011's helper shape.** Caller #2 needed zero changes to `resolveSessionIDViaList`; the helper's exact-match-first / `strings.HasPrefix` / `errAmbiguousPrefix` contract scaled as-is. Lift to `internal/sessions` still defers to caller #3 (Phase 1.1e `attach`) — the trigger remains "third caller", not "second confirms the shape."
- **Test coverage: `internal/e2e/sessions_rename_test.go` extended with two new e2e tests.** `TestSessionsRename_E2E_Success_Prefix` (rename via first 8 hex chars; the canonical-UUID forwarding is implicitly pinned end-to-end — a wrong forward would surface as the wire's `ErrSessionNotFound`). `TestSessionsRename_E2E_AmbiguousPrefix` (mints sessions until pigeonhole-collision on first hex char, asserts non-zero exit + both matched ids+labels in stderr + **both sessions' on-disk labels unchanged** — load-bearing AC#2 check that the resolver bails before any wire mutation; pigeonhole bound 17 over 16 hex digits, mirrored from `TestSessionsRm_E2E_AmbiguousPrefix`). Existing `TestSessionsRename_E2E_UnknownUUID` now traverses the resolver-side `ErrSessionNotFound` arm without test edits (input is a syntactically-valid UUID; resolver finds no match in a freshly-bootstrapped registry; same stderr fragment, same exit code).
- **No unit-test edits.** The parser is untouched (`TestParseSessionsRenameArgs` still passes verbatim) and `TestRunSessions_RenameDispatch` still pins the router wiring — the resolver step happens after dispatch, doesn't change the dispatch-test's assertion. The resolver itself is unit-tested in #99's coverage; the dispatch test is the unit-level responsibility of `cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go`.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § `runSessionsRename` handler (1.1c-B2a → -B2b)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [ADR 011](knowledge/decisions/011-cli-prefix-resolution.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1d-B2, ticket #99)
- **`pyry sessions rm [--archive|--purge] <id>` CLI verb shipped.** Adds one `case "rm":` to `runSessions` (the #76 router), bumps `sessionsVerbList` from `"new"` to `"new, rm"`, updates `printHelp`'s sessions line to match. Three new helpers in `cmd/pyry/main.go`: `parseSessionsRmArgs` (flag-parse + arity, mirroring `parseSessionsNewArgs`), `resolveSessionIDViaList` (client-side prefix resolution via `control.SessionsList`), `runSessionsRm` (parse → resolve → `control.SessionsRm`, with AC-prescribed error messages on stderr + matching exit codes).
- **Prefix resolution is client-side (no new wire verb).** Architectural choice: extending the `sessions.rm` wire to accept prefixes would require a third `ErrorCode` (`ErrCodeAmbiguous`) plus a way to ship the match list over JSON. Reusing `sessions.list` (already shipped via #87) costs one extra round-trip per `rm` invocation — negligible at Phase 1.1's expected pool size — and keeps the wire surface stable. `resolveSessionIDViaList` mirrors `Pool.ResolveID`'s resolution order (exact match wins; otherwise `strings.HasPrefix` scan; zero/one/many → `ErrSessionNotFound`/canonical-id/`errAmbiguousPrefix`) so server-side and client-side resolution behave identically. The first of two/three CLI callers; per the ticket body, the shared-helper extraction defers to Phase 1.1e (`#49 attach refactor`) — a third caller arriving turns "now opportunistic" into "now warranted".
- **AC-prescribed messages are printed via `fmt.Fprintln(os.Stderr, ...)` + `os.Exit(1)`, NOT returned through `main`'s `pyry: ` outer-error printer.** Three named-error cases (ambiguous prefix, unknown UUID, bootstrap rejection) emit plain text without the `pyry:` prefix; other errors flow through `fmt.Errorf("sessions rm: %w", err)` which `main` prepends with `pyry: `. The `runAttach` precedent uses the same shape for its exit-2 path. `os.Exit` skips the `defer cancel()` on the 30s timeout context, but the only state involved is a process-local timer reaped on exit — no socket / file / goroutine leaks.
- **One `errSessionsRmUsage` sentinel covers every parse-time failure.** Mutually-exclusive flags, wrong arity, `flag.Parse` errors all wrap this sentinel via `fmt.Errorf("%w: ...", errSessionsRmUsage, ...)`. `runSessionsRm` matches with `errors.Is` and exits 2 + prints `pyry sessions rm: <wrapped-msg>`. The architect considered one-vs-two sentinels; one wrapper is sufficient because every error path out of the parser is, definitionally, a usage error.
- **Race window is documented but not retried.** Resolve-then-rm has a TOCTOU gap where another caller may remove the session between our `SessionsList` and `SessionsRm`. The wire returns `ErrSessionNotFound` from the second step; the CLI surfaces the *original typed `<id>`* (the operator's input string, possibly a prefix) rather than the canonical UUID — preserves debugging context.
- **Test coverage spans `cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go` (extended) + `internal/e2e/sessions_rm_test.go` (new).** Unit: `TestParseSessionsRmArgs` table covers no-args, only-flags, id-only, `--archive` / `--purge`, both-flags-set (mutually exclusive), trailing positional, flag-after-positional (Go's `flag` halts at the first positional), unknown flag. `TestRunSessions_RmDispatch` pins the router wiring against a bogus socket. E2E: nine tests under build tag `e2e` covering happy path (default / prefix / `--archive` / `--purge`), ambiguous prefix (mints sessions until pigeonhole-collision on first hex char — bound 17 over 16 hex digits), unknown UUID, bootstrap rejection, mutually-exclusive flags (exit 2), no-daemon dial failure (clean error, no panic).
- **Pre-seeded non-bootstrap registry entries are NOT loaded into the in-memory Pool on warm start (Pool.New hydrates only the bootstrap; non-bootstrap entries persist on disk between restarts via the "warm-start does not save" rule).** Discovered while writing the ambiguous-prefix e2e test: the architect's spec proposed seeding `aaaaaaaa-...-001` / `aaaaaaaa-...-002` directly into `sessions.json`, but `sessions.list` returns from `p.sessions` which on warm load contains only the bootstrap. Worked around by minting via `control.SessionsNew` and finding a pigeonhole collision on first hex char (typical run finds one in ≤5 mints, bound 17). If a future ticket needs deterministic prefix-collision e2e fixtures, the underlying issue is "warm-start hydrate of non-bootstrap entries" — out of scope here.
- **Production diff ~155 LOC in `cmd/pyry/main.go`** (router case + parser + resolver + handler + `sort` import + help text + sentinels). Test diff: ~75 LOC unit + ~290 LOC e2e. Wire surface unchanged.
- See [`docs/specs/architecture/99-cmd-pyry-sessions-rm.md`](specs/architecture/99-cmd-pyry-sessions-rm.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1d-B1, ticket #98)
- **`VerbSessionsRm` + `Remover` seam in `internal/control` — wire-only addition that completes the second `sessions.*` namespace member.** New verb `"sessions.rm"`; `SessionsPayload` extended with `omitempty` `ID` and `JSONLPolicy` fields (existing `sessions.new` requests stay byte-identical, pinned by extending `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat`); new `Response.ErrorCode` field (omitempty, so non-error responses and untyped errors round-trip byte-identically). Server adds `handleSessionsRm` mirroring `handleSessionsNew`'s shape (fresh 30s background ctx, single-shot encode); client `SessionsRm(ctx, sock, id, policy) error` mirrors `SessionsNew`/`SendResize` shape using the `request()` helper. CLI subcommand (`pyry sessions rm`) is a sibling ticket; the wire surface is reachable today only via the typed client.
- **`Sessioner` aggregates per-verb sub-interfaces — `NewServer` signature unchanged.** New named interface `Remover { Remove(ctx, sessions.SessionID, sessions.RemoveOptions) error }` lives next to `Sessioner` in `server.go` and is **embedded** into `Sessioner` rather than threaded through as a 7th `NewServer` parameter. `*sessions.Pool` already satisfies the embedded shape via `Pool.Remove` (#94/#95) — no adapter, no `cmd/pyry/main.go` change. The 27-call-site fan-out the constructor-parameter route would require is the failure mode the post-#75 architect prompt was rewritten to prevent. Phase 1.1b/c/e (`list`, `rename`, `attach` orchestration) will continue this pattern: one method (or named sub-interface embed) per verb on the same aggregate facade.
- **Wire-level `Response.ErrorCode` for typed-sentinel propagation.** Two stable string tokens (`"session_not_found"`, `"cannot_remove_bootstrap"`) decouple `errors.Is` matching from `Response.Error` text. Server detects sentinels with `errors.Is` (so future server-side wrapping won't break the wire token) and populates both `Error` (verbatim message) and `ErrorCode`; client maps the token back to the bare sentinel (`sessions.ErrSessionNotFound` / `sessions.ErrCannotRemoveBootstrap`) so callers `errors.Is` against it. Renaming a sentinel's message string is no longer a wire-protocol break — only the `ErrorCode` enum is. `omitempty` keeps non-typed-error responses byte-identical. `Pool.Remove` returns the sentinels bare today, so client returns the sentinel directly without `fmt.Errorf("%s: %w", resp.Error, sentinel)` (which would double-prefix the message: `"sessions: session not found: sessions: session not found"`).
- **Wire enum (`JSONLPolicy` string `"leave"`/`"archive"`/`"purge"`) deliberately distinct from `sessions.JSONLPolicy` (uint8).** Three motivations: (1) `protocol.go` stays import-free; (2) wire bytes are jq-debuggable strings rather than integers; (3) durable across protocol versions if the underlying enum order ever changes. Empty wire value maps to `JSONLLeave` (matches the internal zero value, so an omitted field gets the documented default); unknown values surface as `"sessions.rm: unknown jsonl policy %q"` in `Response.Error` (fail-loud, no silent fallback). Translation lives in one place — `toSessionsPolicy` next to `handleSessionsRm`.
- **Empty `ID` rejected at the handler boundary.** Server-side guard returns `"sessions.rm: missing id"` (no `ErrorCode`). Passing `""` through to `Pool.Remove` would also work but produces the wrong `ErrorCode` (an empty ID is a malformed-input condition, not a "not found" condition). Mirrors `handleResize`'s `payload == nil` guard.
- **Test coverage in `sessions_rm_test.go` (~344 LOC).** `fakeSessioner` (in `sessions_new_test.go`) gained one `Remove` method on the existing struct — no new fake type. Mandatory tests: byte-equality back-compat (asserts `sessions.new` payloads + `Response{}` + `Response{OK:true}` marshal byte-identically post-`ID`/`JSONLPolicy`/`ErrorCode` additions); success path; each `JSONLPolicy` value (`""`, `"leave"`, `"archive"`, `"purge"`); both typed-error sentinel propagations (assert `errors.Is` round-trips); other-pool-error untyped path (`errors.Is` against typed sentinels returns false); nil-Sessioner branch; missing-ID guard (zero `Remove` calls on fake); bad-policy guard (zero `Remove` calls on fake); wire shape (hand-rolled `net.Listen` captures the JSON line for three `(id, policy)` cases including empty-policy omitempty); empty-response-as-error.
- **Production diff ~205 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go`: +55 for `VerbSessionsRm` + `JSONLPolicy` + `ErrorCode` + `SessionsPayload` fields + `Response.ErrorCode`; `internal/control/server.go`: +92 for `Remover` + `Sessioner` embed + dispatch + `handleSessionsRm` + `toSessionsPolicy`; `internal/control/client.go`: +35 for `SessionsRm`). Test diff ~412 LOC. CLI surface unchanged.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md § Sessions: removal seam (1.1d-B1)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/98-control-sessions-rm.md`](specs/architecture/98-control-sessions-rm.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1c-A, ticket #62)
- **`Pool.Rename(id SessionID, newLabel string) error` write primitive** — typed mutator for the `label` field. Resolves `id` under `Pool.mu` (write); unknown id ⇒ `ErrSessionNotFound` with on-disk and in-memory state byte-identical to before (no `saveLocked` call). No-op rename (`newLabel == sess.label`) also skips `saveLocked`, keeping registry mtime stable for idempotent calls (same precedent as `RotateID(x, x)`). Otherwise mutates `sess.label` and persists via `saveLocked`. The internal seam Phase 1.1c-B's `pyry sessions rename` CLI verb (#47-B) consumes instead of touching `sessions.json` directly.
- **Empty `newLabel` permitted; bootstrap substitution from #60 falls out for free.** `Rename` writes the verbatim string through to disk and does not branch on `sess.bootstrap`. `Rename(bootstrapID, "")` clears the on-disk label, then `Pool.List`'s synthetic `"bootstrap"` substitution resumes; `Rename(bootstrapID, "primary")` persists `"primary"` and `Pool.List` reflects it verbatim. Substitution rule lives in `List`, not in `Rename` — uniform across consumers.
- **Save-failure rollback as belt-and-suspenders.** `saveRegistryLocked`'s temp+rename discipline makes partial writes unreachable, so disk state never disagrees with the rolled-back in-memory state. The `sess.label = prev` rollback exists so a subsequent retry has consistent inputs and a `Lookup` after a failed `Rename` doesn't return a label that isn't on disk. `saveLocked` error returned verbatim — no `Rename:`-specific wrap, preserves `errors.Is` symmetry with other persist sites.
- **`Session.label` guarded by `Pool.mu`, not `Session.lcMu`.** Lifecycle goroutine in `Session.Run` does not read `label`; only readers are `Pool.List` (RLock) and `saveRegistryLocked` (Lock — caller holds write). Same shape as `RotateID`'s mutation of `session.id` without `lcMu`. Doc-comment on `Session.label` updated to reflect mutation via `Pool.Rename`. No new lock-order edges.
- **No new exported types or sentinels.** `Pool.Rename` is the only new exported name; `ErrSessionNotFound` (existing) is the only sentinel. Strict full-`SessionID` only — UUID-prefix resolution is a CLI/UX concern for 47-B that may reuse `Pool.List`. No validation of `newLabel` (length, character class, uniqueness) — same posture as `Pool.Create`'s unvalidated `label` parameter.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md § Pool.Rename](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1b-A, ticket #60)
- **`Pool.List() []SessionInfo` read primitive** — typed snapshot of every session in the pool (bootstrap and minted alike), sorted by `LastActiveAt` desc with `SessionID` asc tiebreak for determinism. Each entry carries `ID`, `Label`, `LifecycleState`, `LastActiveAt`, `Bootstrap`. Read-only — no `lastActiveAt` bump, no state transition, no `persist()`. The internal seam Phase 1.1b-B's `pyry sessions list` CLI verb (#46-B) consumes instead of touching `sessions.json` directly.
- **New `SessionInfo` value type, deep-copy-safe by construction** — every field is a value (`SessionID`/`string`/`time.Time` are values; `lifecycleState` is a `uint8` enum). Mutating a `SessionInfo` cannot affect pool state or registry contents. No defensive cloning, no documentation contract that callers can violate.
- **Synthetic `"bootstrap"` label substitution at this layer, not in 46-B's renderer.** When the bootstrap's on-disk `label` is empty, `List` substitutes `"bootstrap"` — but the on-disk registry entry is **not** mutated. An operator-set bootstrap label passes through verbatim; the `Bootstrap` bool is the discriminator, not the label string. Putting the substitution at the read primitive (rather than at the wire/CLI layer) means every future internal consumer gets the same UX guarantee.
- **Why a new type, not extending `SnapshotEntry{ID, PID}`** — `SnapshotEntry` exists for the rotation watcher's closure-over-primitives boundary (`internal/sessions/rotation` cannot import `internal/sessions`). Adding `lifecycleState` to it would either bloat every rotation snapshot or push the enum into `rotation`'s import set. Two distinct types, one per consumer, is cleaner than a shared shape.
- **Lock order — unchanged.** `Pool.mu` (RLock) → `Session.lcMu` (Lock). Identical to `Pool.saveLocked` and `Pool.pickLRUVictim`. `id`/`label`/`bootstrap` read off-`lcMu` (immutable post-`New`/`RotateID` from any reader holding `Pool.mu`); `lcState`/`lastActiveAt` read under `lcMu` (the lifecycle goroutine writes them there). Each session's pair is read under one `lcMu` acquire — no torn reads.
- **No new ADR — design follows existing patterns.** Typed read accessor; `sort.Slice` to match `registry.go`'s style; per-consumer value type per the existing `SnapshotEntry` convention; no new sentinel errors (the method has no error path).
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md § Pool.List](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1a-A2, ticket #73)
- **`Pool.Create(ctx, label) (SessionID, error)`** — user-facing primitive that mints a fresh non-bootstrap session: `NewID` → build `*Session` in `stateEvicted` (label verbatim, `bootstrap=false`, `ResumeLast=false`, `ClaudeArgs` cloned + `--session-id <uuid>` appended) → register-and-persist under `Pool.mu` (rollback on save failure) → `RegisterAllocatedUUID` (rotation skip-set) → `supervise` (#72's seam) → `Pool.Activate` (cap-aware spawn from #41). One well-tested entry point for Phase 1.1a-B's `sessions.new` verb (#71) and Phase 2.0's channel-driven auto-mint. Bootstrap unchanged (`Pool.Lookup("")` returns the same `*Session` pre/post `Create`).
- **Per-session template fields on `*Pool`** — `sessionTpl SessionConfig` (shallow copy of `cfg.Bootstrap` captured at `New()`) + `idleTimeoutDefault time.Duration` (mirror of `Config.IdleTimeout`), both read-only after `New`. `Create` clones `tpl.ClaudeArgs` via `slices.Clone` (appending to the template directly would mutate it across calls), and mints a fresh `supervisor.NewBridge(p.log)` per session in service mode (`tpl.Bridge != nil`) — sharing one bridge across N sessions would multiplex their I/O into a single client view.
- **Persist-then-activate ordering, with id-or-empty discriminator.** Save failure with claude already running would leave an unsupervised orphan whose JSONL has no on-disk record; a registry-only entry that didn't activate is benign (recoverable on next `Activate`). Returned `SessionID == ""` iff nothing persisted; non-empty id + non-nil err means "entry on disk, decide what to do." Caller uses `errors.Is(err, ErrPoolNotRunning)` to distinguish the not-running case from an Activate failure.
- **Cap pre-flight via `Pool.Activate` directly (choice (a))** — the new session is in `stateEvicted` at cap-check time, so it doesn't increment `active`; `pickLRUVictim` excludes the target. No duplicated cap logic and no transient inconsistent view from `Snapshot`/`Lookup` (the alternative — pre-flight before registering — would create one).
- **Lock order unchanged.** `Pool.mu → Session.lcMu` for the persist couple; `capMu → Pool.mu → Session.lcMu` on the cap path. `Create` does NOT hold `p.mu` across `supervise`, `Activate`, or `RegisterAllocatedUUID` — the lock is taken only for register+persist, then released. ctx-cancellation race documented: caller may see `(id, ctx.Err)` while the lifecycle goroutine spins up anyway (it respects the pool's run-ctx, not the caller's).
- **No new public types or sentinels.** `Pool.Create` is the only new exported name; `ErrPoolNotRunning` (from #72) is the only sentinel propagated.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md § Pool.Create](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1a-A1, ticket #72)
- **Pool supervisor fan-out seam** — unexported `Pool.supervise(sess *Session) error` schedules `sess.Run(gctx)` on `Pool.Run`'s live errgroup. Returns the new sentinel `ErrPoolNotRunning` when called before `Run` has wired the handle or after `Run` has cleared it (matchable with `errors.Is`). The helper is the join point Phase 1.1a-A2's `Pool.Create(ctx, label)` consumes; the bootstrap fan-out inside `Pool.Run` is itself rewritten to call `supervise` so the helper is exercised in production from day one. Watcher fan-out is unchanged (not a `*Session`).
- **Supervisor handle on `*Pool`** — `runGroup *errgroup.Group` + `runCtx context.Context`, both guarded by `Pool.mu` (RWMutex) and read together so a caller never sees a half-initialised handle. Set in `Pool.Run` under `Pool.mu` (write) right after `errgroup.WithContext`; cleared in a `defer` so a panicking goroutine still resets the handle. `supervise` reads under `Pool.mu` (RLock) and calls `g.Go` *off-lock*. No new lock-order edges (`Pool.mu → Session.lcMu` and `Pool.capMu → Pool.mu → Session.lcMu` unchanged) — the helper does not touch `Session.lcMu`.
- **Why fields-on-Pool, not a separate guard struct** — `Pool.mu` already protects every other "what's in this pool right now" read. A second mutex would double the lock count without buying anything; RWMutex matches the access pattern (N concurrent supervise readers, one-shot writes by `Run` setup/teardown). Concurrent `supervise` callers don't contend with each other.
- **Race-with-teardown is benign** — a `supervise` call interleaved with the deferred clear either (a) acquires RLock first, schedules onto a group whose ctx is about to cancel, and `Session.Run` exits via the existing shutdown path, or (b) acquires after, observes `nil`, returns the sentinel. No silent leak, no deadlock.
- **Defensive wrap on the bootstrap call** — `Pool.Run` does `if err := p.supervise(bootstrap); err != nil { return fmt.Errorf("sessions: supervise bootstrap: %w", err) }` even though the precondition is established two lines above. Cheap insurance against a future reordering bug.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md § Supervisor handle](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.2c-B, ticket #41)
- **Concurrent active cap (LRU eviction)** — `Config.ActiveCap` bounds the number of concurrently running claudes. `<= 0` is unset (uncapped, byte-identical to 1.2c-A); `>= 1` enforces. When activating one more session would exceed the cap, the LRU peer (oldest `lastActiveAt` among currently-active sessions, excluding the target) is evicted via the new public `Session.Evict` primitive before the new spawn proceeds. **No CLI flag yet** — Phase 2.0 will wire `-pyry-active-cap` when the auto-mint workload makes it load-bearing.
- **`Session.Evict(ctx)` public primitive** — symmetric to `Activate`. Force-eviction: unlike the idle timer, it does **not** defer for `attached > 0`. The cap is a hard limit; an attached caller will see EOF on its bridge. Phase 2.0 may add an attach-aware filter to the LRU candidate set; not in scope for #41. Pairs `evictCh` (buffered 1 signal) with `evictedCh` (closed-on-evicted broadcast), mirroring `activateCh`/`activeCh`.
- **`Pool.capMu` outermost lock** — taken only on the cap path (`activeCap > 0`). Lock order: `Pool.capMu → Pool.mu → Session.lcMu`. Serialises cap-check + victim eviction + new spawn so concurrent `Activate`s can't both observe `active < cap` and both proceed. Never re-acquired by callees, so `Session.Evict`'s callback into `Pool.persist` (which takes `Pool.mu`) is deadlock-free. The uncapped path doesn't take `capMu` at all — "byte-identical when unset" includes "doesn't even take the cap mutex".
- **`Pool.pickLRUVictim`** — O(n) iteration over `pool.sessions` under `Pool.mu.RLock`, reads each `Session.lcState`/`lastActiveAt` under `lcMu`, returns the oldest-`lastActiveAt` peer (excluding target). Premature optimisation rejected: a heap/linked-list would defeat the zero-cost-when-unset property and add a counter-vs-truth drift class of bug for an O(n) cost that doesn't matter at pyry's scale (≤ 100s of sessions).
- **`Session.touchLastActive`** — bumps `lastActiveAt` in-memory only on a cap-path `Activate` against an already-active session. **Not persisted** (the registry's `lastActiveAt` only flushes on transitions). Keeps in-memory LRU ordering reflective of the most recent touch.
- **`Pool.Activate` is now the spawn-path entry, not just a thin Lookup wrapper.** Phase 2.0's router calls this. Cap-unset path: one early-return branch and forward to `Session.Activate`. Cap-set path: cap check + victim eviction + new spawn under `capMu`.
- See [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [ADR 006](knowledge/decisions/006-concurrent-active-cap-lru.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.2c-A, ticket #40)
- **Idle eviction + lazy respawn** — per-`*Session` lifecycle goroutine drives a two-state machine (`active` ↔ `evicted`). When `attached == 0` and the idle timer fires, the supervisor's inner ctx is cancelled and claude exits cleanly; the JSONL on disk is preserved. `Session.Activate(ctx)` respawns the supervisor pointing at the same JSONL on disk so the conversation continues. `Session.Run` rewritten from one-line supervisor delegate into a `runActive` / `runEvicted` loop; `Pool.Run` shape **unchanged** (multi-session fan-out is Phase 1.1's job).
- **Activity = attach state** — while `attached > 0` the timer re-arms on fire (poll-with-grace; eviction may overshoot the configured timeout by up to one window). `last_active_at` is bumped on every state transition for the upcoming LRU follow-up's victim selection.
- **`-pyry-idle-timeout` flag** — production default `15m`, `0` disables eviction entirely (test default + operator escape hatch). Wired through `Config.IdleTimeout` → `SessionConfig.IdleTimeout` (per-session override falls back to pool default).
- **Activate-before-Attach contract** — `bridge.Attach` on an evicted session would block on the pipe forever. `internal/control.Session` interface gained `Activate(ctx)`; `handleAttach` calls it with a 30s timeout cap before binding the bridge. `handleStatus` does **not** activate (faithful `PhaseStopped` for evicted; no spurious wakeups from a poll). Wire response on respawn failure: `attach: activate: <err>`.
- **Registry `lifecycle_state` field** — `"active"` / `"evicted"`, `omitempty` so the dominant active case stays off disk (preserves #34's idempotent-reload byte-stability). Old pyry binaries ignore the field; new pyry reading old files defaults to `"active"`. Bootstrap warm-starts in whatever state the registry says — including starting in `evicted` if pyry was stopped while evicted.
- **Lock order: `Pool.mu → Session.lcMu`** — `Session.lcMu` protects `lcState` / `attached` / `activeCh` / `lastActiveAt` (when read for the registry snapshot). `Session.transitionTo` releases `lcMu` before calling `Pool.persist` so `saveLocked`'s per-session re-acquire doesn't deadlock. `RotateID` mutates `session.id` without `lcMu` — documented invariant (today's only callers run before any lifecycle goroutine observes the id).
- **Concurrency primitives** — `activeCh` (closed-on-active broadcast) + `activateCh` (buffered 1 signal). `Activate` snapshots `activeCh` under `lcMu` *before* waiting so a concurrent evict-replace doesn't drop the wakeup. Concurrent `Activate`s collapse to one signal via the buffered send.
- See [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [ADR 005](knowledge/decisions/005-idle-eviction-state-machine.md).

### Codebase (rotation fix, ticket #118)
- **Rotation-watcher path comparison resolves symlinks at construction.** `Watcher` gained an unexported `resolvedDir` (`filepath.EvalSymlinks(cfg.Dir)`, captured once in `New`). `handleCreate`'s match gate became `filepath.Clean(open) == filepath.Join(w.resolvedDir, base)`. Pre-#118 the gate compared `filepath.Clean(open)` to `filepath.Clean(fullPath)` from the fsnotify event — `filepath.Clean` is lexical and never resolves symlinks, so on macOS where `/var → /private/var`, fsnotify's `/var/...` ev.Name and lsof's `/private/var/...` probe output never matched and rotation was silently dropped (symptom: session UUID stops updating after `/clear`). Affects every macOS user whose `~/.claude/projects/` lives behind a symlink (custom HOME, external-drive home) and every `t.TempDir`-based test on macOS — surfaced by #55's e2e harness landing `t.TempDir()` under `/var/folders/...`.
- **Resolve once, not per event — three properties.** (1) Zero per-event syscalls; (2) no race window between event and resolution (the directory's lifetime spans the watcher's, ducking the AC's "file unlinked between event and resolution" failure mode); (3) no API change — `Config.Dir` stays as-is, `pool.go`'s call site untouched. `EvalSymlinks` failure at startup logs `Warn` and falls back to `cfg.Dir` unmodified — the macOS-symlink case continues to fail in that specific run (no worse than today), startup proceeds.
- **`TestWatcher_DetectsRotationThroughSymlink` regression test.** Explicit `os.Symlink` from a side dir to the real sessions dir; watcher set up against the link; probe reports the *resolved* path (mimicking what `lsof` / `/proc/<pid>/fd` actually return). Fails on the pre-#118 code (gate rejects `Clean(real/...)` vs `Clean(link/...)` because they're different absolute paths); passes after the fix. Portable across Linux and macOS via the explicit `os.Symlink` — Linux CI exercises the symlink branch even though Linux defaults don't put `t.TempDir` behind a symlink. Existing six tests that build a `dir` from `t.TempDir()` were updated to wrap with `filepath.EvalSymlinks(t.TempDir())` so probe-returned paths and the watcher's resolved view stay in the same canonical form.
- **Production diff: ~8 lines in `internal/sessions/rotation/watcher.go`** (one struct field, ~5 lines in `New`, one rewritten line in `handleCreate`). Test diff: ~30 LOC for the new test plus mechanical 2-line additions across the existing tests. Two files total. Zero consumer call sites touched.
- See [knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md § Symlink-resolved match path](knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md), `lessons.md § fsnotify reports as-watched, kernel probes report canonicalised`.

### Codebase (Phase 1.2b-B, ticket #39)
- **Live `/clear` rotation watcher** — `internal/sessions/rotation` package: fsnotify on `cfg.ClaudeSessionsDir` + per-PID FD probe (Linux walks `/proc/<pid>/fd`, macOS shells out to `lsof -nP -p <pid> -F fn`). On a CREATE for `<new>.jsonl` whose UUID a tracked PID has open, calls `Pool.RotateID(old, new)` — same seam #38 established. Detection latency ~250ms worst-case (probeWithRetry walks 0/50/200ms attempts to handle CREATE-before-open races).
- **`Pool.Run` errgroup wrap** — `golang.org/x/sync/errgroup` ties the bootstrap supervisor and the watcher; cancellation propagates both ways. Phase 1.1's N-session fan-out reuses the same wrapper — the extension point is one `g.Go` per pool entry.
- **Pyry-allocated UUID skip set on `Pool`** — `RegisterAllocatedUUID` / `IsAllocated`. Consume-on-first-hit, 30s TTL pruned opportunistically, all under `p.mu` (write). No live caller in 1.2b-B (pyry still uses `--continue`); scaffolding lands now so Phase 1.1's `claude --session-id` is a one-liner.
- **`rotation.Config` closures over primitives** — the rotation package never imports `internal/sessions`. The `SessionID ↔ string` conversion happens once, inside `Pool.Run`'s closure wiring. `Pool.Snapshot` returns a small `SnapshotEntry` struct; `snapshotForRotation` translates to `rotation.SessionRef`.
- **Failure posture** — rotation detection is never load-bearing. fsnotify init failure, missing `lsof`, missing `/proc`, save failure during `OnRotate` — all logged warn/debug; pyry continues. `MkdirAll(dir, 0700)` for a not-yet-existing claude dir.
- **First new external runtime dep since `creack/pty`** — `github.com/fsnotify/fsnotify` v1.10.0, justified in [ADR 004](knowledge/decisions/004-fsnotify-for-rotation-detection.md). `golang.org/x/sync` lands as a sibling for errgroup.
- See [knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md](knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md), [ADR 004](knowledge/decisions/004-fsnotify-for-rotation-detection.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.2b-A, ticket #38)
- **Startup JSONL reconciliation** — `Pool.New` scans `~/.claude/projects/<encoded-cwd>/<uuid>.jsonl`, picks the most-recently-modified one, and rotates the registry's bootstrap entry to that UUID if it disagrees. Self-heals after `/clear` (claude rotates session UUIDs on `/clear`; without reconciliation, post-`pyry stop` the registry would still point at the pre-`/clear` UUID).
- **`Pool.RotateID(oldID, newID)`** — atomic swap of in-memory map key + bootstrap pointer + `saveLocked`, all under `p.mu` (write). `RotateID(x, x)` is a no-op; unknown old id returns `ErrSessionNotFound`. Bumps `last_active_at`; preserves `created_at`. The load-bearing seam reused by Phase 1.2b-B (live-detection via fsnotify).
- **`encodeWorkdir`** — claude maps both `/` AND `.` to `-` in its `~/.claude/projects/` path component (verified empirically 2026-05-02). `/foo/.bar` → `-foo--bar` (note the doubled dash). Unexported; encoding lives inside `internal/sessions` and `cmd/pyry` only sees the resolved path via `DefaultClaudeSessionsDir`.
- **JSONL location** — files live directly in `<encoded-cwd>/<uuid>.jsonl`. There is **no** `sessions/` subdirectory (the ticket body claimed otherwise; the spec followed reality).
- **Failure posture** — missing/unreadable claude dir is logged warn and ignored (startup proceeds). Save failure during rotation is fatal-at-startup (matches 1.2a cold-start). The pre-rotation JSONL is never deleted or modified — only the registry pointer moves.
- **Expected one-time rotation in 1.2a** — on the second `pyry` restart, claude's UUID ≠ pyry's mint, so reconcile fires once and logs an Info line. Becomes rare after Phase 1.1+ wires `claude --session-id <uuid>`.
- See [knowledge/features/jsonl-reconciliation.md](knowledge/features/jsonl-reconciliation.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.2a, ticket #34)
- **Session registry on disk** — `~/.pyry/<sanitized-name>/sessions.json` (file 0600, dir 0700), sibling to the per-name socket. Schema: `version` (forward-marker), `sessions[]` with `id` / `label` / `created_at` / `last_active_at` / `bootstrap`. Default `encoding/json` decoder tolerates unknown fields for forward compat.
- **`Pool.New` load-or-mint** — Cold start (missing or empty file) mints a fresh UUID and writes the registry before returning. Warm start reads the bootstrap-marked entry, reuses its UUID + metadata, and does **not** rewrite the file (warm reload is not a state change). Malformed JSON is fatal at startup — operator must fix or remove.
- **Atomic write seam** — `saveRegistryLocked` does `os.CreateTemp` → `Chmod 0600` → encode → fsync → close → `os.Rename`. Rename is the commit point; partial JSON is unreachable in the target. `defer os.Remove(tmp)` cleans up orphaned temps best-effort. `Pool.saveLocked` is the package-internal hook Phase 1.1's `Pool.Add` / `Rename` / `Remove` will call before returning success — caller holds `Pool.mu` (write) across the disk I/O.
- **Bootstrap marker on disk** — `bootstrap: true` is persisted explicitly so `Pool.Lookup("")` doesn't depend on file ordering. Phase 1.1's `pyry sessions rm <bootstrap-uuid>` thus has a clean question to answer (refuse, or promote another entry) instead of relying on array position. `omitempty` keeps non-bootstrap entries clean on disk.
- **Stable disk ordering** — `sortEntriesByCreatedAt` (then by `ID`) before write makes the file's byte content a deterministic function of the in-memory set, defeating Go's randomized map iteration and giving the AC's idempotent-reload guarantee. Degenerate for 1.2a's single entry; the property is paid for upfront ahead of 1.1.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-registry.md](knowledge/features/sessions-registry.md).

### Documentation
- README, plan.md (phase roadmap), CLAUDE.md, CODING-STYLE.md
- Knowledge base: system-overview, 2 ADRs (Go language, PTY supervisor)
- This file, lessons.md

### Infrastructure
- GitHub Actions CI: go vet, staticcheck, go test -race
- QMD search: pyrycode-docs, pyrycode-root collections
- .claude/settings.json with safety rules

## Patterns Established

- **Config struct pattern** — all configuration in a single `Config` struct, defaults applied in `New()`
- **Context-based cancellation** — `context.Context` flows through `Run()` → `runOnce()`, checked at every wait point
- **Structured logging** — `log/slog` with injected logger, not a global
- **Exponential backoff with stability reset** — backoff doubles on restart, resets to initial if child stayed up longer than `BackoffReset`
- **Deferred cleanup** — `defer` for terminal restore, PTY close, signal stop
- **Empty ID resolves to default** — `Pool.Lookup("")` returns the bootstrap session, so future `req.SessionID` fields can be added with no handler-side branching (old clients send empty, get the bootstrap; new clients send a real ID, get the right entry)
- **Introduce-then-rewire slicing** — split #27 into #28 (new package + tests, no consumers) and #29 (mechanical consumer rewiring) to keep each PR focused
- **Consumer-side interface definition** — `internal/control` defines the interfaces it consumes (`SessionResolver`, `Session`) rather than importing them from the producer package. Keeps `internal/sessions` free of control-plane concerns and lets tests fake the surface without exporting test seams from the producer.
- **Wire-string preservation via `errors.Is` mapping** — when refactoring an error path that crosses package boundaries, map the new sentinel back to the old wire string explicitly (`if errors.Is(err, sessions.ErrAttachUnavailable) { … Phase 0 string … }`) rather than letting `fmt.Sprintf("%v", err)` change client output. Required when an AC says "byte-identical."
- **Atomic on-disk writes via temp + rename** — for operator-recoverable JSON state files, `os.CreateTemp` in the same dir → encode → `f.Sync()` → `f.Close()` → `os.Rename(tmp, path)` makes the rename the commit point and partial files unreachable. `defer os.Remove(tmp)` cleans up orphans best-effort (no-op after successful rename). Don't bother with directory fsync unless real-world corruption is observed — pyry's registry is recoverable, not a database.
- **Stable disk ordering for idempotent reload** — sort serialized collections by a stable key (e.g. `created_at` then `id`) before writing. Defeats Go's randomized map iteration so save→load→save round-trips are byte-stable, and makes load-twice-equals-load-once into a real property rather than a probabilistic one.
- **Persistence as a Config field, empty disables** — `Config.RegistryPath` (or any "where to persist" string) defaulting to empty = no I/O lets unit tests construct a Pool with `t.TempDir()` or with persistence off entirely, with no test-only branches inside `New`. Production callers always pass a real path; the empty case is genuinely test-only. Same shape reused for `Config.ClaudeSessionsDir` in 1.2b-A.
- **One mutation seam, multiple drivers** — `Pool.RotateID` is the single place that swaps a session's in-memory id and persists. Startup reconciliation drives it from a directory scan; the live-detection watcher drives it from an fsnotify event. Defining the seam once with the lock-and-save contract baked in meant the second driver landed as a goroutine that calls a function, not a redesign.
- **Closures over primitives across package boundaries** — when a downstream package (`internal/sessions/rotation`) needs to call back into its host (`internal/sessions`), express the contract as a struct of closures over primitive types (`string`, `int`) rather than an interface that references the host's domain types (`SessionID`). The downstream package then has zero knowledge of the host, and the type-safety conversion (`SessionID ↔ string`) happens exactly once, in the wiring site. Avoids the import cycle the obvious "watcher takes a `*Pool`" design would create.
- **Test seam via package var, not interface injection** — `var newProbe = rotation.DefaultProbe` in `internal/sessions/pool.go`. Tests overwrite to inject a fake; production callers see no extra plumbing. Same shape as `allocatedTTL` and `probeRetryDelays` (test-tunable knobs that aren't config). Cheaper than threading a factory through `Config` for a single test surface.
- **Errgroup as the fan-out seam** — `Pool.Run`'s `errgroup.WithContext` ties the bootstrap supervisor and the rotation watcher; Phase 1.1's N-session fan-out reuses the same cancellation+error semantics. The 1.1a-A1 (#72) seam is the natural shape: stash `*errgroup.Group` + `context.Context` on the host struct under its existing RWMutex, expose an unexported helper that RLock-snapshots both and calls `g.Go` off-lock, and pair it with a sentinel error (`ErrPoolNotRunning`) for before/after-`Run` calls. The helper is the join point post-`Run` consumers (`Pool.Create`) plug into; the existing bootstrap fan-out is refactored onto the helper so the helper is exercised in production from day one rather than living dormant.
- **Two-state machine with explicit-verb wake-up** — when a runtime entity needs an `idle ↔ live` lifecycle, prefer (a) a per-entity goroutine that owns both the state machine and the underlying resource lifecycle, (b) an explicit `Activate(ctx)` call rather than implicit wake on resolve/lookup, and (c) a closed-on-state broadcast channel + buffered(1) signal channel for the wake-up handshake. Implicit wake-on-lookup tangles read-side concerns (status reads paying respawn latency); explicit Activate keeps every caller's contract sharp. Used for `Session.Activate` (1.2c-A); will be reused by future per-session lifecycles (router, bind/unbind).
- **Lock order `Pool.mu → Session.lcMu` with release-before-callback** — when a callee needs to call back into the host's lock-protected persistence (`Pool.persist` from `Session.transitionTo`), release the inner lock *before* the callback so the host's re-acquire of the inner lock inside its serialization path doesn't deadlock. Document the order at every site that takes both. Same shape would apply to any "child mutates state then asks parent to persist" coupling.
- **Dedicated outer mutex for "cap-shaped" critical sections** — when a sequence (cap-check + victim eviction + new spawn) must be atomic but its inner steps already take the host's main mutex (and may re-take it via persistence callbacks), introduce a *separate* outer mutex (`Pool.capMu` for #41) rather than holding the main mutex (`Pool.mu` write) across the whole sequence. The outer mutex serialises the policy decision; the inner work continues to take/release the main mutex normally. Avoids both the deadlock (re-entrancy on `Pool.mu` via `persist`) and the contention (blocking unrelated `Pool.mu` reads for the eviction's bounded window). Lock order documented; outer mutex is never re-acquired by callees.
- **"Zero cost when unset" as a hot-path discipline** — when a feature is configurable and most operators leave it unset (`Config.ActiveCap == 0`), gate ALL of its bookkeeping behind the early-return branch — including the new mutex it needs. The uncapped `Pool.Activate` doesn't even take `capMu`, doesn't iterate `sessions`, doesn't read `lastActiveAt`. The branch is one `if cap <= 0 { return … }` at the top of the cap-only path. The property "the previous phase's behaviour is byte-identical with the new feature unset" is paid for by being *strict* about what happens before the early return.
- **Id-or-empty as the failure-mode discriminator for "mint, persist, activate" primitives** — when a constructor-shaped method returns `(ID, error)` and has multiple failure points (rng, validation, persist, activate, supervise), make the returned id the caller's discriminator: empty id ⇒ "nothing was persisted, nothing to clean up"; non-empty id ⇒ "entry is on disk, decide what to do (retry the rest, accept eventual lifecycle, leave for next process start)." Callers distinguish further with `errors.Is` against named sentinels. Cleaner than a multi-valued status struct, and the empty/non-empty rule is checkable at every call site without deconstructing the error chain. Used for `Pool.Create` (1.1a-A2). The same shape suits any future "create-then-activate" seam where partial completion is recoverable.
- **Synthetic substitution at the read boundary, not at the renderer** — when an on-disk record's empty field has a well-known operator-facing default (e.g. `"bootstrap"` for an unlabelled bootstrap session), do the substitution in the *read primitive* that returns the typed snapshot, not in the CLI/wire renderer that consumes it. The on-disk record stays unmutated; every future consumer (a JSON renderer, a TUI, an HTTP handler) gets the same UX guarantee for free without re-implementing the rule. Pair with a discriminator field (e.g. `Bootstrap bool`) so the substitution is a UX nicety rather than the only signal — an operator who sets `Label="bootstrap"` on a non-bootstrap session is still distinguishable. Used for `Pool.List`'s bootstrap label (1.1b-A); same shape suits any "default for empty field" rule that crosses multiple consumers.
- **Per-consumer value type, not a shared "kitchen-sink snapshot"** — when multiple consumers each need a typed snapshot of part of a domain object's state, prefer one small value type per consumer over one shared type that unions every field everyone might want. `SnapshotEntry{ID, PID}` for the rotation watcher (closure-over-primitives boundary, cannot import the host's domain types); `SessionInfo{ID, Label, LifecycleState, LastActiveAt, Bootstrap}` for the operator-visible list. Adding lifecycle state to `SnapshotEntry` would either bloat every rotation snapshot or leak the host's enum into the rotation package's import set. Two ~5-field types are clearer than one ~10-field type with most fields irrelevant per call site.
- **Per-session template fields snapshotted at construction, read-only after** — when a Pool/Registry needs a "shape of new entries" template (claude bin, work dir, backoff timings, bridge presence), capture it as an unexported field on the host (`Pool.sessionTpl`) at `New()` time and treat it as immutable thereafter. Per-create call clones the slice fields (`slices.Clone(tpl.ClaudeArgs)`) and mints fresh resources where sharing would be wrong (`supervisor.NewBridge(p.log)` per session in service mode). No lock needed for reads; mutation is impossible by construction. Two ~15-line struct constructions (bootstrap in `New`, fresh entry in `Create`) with different lifecycle-state defaults is clearer than a `lcState lifecycleState` parameter on a shared helper — accepted intentionally.
- **Side-fd + Close to drain a blocked Read goroutine — only works with `O_NONBLOCK` on character devices.** When a goroutine is blocked in `io.Copy`/`Read` on a process-wide fd (e.g. `os.Stdin`) with no way to wake it, the standard fix is to open a parallel fd to the same underlying device, copy from *that* fd, and `Close` it on cleanup. For sockets and pipes the runtime poller mediates Reads automatically; for character devices like `/dev/tty` you must pass `os.O_RDONLY|syscall.O_NONBLOCK` so `Read` returns `EAGAIN` and the goroutine parks on the poller — only then does `Close` wake it via `runtime_pollUnblock`. Plain blocking `open` produces an fd whose in-flight `syscall.Read` cannot be interrupted by `Close` on another goroutine. Used for the foreground-mode input bridge in `internal/supervisor` (#78); applies to any "wake a stuck reader by closing a side fd" pattern.
- **Symmetric channel pairs for two-way state-machine signalling** — when a two-state machine (`active` / `evicted`) needs both *enter-state* and *exit-state* external triggers, mirror the channel pair: `activateCh` (buffered 1 signal) + `activeCh` (closed-on-active broadcast) gets a sibling `evictCh` (buffered 1 signal) + `evictedCh` (closed-on-evicted broadcast). Both pairs follow the same snapshot-under-lock-then-wait discipline. The state-transition code closes one channel and re-opens the other in lockstep. One pattern, two directions.
- **Wake-after-persist: close the broadcast channel only after the side-effect that observers depend on has committed.** When a state-machine transition has both an in-memory flip and a persistent side effect (registry write, file rename, DB commit), broadcast the wake to external waiters *after* the persist returns — never before, never under the same lock as the persist (causes deadlock when persist re-acquires the inner lock via its own serialization path). Restructure the transition into three phases: (1) flip in-memory state + allocate the *next* transition's wake channel under the inner lock; (2) release the inner lock and run the persist; (3) re-acquire the inner lock and close the *current* direction's wake channel. The two inner-lock acquisitions are sequential, not nested. Drop any "already in target state" early-return in the wait-side primitive — always wait on the channel; a closed channel returns immediately, an in-flight transition correctly blocks. The new invariant ("channel is closed iff state-flipped AND persist completed") makes "post-`Wait` reads see post-transition disk state" structurally true. Used for `Session.transitionTo` / `Activate` / `Evict` (#169); applies to any "transition + persist + broadcast wake" coupling. See [ADR 013](knowledge/decisions/013-evict-activate-persist-ordering.md).
- **`HOME=t.TempDir()` as the e2e isolation envelope** — when the binary under test resolves all of its persistent paths via `os.UserHomeDir()` (which honors `$HOME` on Unix), redirecting the child's `HOME` to `t.TempDir()` contains every ~-relative path with a single env var — no per-resource flag plumbing required. Belt-and-suspenders explicit flags (e.g. `-pyry-socket=<tmp>/pyry.sock`) cover the load-bearing path without inventing new flags for ancillary state. The corollary: keep ALL persistent paths under `~/...` (don't sprinkle `/var/`, `/etc/`, `/tmp` defaults) so this trick keeps working.
- **Subprocess re-exec for "test the test framework's failure path"** — when verifying that a `t.Fatal`/`t.FailNow` path doesn't leak resources, you can't observe it from a same-process subtest (Go's testing framework propagates inner failures to the parent and ends the outer test before assertions run). Re-exec `os.Args[0]` with `-test.run=^TestInnerChild$` and an env-var flag (`PYRY_E2E_INNER_FATAL_OUT=<state-file>`) so the failing path runs in a fresh process; the child writes observed state (pid, socket path) to the file before failing; the parent reads it and asserts externally. The inner test is gated on the env var (`os.Getenv(...) == "" → t.Skip`) so normal runs are no-ops. Pairs naturally with the POSIX zero-signal probe (`os.FindProcess` + `Signal(syscall.Signal(0))`) for liveness checks.
- **Sentinel + `fmt.Errorf("%w: …")` over a struct error type when the only data the caller needs is a printable list** — when an error needs to carry "and here's what matched" data alongside a typed-discriminator (e.g. ambiguous prefix → list of candidate ids), prefer `var ErrFoo = errors.New(...)` plus `fmt.Errorf("%w:\n%s", ErrFoo, formattedLines)` over a struct error type with an exposed `Matches []Ref` field. Pros: zero new exported types; `errors.Is` is one pointer compare via the wrapped chain; CLI consumers do one `fmt.Fprintln(os.Stderr, err)` and get the human-readable list verbatim. Cons: callers cannot programmatically iterate matches — accept this whenever the data is fundamentally for human consumption (CLI disambiguation prompts, debug logs) and downstream code only needs the typed branch. Used for `Pool.ResolveID`'s `ErrAmbiguousSessionID` (1.1e-A); the same shape suits any "typed error + descriptive payload for printing" surface.
- **Loose-input resolver pairs with strict-input lookup** — when a domain object is keyed by a canonical id (e.g. `SessionID`) and external callers (CLIs, wire APIs) hand in loose strings (UUIDs, prefixes, empty), expose two methods: `Lookup(canonical)` for code-internal callers that already have the canonical form, and `ResolveID(loose) (canonical, error)` for input-handling callers. Resolution returns the canonical id, not `*Session` — callers then call `Lookup`/`Activate`/`Remove` with the resolved id, which guards against the entity being removed between resolve and use without saving any meaningful work. Resolver runs under the host's read lock; consumers each pay one extra hashmap probe but never observe a half-removed state. Same shape would suit any "user-input → canonical-id" transformation that today's consumers inline against the host's lock.
- **Exit-1 for runtime errors, exit-2 for "user typed it wrong"** — in CLI subcommands, return errors up the call stack for runtime failures (RPC failed, daemon-not-running, resolver error) so `main` prints them and exits 1. Use `os.Exit(2)` directly for argument-shape errors (extra positionals, missing required arg) so the two failure classes stay visually distinct in shell exit codes. POSIX convention; matches the existing `os.Exit(2)` shape at the top of `cmd/pyry/main.go`. The split is checkable: error return ⇒ runtime, `os.Exit(2)` inline ⇒ user typed wrong. Pair the inline exit with a unit-testable helper that returns a sentinel (`attachSelectorFromArgs` returning `errTooManyAttachArgs`) so the argument-shape rule is covered in a table test without intercepting `os.Exit`.
- **Extend an exported function's signature in place when there is exactly one caller.** Adding a sibling (e.g. `AttachWithID`) for a single new parameter splits the call surface for no benefit. The grep-for-callers test is the discriminator — if extending churns >1 production caller, consider a sibling; if it's one, extend. Used for `control.Attach` in 1.1e-D (one call site, fifth arg added). Same shape suits any "one new parameter, one caller" growth.
- **Sibling functions (not shared core) when divergent tails dominate the prologue.** The complement of the rule above: when a new variant *changes the I/O loop*, not just a parameter, prefer a sibling exported function over an `if mode { … }`-laden core. `control.Attach` (PTY mode: `term.MakeRaw` + SIGWINCH watcher + `copyWithEscape`) and `control.AttachStdio` (no-PTY: plain `io.Copy(out, conn)` joined goroutine + `io.Copy(conn, in)`) share ~10 lines of dial-and-handshake prologue but diverge entirely in the post-ack body. Two sibling functions are clearer than one core branching on a `stdio bool` for every blocking primitive in the loop. The cost is the prologue duplication; the win is each function reads top-to-bottom without mode-gates. Factor into a shared core only when a third transport variant lands. Used for `AttachStdio` (1.3a, #154).
- **Explicit flag, not implicit auto-detect, when modes have wildly different semantics.** When a CLI surface has two modes whose behavioural contracts diverge significantly (PTY-mode `pyry attach` does raw mode + escape-key detection; `--stdio` does verbatim byte forwarding), require an explicit flag rather than auto-detecting from environment (e.g. `term.IsTerminal(stdinFd)`). Auto-detect produces silent surprise in both directions: a test running under captured stdin gets stream-json behaviour; a heredoc redirected into the human-mode tool loses the escape surface. The explicit flag is the discriminator: SDKs pass it, humans don't, nothing changes accidentally. Used for `pyry attach --stdio` (1.3a, #154); same shape applies to any "behaviourally divergent transport variant" growth on a stable verb.
- **Build-tag-gated test packages for opt-in expensive tests** — when a test category is heavy (spawns binaries, requires `go build`, takes seconds) and not part of every-PR CI, gate the whole package with `//go:build e2e` (or similar). Default `go test ./...` doesn't compile or run it; opt-in via `go test -tags=e2e ./<path>/...`. Document the invocation in the package doc comment so godoc surfaces it. Lighter than a separate `make` target for the gating itself; the make target is the operator-facing convenience, not the mechanism.
- **Caller-supplied path + caller-owned cleanup, with a sugar wrapper for the common case** — when a test-harness primitive that originally allocated its own resource (e.g. `Start(t)` calling `t.TempDir()`) needs a caller-controlled variant for one specific scenario (here: pre-populating HOME for a restart-shaped test), refactor the body into a "primitive that takes the resource" (`StartIn(t, home)`) and redefine the original as a one-line wrapper (`return StartIn(t, t.TempDir())`). Caller-owned cleanup means the primitive does not register the resource with `t.Cleanup` — the caller decides whether to reuse it across calls. Existing callers see no change; new use cases compose. `Options` struct migration is non-breaking later when a second knob shows up. Used for `e2e.StartIn` (#106).
- **Public wrapper around a private cleanup primitive, idempotent via `sync.Once`** — when a `t.Cleanup`-registered teardown needs to also be callable mid-test (here: `Stop()` to enable a restart pattern), expose the public verb as a one-line wrapper around the internal `teardown` rather than renaming. The `sync.Once` already guarding teardown makes both call paths safely idempotent without new state. The naming asymmetry (`Stop` public, `teardown` private) signals the public/private split to readers; renaming the private helper to "Stop_internal" or similar is anti-simplicity. Used for `Harness.Stop` (#106).
- **Sibling harness for an interactive surface, not retrofitted onto the non-interactive one** — when a binary has both a non-interactive surface (verbs over a socket) and an interactive one (PTY-bound `attach`), give each its own harness (`Harness` + `Start(t)` for daemon-only verbs; `AttachHarness` + `StartAttach(t, sessionID)` for PTY round-trips) rather than parameterising one harness with an "interactive?" mode. The two have different lifecycle invariants (3 OS resources vs. 1), different skip conditions (`pty.Open` failure vs. only `cmd.Start`), different teardown ordering (master→slave→attach→daemon vs. just daemon), different env-injection needs (helper vars on daemon's env so `runOnce` propagates them vs. plain `childEnv`). Sharing the binary cache (`ensurePyryBuilt`), `childEnv`, `killSpawned`, and the readiness timing constants is the right reuse boundary; sharing `Start`'s entry point would force an "options polymorphism" hairball. Used for #125's `AttachHarness`. Same shape suits any future harness that wraps a third interface (e.g. an HTTP API for Phase 2.0).
- **`time.Time` on the wire when consumers compute on it; pre-formatted string when display-only** — `encoding/json` marshals `time.Time` to RFC3339Nano (jq-debuggable, byte-stable) and decodes back into a typed value. Use the typed value when at least one consumer needs to do math (relative-time formatting, comparisons, durations) — going string forces every consumer to re-parse on every read. Use a pre-formatted string (`"310ms"`, `"1.5s"`) when the value is purely display-bound and no consumer ever subtracts. `LastActive` on `control.SessionInfo` (1.1b-B1) takes the typed shape; `StatusPayload`'s duration fields take the string shape — different jobs, different encodings. Pair the typed-time choice with the `time.Equal` test discipline (monotonic-clock strip on roundtrip; never `==` or `reflect.DeepEqual`).
- **Take-or-create over insert-or-error for caller-supplied-id primitives.** When a primitive accepts a caller-supplied id and "already exists" is a normal outcome (not an error), prefer take-or-create (`GetOrCreate(id) → (canonical, nil)`) over insert-or-error (`CreateWithID(id) → ErrIDInUse`). The handler's natural shape becomes "ensure entity X exists, then operate" — both branches share the rest of the path. Insert-or-error forces every caller to do `if errors.Is(err, ErrIDInUse) { Lookup(id) }`, which re-introduces a TOCTOU window between the failed insert and the lookup that a concurrent `Remove` can race through. The take-or-create form collapses both branches into one atomic call. Used for `Pool.GetOrCreate` (1.3b, #155). See [ADR 014](knowledge/decisions/014-get-or-create-take-or-create.md).
- **Hold the registry lock across the lifecycle-goroutine schedule for caller-supplied-id primitives.** When a primitive registers an entry in a shared map and schedules a per-entry goroutine that observers will block on (e.g. `g.Go(sess.Run)` parking on a `Activate` signal), keep the lock across BOTH the map insert AND the schedule. A primitive that releases the lock between the two has a window where a concurrent same-id observer can read the entry, return its id, call the wait primitive, and block until ctx times out — because the lifecycle goroutine has not been scheduled yet and will never close the wake channel. The race detector cannot catch it; the failure mode is a long hang at the wait site. `errgroup.Group.Go` is non-blocking (the spawned goroutine parks immediately), so holding the lock across `g.Go` introduces no new lock-order edges. Don't try to plug the hole with a "wait for a separate ready signal from the goroutine" — that's two synchronization points where one would do. Used for `Pool.GetOrCreate` (1.3b, #155); applies to any "register + schedule per-entry goroutine + caller waits via the goroutine's signal" coupling.
- **Validate caller-supplied ids at the primitive boundary, not the verb handler.** When a primitive newly accepts caller-supplied ids (vs. always minting them), put the canonical-shape validator (e.g. `ValidID` next to `NewID`) as the first thing the primitive checks. Not in the handler. The primitive is the universal entry point for direct Go consumers, test harnesses, and future verbs — if the validator lives in the handler, every future caller has to remember to add it. The validator is cheap (character-class check, ~30 LOC), stdlib-only, and rejects "a session with id `b`" before any state mutates. Belt-and-suspenders version + variant checks (rejecting v3 / non-RFC-4122 ids) are free given the SDK only sends v4. Used for `Pool.GetOrCreate` (1.3b, #155).
- **Reuse an existing seam over adding a parallel sub-interface when the read primitive already fits.** The post-#98 pattern is "one named per-verb sub-interface (`Remover`/`Renamer`/`Lister`/`GetOrCreator`) embedded into `Sessioner`, satisfied structurally by `*sessions.Pool`." That pattern fits when the seam needs a method that doesn't already exist on the resolver. When the registry-read the new verb needs is **already** reachable through an existing seam — e.g. `SessionResolver.Lookup`'s `(*Session, ErrSessionNotFound)` contract is functionally a "is this id registered?" boolean if you ignore the `*Session` — adding a parallel interface (`HasIDer`) + a parallel `Pool` method (`Pool.HasID`) doubles the surface for the same map read. The discriminator is "does the primitive I need exist on `SessionResolver` already, possibly under a different name?" — if yes, reach for it (and accept that the verb answers correctly even when `sessioner == nil`); if no, add the sub-interface. Used for `VerbSessionsHasID` (1.3c-1, #157). Re-evaluate per future verb; the rule is "use what's there", not "never add another sub-interface".
- **Inner-struct boolean field deliberately NOT omitempty when zero/absent must be on-the-wire-distinguishable.** When a wire response carries an inner struct whose only meaningful field is a boolean (`SessionsHasIDResult{Has bool}`), the wrapper-pointer's omitempty on the outer field handles back-compat byte-shape (other verbs unchanged); the *inner* boolean's omitempty would elide `false` and produce `{"sessionsHasID":{}}` — indistinguishable from a malformed response that forgot to populate the field. Drop omitempty on the inner boolean even though it costs ~10 bytes per response — the wire becomes unambiguous (`{"has":false}` vs `{"has":true}` vs missing-field-bug `{}`). Pin with a `Test*ResultHasNotOmitempty` regression at the marshal layer. Used for `SessionsHasIDResult.Has` (1.3c-1, #157); the same shape suits any "single-bool inner result" wire surface.
- **`SysProcAttr{Setsid: true, Setctty: true}` to attach a child to a specific PTY slave** — when `exec.Cmd`'s stdio is a PTY slave fd and the child needs to treat it as its controlling terminal (so `IsTerminal(0)` reflects the slave and `term.MakeRaw` puts the right tty into raw mode), set both fields on `SysProcAttr`. `Setsid` puts the child in a fresh session (a controlling terminal can only be acquired by a session leader); `Setctty` then attaches the slave fd as the new session's controlling tty. Without this, the child inherits the parent's controlling terminal and writes to the slave still happen, but `IsTerminal` and `MakeRaw` operate on the wrong device. Used in `StartAttach` (#125) so the attach client's `term.MakeRaw(slave fd)` reaches the slave PTY rather than the test process's terminal.
- **Probe-stat lives next to the consuming verb; pure-decision stays in `internal/`.** When a verb in `cmd/pyry` needs to decide what platform-specific action to run (e.g. which restart command for the locally-installed daemon), split the work in two: a pure decision function in `internal/<area>` that takes a typed shape (`RestartProbe{LaunchdPlistExists, SystemdUnitExists, UID}`) and returns the argv, and an `os.Stat`-driven probe helper inline in `cmd/pyry` that populates the typed shape from canonical filesystem paths. The pure function is trivially testable from struct literals; the probe helper is short enough to leave to manual smoke tests. Don't fold the stats into the `internal/` package — it conflates "decide what" with "probe where" and forces every test of the decision to manage `$HOME` + fake plist/unit files. Used for `pyry update`'s daemon-restart wiring (#190); same shape suits any future "stat for platform-specific install state, then decide" growth. See [ADR 015](knowledge/decisions/015-update-restart-probe-inline.md).
- **Function-typed seam fields on the verb's options struct, not package-level vars or build tags.** When an integration test needs to assert what a CLI verb *would* exec (or stat, or HTTP-call) without spawning real binaries, add a function-typed field to the verb's options struct alongside other seams (`replace`, `executablePath`, `fetcher`). `runUpdate` populates with production defaults (`exec.CommandContext` wrapper, `os.Stat`-based probe); tests substitute closures that record calls into captured slices or return sentinel errors. No globals, no build tags, no `t.Cleanup` to restore mutable state. Pattern is consistent across every seam the verb's test surface needs. Used for `updateOptions.runRestart` + `updateOptions.probeRestart` (#190); the precedent is `updateOptions.replace` (#189) and `Pool.RegistryPath` empty-disables-I/O (#?).
- **Defensive smoke checks live at the install chokepoint, in shell, and gate on running-state — not "unit loaded".** When a class of regression has been observed (the #202 non-TTY-stdin hang) and produces a one-line stdout sentinel (`Uptime: 2562047h47m16.854775807s`), the install-time probe lives in `install.sh` rather than a new Go subcommand: `install.sh` is the chokepoint every binary update flows through, has no chicken-and-egg with the freshly-extracted binary, and adds zero new dependencies. Three discipline points: (a) detect "is there a default-named service this script should care about?" by gating on **running state** (`launchctl print | grep 'state = running'`, `systemctl --user is-active --quiet pyry`), not by "unit file exists" — gating-on-loaded would auto-start operator-disabled units, and the smoke check's job is regression detection on the update path (`is-active` matches the population at risk); (b) lean on what's already there — `pyry status`'s built-in `dialWithRetry` (#199) + 5s deadline IS the grace period, no manual `sleep` on top; (c) split failure modes into distinct exit codes (0 healthy / 2 sentinel / 3 dial-fail / 4 restart-fail) so downstream automation can branch — collapsing them under "exit 1, look at stderr" loses the diagnostic distinction the probe exists to draw. Sentinel detection is one anchored grep (`^Uptime: +<sentinel>$`) against the documented zero-time tell; do NOT also parse the correlated `Started at: 0001-01-01T00:00:00Z` line — two checks against the same observable add zero coverage and one risks false negatives if `runStatus`'s format drifts. Used for `install.sh`'s `smoke_check` (#203). See [ADR 017](knowledge/decisions/017-install-script-smoke-check.md).
- **Bounded retry loop wrapping a primitive: function-typed dial seam + identical wrap at every exit door.** When wrapping a one-shot primitive (`dial`) in a bounded retry, three discipline points keep the wrapper invisible to callers: (a) extract the primitive as an unexported function-typed alias (`dialFunc`) and let production wire the real implementation while tests pass a fake — same shape as `updateOptions`'s function-typed seams but at package scope; (b) make every exit door preserve the original error via the *exact same* `fmt.Errorf("dial %s: %w", socketPath, err)` wrap so wire-output (`pyry: status: dial /…/pyry.sock: connect: no such file or directory`) is byte-identical to the pre-wrap single-shot dial — three replicated wraps so a future grep on the format string finds all three; (c) shape the loop as **first-attempt-immediate → predicate-then-deadline-then-sleep** with `!time.Now().Before(deadline)` (not `After`) for the boundary tick, `time.NewTimer + Stop()` (not `time.After`, which leaks per cancel), and `ctx.Done()` short-circuiting only the inter-attempt sleep (the dial itself takes the cancel via the stdlib's context-aware `DialContext`, surfaces as wrapped `context.Canceled`, and exits at the next iteration's non-transient branch). The wrapper introduces zero new goroutines, zero shared state, no behavioural change on the fast path. Used for `dialWithRetry` (#199); same shape suits any future "wrap a one-shot primitive in a bounded retry" growth.

## Open Questions

- **Backoff cooldown/bail-out** — if crashes happen N times in T seconds, should the supervisor give up? Currently retries forever, which is the right default for a service supervisor (a supervised child that never starts is the operator's problem to investigate, not for pyry to give up on).
- **Phase 0.5 — Real production test** — supervisor hasn't been tested with a real `claude` child on pyrybox running as a launchd/systemd service. The tmux setup is still running. This is the only Phase 0 item left after PRs #1-#10.

(Earlier "Session ID tracking" and "Control socket design" questions were resolved by the PR series that landed Phase 0.2–0.4: `--continue` for session continuity, line-delimited JSON over a Unix socket for control.)
